The 'Sisters' Issues: Ownership During Khiyar
List of subsidiary issues derived from the core dispute on ownership during the option period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on ownership during khiyar al-shart and apply them to predict the ruling for any subsidiary issue drawn from the same principle.

Core Idea
Ownership during khiyar determines every subsequent legal effect: istibra, emancipation, deposit, and more.

This passage from al-Hidayah unpacks the practical fallout of the intra-Hanafi dispute over whether the buyer owns the purchased item during the option period. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that ownership does not transfer; the two companions (Sahibayn) hold that it does. From this single difference, eight 'sisters' are derived — concrete cases where the ruling flips based on the underlying ownership principle. Later commentaries add further scenarios. Understanding this dispute equips you to solve a class of fiqh problems with one decisive key.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the core dispute
Recognize that the entire passage is built on one question: does the buyer own the item during khiyar al-shart? Abu Hanifa says no; Sahibayn say yes. This is the axis around which all the 'sisters' revolve.
All eight issues are explicitly said to 'build upon' (tabtani) this difference.
2
Work through each 'sister' systematically
For each of the eight cases listed—emancipation, istibra, umm walad, deposit, release of price, wine purchase, etc.—identify the scenario and note how the ruling differs between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Record the practical consequence.
Use the headings in the passage: 'منها' marks each new sister.
3
Identify the illa (effective cause)
In each case, the difference in ruling stems from whether ownership is established. Ask: if ownership is present, what effect follows? If absent, what effect? This reveals why the rulings split.
For example, if the buyer owns the item, his emancipation of a slave relative is valid and the option drops; if not, the emancipation is ineffective and the option remains.
4
Extend to the additional issues from commentaries
The passage adds scenarios like turning grape juice into wine, continued residence, deer in ihram, and benefits. Treat these the same way: apply the ownership principle to determine the Hanafi and Sahibayn positions.
Some commentaries also mention an internal split between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the release of debt (ibra). Note this secondary ikhtilaf.
5
Synthesize the pattern
Conclude that the whole set of 'sisters' is a single logical tree. If you know the root principle (ownership or no ownership), you can derive the ruling for any new scenario without memorization.
This illustrates the power of usul al-fiqh: one root principle generates many furu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر في الهداية أن لهذه المسألة أخوات كلها تبتني على وقوع الملك للمشتري بشرط الخيار وعدمه منها : عتق المشتري على المشتري إذا كان قريباً له في مدة الخيار، ولو كان للبائع فمات المشتري فأجاز البائع عتق الابن ولا يرث أباه كما قدمناه عن الخانية. ومنها عتقه إذا كان المشتري حلف إن ملك عبداً فهو حر بخلاف ما إذا قال إن اشتريت لأنه يصير كالمنشئ للعتق بعد الشراء فسقط الخيار ومنها أن حيض المشتراة في المدة لا يجتزأ به من الاستبراء عنده، وعندهما يجتزأ، ولو ردت بحكم الخيار إلى البائع لا يجب الاستبراء عنده، وعندهما يجب إذا ردت بعد القبض ومنها إذا ولدت المشتراة في المدة بالنكاح لا تصير أم ولد له عنده خلافاً لهما، ومحله ما إذا كان قبل القبض، أما بعده فسقط الخيار اتفاقاً وتصير أم ولد للمشتري لأنها تعيبت عنده بالولادة ؛ كذا في النهاية وفي الخانية : إذا ولدت بطل خياره وإن كان الولد ميتاً ولم تنقصها الولادة لا يبطل خياره .اهـ. ثم اعلم أنهم لم يقيدوا بدعوى الولد وقيده بها في إيضاح الإصلاح قال : لأنه ولد والفراش ضعيف اهـ. وهو تقييد لقولهما. ومنها إذا قبض المشتري المبيع بإذن البائع ثم أودعه عند البائع فهلك في يده في تلك المدة هلك من مال البائع لارتفاع القبض بالرد لعدم الملك، وعندهما من لصحة الإيداع باعتبار قيام الملك ، ولو كان الخيار للبائع فسلم المبيع إلى المشتري فأودعه البائع فهلك عنده بطل البيع عند الكل، ولو كان البيع باتاً فقبض المشتري المبيع بإذن البائع أو بغير إذنه ثم أودعه البائع فهلك كان على المشتري اتفاقاً لصحة الإيداع؛ كذا في التتارخانية. ومنها لو كان المشتري عبداً مأذوناً فأبرأه البائع عن الثمن في المدة بقي خياره عنده لأن الرد امتناع التملك والمأذون له يليه وعندهما بطل خياره لأنه لما ملكه كان الرد منه تمليكاً بغير عوض وهو ليس من أهله وهذا يقتضي صحة الإبراء، وقدمنا أنه لا يصح عند أبي يوسف قياساً، ويصح عند محمد استحساناً ونبه عليه هنا في النهاية ومنها إذا اشترى ذمي من ذمي خمراً على أنه بالخيار ثم أسلم بطل الخيار عندهما لأنه ملكها فلا يملك ردها وهو مسلم، وعنده يبطل البيع لأنه لم يملكها فلا يتملكها بإسقاط الخيار بعده وهو مسلم اهـ. فقد ذكر فيها ثمان مسائل وقد زاد الشارحون مسائل أيضاً ففي فتح القدير : الأولى ما إذا تخمر العصير في بيع مسلمين في مدته فسد البيع عنده لعجزه عن تملكه وعندهما يتم لعجزه عن رده . الثاني اشترى داراً على أنه بالخيار ثلاثة أيام وهو ساكنها بإجارة أو إعارة فاستدام سكنها قال السرخسي : لا يكون اختياراً وهو في ابتداء السكنى وقال خواهر زاده: استدامتها اختيار عندهما لملك العين، وعنده ليس باختيار الثالثة حلال اشترى ظبياً بالخيار فقبضه ثم أحرم والظبي في يده فينقض البيع عنده ويرد إلى البائع وعندهما يلزم المشتري، ولو كان الخيار للبائع ينتقض بالإجماع، ولو كان للمشتري فأحرم المشتري له أن یرده . الرابعة إذا كان الخيار للمشتري وفسخ العقد فالزوائد ترد على البائع عنده لأنها لم تحدث على ملك المشتري، وعندهما للمشتري لأنها حدثت على ملكه اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين: لو اشترى بخيار فدام على السكني لا يبطل خياره، ولو ابتدأها بطل يماثله خيار العيب وخيار الشرط في القسمة لا يبطل بدوام السكنى .اهـ. وفي التتارخانية أن محمداً ذكر في البيوع أن خيار الشرط يبطل بالسكنى وفي القسمة ذكر أنه لا يبطل فاختلف المشايخ؛ فمنهم من حمل ما في البيوع على الابتداء وما في القسمة على الدوام، ومنهم من أبقى ما في البيوع على إطلاقه فيبطل بالابتداء والدوام وأبقى ما في القسمة على إطلاقه فلا يبطل خيار الشرط فيها بالابتداء والدوام.
And it is mentioned in al-Hidayah that this issue has sisters, all of which are built upon whether ownership falls to the buyer with the condition of option or not. Among them: the emancipation of the buyer (i.e., of a slave) if he is a relative of the buyer during the option period; and if the slave belonged to the seller and the buyer died, and the seller validates the emancipation, the son does not inherit from his father as we have mentioned from al-Khaniyya. And from them: his emancipation if the buyer swore 'If I own a slave, he is free,' as opposed to if he said 'If I buy' because he becomes like one initiating emancipation after purchase, so the option falls. And among them: that the menstruation of the purchased (slave-woman) during the period is not counted for istibra' according to him (Abu Hanifa), but according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is counted. And if she is returned by virtue of the option to the seller, istibra' is not obligatory according to him, but according to them it is obligatory if she is returned after possession. And among them: if the purchased woman gives birth during the period due to marriage, she does not become umm walad for him according to him, contrary to them. Its place is before possession; after possession, the option falls by agreement and she becomes umm walad for the buyer because she became defective by childbirth; likewise in al-Nihaya. And in al-Khaniyya: if she gives birth, his option is void even if the child is dead and the birth does not decrease her value; his option is not void. Then know that they did not restrict it to claiming the child, but it is restricted in Idah al-Islah: because it is a child and the bed is weak. This is a restriction of their statement. And among them: if the buyer takes possession of the sold item with the seller's permission then deposits it with the seller and it perishes in his hand during that period, it perishes from the seller's wealth because possession is cancelled by return due to lack of ownership; according to them it is from the validity of deposit considering the existence of ownership. And if the option is for the seller and he delivers the sold item to the buyer then the seller deposits it and it perishes in his hand, the sale is void according to all. And if the sale is absolute (bat) and the buyer takes possession with or without the seller's permission then deposits it with the seller and it perishes, it is on the buyer by agreement due to the validity of deposit; likewise in al-Tatarkhaniyya. And among them: if the buyer is a permitted slave and the seller releases him from the price during the period, his option remains according to him because return is prevention of ownership and the permitted slave can undertake it; according to them his option is void because when he owned (the right to return), the return from him is a transfer without compensation, and he is not qualified for that, and this necessitates the validity of the release. And we have mentioned that it is not valid according to Abu Yusuf by qiyas, and it is valid according to Muhammad by istihsan, and he pointed to it here in al-Nihaya. And among them: if a dhimmi buys wine from a dhimmi on the condition of option, then he becomes Muslim, the option is void according to them because he owned it, so he cannot return it while being Muslim; and according to him (Abu Hanifa) the sale is void because he did not own it, so he does not own it by dropping the option afterwards while being Muslim. So there are eight issues mentioned here, and the commentators have added more issues. In Fath al-Qadir: the first: if grape juice becomes wine in a sale between two Muslims during the option period, the sale is corrupted according to him due to inability to own it; according to them it is valid due to inability to return it. The second: he bought a house on the condition of having the option for three days while he is residing in it by lease or loan, and he continues residence. Al-Sarakhsi said: it is not considered choice; and it is in the beginning of residence. Kharzada said: its continuation is choice according to them due to ownership of the property; according to him it is not choice. The third: a man bought a deer on option, took possession, then entered ihram while the deer is in his hand; the sale is annulled according to him and it is returned to the seller; according to them the sale is binding. If the option was for the seller, it is annulled by consensus. If the option was for the buyer and the buyer entered ihram, he has the right to return it. The fourth: if the option is for the buyer and he rescinds the contract, the benefits (offspring) are returned to the seller according to him because they did not arise under the buyer's ownership; according to them they belong to the buyer because they arose under his ownership. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: if he buys with an option and continues residence, his option is not void; if he begins it, it is void. Similarly, the option of defect and option of condition in division (qisma) is not void by continued residence. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: Muhammad mentioned in al-Buyu' that khiyar al-shart is void by residence, and in al-Qisma he mentioned that it is not void, so the scholars differed: some interpreted what is in al-Buyu' as referring to beginning, and what is in al-Qisma as referring to continuity; others left what is in al-Buyu' general so it is void by beginning and continuity, and left what is in al-Qisma general so khiyar al-shart is not void by beginning or continuity.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the core dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn) regarding whether the buyer acquires ownership of the purchased item during the option period (khiyar al-shart). Al-Hidayah lists eight 'sisters' – subsidiary issues that depend on this fundamental difference. Each issue illustrates the practical consequences of the disagreement. The passage then adds further issues from later commentaries like Fath al-Qadir and Jami' al-Fusulayn. The author systematically presents each scenario: emancipation by the buyer, istibra' (waiting period after purchase of a slave-woman), umm walad status, deposit and destruction, release of price, and the specific case of wine purchase and conversion to Islam. The dominant theme is that according to Abu Hanifa, the buyer does not fully own the item during the option period, so many legal effects (like emancipation, validity of deposit, etc.) are not binding; according to the Sahibayn, the buyer does own it, and thus the effects are binding. Later, additional issues about residence in a purchased house, entering ihram with a hunted animal, and the fate of benefits (offspring) are discussed, again hinging on the same core disagreement. The text also notes an internal dispute between Abu Yusuf (qiyas) and Muhammad (istihsan) regarding the validity of the release of a slave's debt. The passage is a dense exercise in legal application of a single usul principle.

Key Terms
استبراء (istibra'): A waiting period to ensure a slave-woman is not pregnant, in the context of purchase
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave-woman who bears a child to her owner, becoming free upon his death
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option to rescind a sale within a stipulated period

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the fundamental difference between Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn) regarding khiyar al-shart that leads to all the subsidiary issues discussed?
A) Whether the option period can be extended
B) Whether the buyer owns the item during the option period
C) Whether the seller owns the price during the option period
D) Whether the sale is valid at all

Key Takeaway
The entire set of subsidiary issues in khiyar al-shart reduces to one question: ownership during the option period.

Conversion to Islam and Khiyar on Wine: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar and conversion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a dhimmi buyer of wine converts to Islam during the option period, explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn, and identify the role of possession.

Core Idea
Ownership during khiyar decides: conversion voids the sale (Abu Hanifa) or voids the option (Sahibayn).

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a nuanced scenario: a dhimmi buys wine with an option condition (khiyar al-shart) and then converts to Islam. The Hanafi school splits internally on whether the sale is void or the option is void, based on a deeper disagreement about ownership during the option period. Al-Zayla'i adds further distinctions depending on whether the buyer or seller converts, and whether possession has occurred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and contract
Both parties are dhimmis; the subject matter is wine; the sale includes a khiyar al-shart for the buyer. Note that the sale itself is valid between non-Muslims.
Wine is not a commodity for Muslims, but dhimmis can trade it among themselves.
2
Understand the dispute on ownership during khiyar
Abu Hanifa holds that the buyer does not own the item during the option period, while the Sahibayn hold that ownership transfers immediately subject to rescission.
This is the root of the ikhtilaf.
3
Apply the ruling to the buyer's conversion
According to Sahibayn, since the buyer owned the wine at the time of conversion, he cannot return it (as a Muslim cannot own wine), so the option is void and the sale becomes binding. According to Abu Hanifa, since he did not own it, the sale is void because he cannot acquire ownership after conversion.
Both positions are logically consistent with their respective premise.
4
Note the consensus on seller conversion
If the seller converts while the buyer has the option, the buyer's option remains, and he may choose to keep or return the wine. If returned, the now-Muslim seller may own it by inheritance analogy.
This is by consensus; the seller's conversion does not affect the buyer's rights.
5
Distinguish before and after possession
Before possession, conversion voids the sale in all cases (whether absolute or with option). After possession in an absolute sale, the sale remains valid because it was completed before conversion. After possession with option, the above dispute applies.
Possession (qabd) is a critical factor in validating the transfer of ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها إذا اشترى ذمي من ذمي خمراً على أنه بالخيار ثم أسلم بطل الخيار عندهما لأنه ملكها فلا يملك ردها وهو مسلم، وعنده يبطل البيع لأنه لم يملكها فلا يتملكها بإسقاط الخيار بعده وهو مسلم اهـ. ثم رأيته في شرح الزيلعي قال : ولو أسلم البائع والخيار للمشتري بقي على خياره بالإجماع، ولو ردها المشتري عادت إلى ملك البائع لأن العقد من جانب البائع بات، فإن أجازه صار له، وإن فسخ صار الخمر للبائع والمسلم من أهل أن يتملك الخمر حكماً كما في الإرث. ثم ذكر ما لو كان الخيار للبائع ثم قال : وهذا كله فيما إذا أسلم أحدهما بعد القبض والخيار لأحدهما، وإن أسلم قبل القبض بطل البيع في الصور كلها سواء كان البيع باتاً أو بشرط الخيار لأحدهما أولهما لأن للقبض شبهاً بالعقد من حيث إنه يفيد ملك التصرف فلا يملكه بعد الإسلام وإن أسلم أحدهما أو كلاهما بعد القبض وكان البيع باتاً لا يبطل لأنه قد تم بالقبض بخلاف ما إذا كان بشرط الخيار على ما مر اهـ.
And among them: if a dhimmi buys wine from a dhimmi on the condition that he has the option, then he (the buyer) becomes Muslim, the option is void according to them (Sahibayn) because he owned it, so he cannot return it while being a Muslim; and according to him (Abu Hanifa) the sale is void because he did not own it, so he does not own it by dropping the option afterwards while being Muslim. Then I saw in Sharh al-Zayla'i that he said: and if the seller becomes Muslim and the option is for the buyer, the buyer remains on his option by consensus. And if the buyer returns it, it returns to the seller's ownership because the contract from the seller's side is absolute; if he (the now-Muslim buyer) validates it, it becomes his; if he rescinds, the wine becomes for the seller, and a Muslim is qualified to own wine legally as in inheritance. Then he mentioned the case when the option is for the seller, then said: all this is when one of them becomes Muslim after possession and the option is for one of them. If he becomes Muslim before possession, the sale is void in all cases, whether the sale is absolute or conditional with option for one or both, because possession has a resemblance to the contract in that it gives ownership of disposal, so he cannot own it after Islam. If one or both become Muslim after possession and the sale was absolute, it is not void because it has been completed by possession, unlike when it is with option as mentioned.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage focuses on the specific scenario where a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject) buys wine from another dhimmi with an option condition, and then the buyer converts to Islam. The core disagreement again stems from whether the buyer owned the wine during the option period. According to the Sahibayn, the buyer owned it, so upon conversion he cannot return the wine (since Muslims cannot own wine), so the option is void and the sale becomes binding. According to Abu Hanifa, the buyer did not own it, so when he converts, the sale is void because he cannot own it even by dropping the option later. Then the commentator al-Zayla'i adds: if the seller converts (instead of the buyer) while the option is for the buyer, the buyer's option remains by consensus. If the buyer returns the wine, it goes back to the seller's ownership; if he confirms, he owns it legally. If the option is for the seller, different rules apply. The passage then distinguishes between conversion before and after possession. Before possession, the sale is void in all cases because possession is necessary for full ownership of the item, and a Muslim cannot possess wine. After possession in an absolute sale (bat), the sale is valid because it was completed before conversion; but if it was with option, the ruling depends on the option period rules. This passage demonstrates the practical interface between khiyar al-shart, conversion to Islam, and the prohibition of wine.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under Muslim rule with a covenant of protection
قبض (qabd): Physical possession; a key factor in determining ownership and completion of sale
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option condition in a contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a dhimmi buys wine with an option condition and converts to Islam before taking possession, what is the ruling according to the text?
A) The sale is void in all cases.
B) The buyer keeps the option until he takes possession.
C) The sale becomes binding because the contract is valid.
D) The seller must refund the price.

Key Takeaway
The effect of conversion on a wine sale with option hinges on the dispute over ownership during khiyar and the timing of possession.

Wine Turning to Vinegar During Khiyar al-Shart: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-shart with khamr turning to vinegar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on the validity of a sale when wine becomes vinegar during the option period and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa voids the sale; the Sahibayn uphold it: ownership impossibility vs. return impossibility.

The first dispute in this passage examines a sale where grape juice becomes wine (khamr) during the option period of a khiyar al-shart contract. Both parties are Muslim. The core question: does the sale remain valid? Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) diverge based on how they conceptualize the inability—either to own the subject matter or to return it. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The case is a sale where grape juice becomes wine during the khiyar al-shart period. Both parties are Muslim. Determine whether the sale is valid or void.
This is a pure intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its rationale
Abu Hanifa says the sale is void because the Muslim buyer cannot own wine—a prohibited substance—at any point. The inability to own the subject matter at the time of contract or during the option period invalidates the sale.
The key term: 'عجز عن تملكه' (inability to own it).
3
State the Sahibayn's position and its rationale
The two Sahibayn say the sale is complete (yatimmu) because the buyer cannot return the wine to the seller—the wine has transformed into vinegar and can no longer be returned in its original state. This practical impossibility makes the sale binding.
The key term: 'عجز عن رده' (inability to return it).
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the wine becomes vinegar (permissible), who owns it? According to Abu Hanifa, the seller keeps it because the sale was void. According to the Sahibayn, the buyer owns it because the sale was valid.
This difference affects the rights of the parties to the vinegar.
5
Weigh the opinions and determine mufta bihi
Although both views are within the Hanafi school, the passage presents Abu Hanifa's view first and it is generally given preference as the more cautious position regarding prohibited substances.
Most later Hanafi fatwa collections adopt Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب خيار الشرط وعنده يبطل البيع لأنه لم يملكها فلا يتملكها بإسقاط الخيار بعده وهو مسلم اهـ. ولو كان الخيار للبائع فأسلم بطل البيع ولو أسلم المشتري لا وخيار البائع على حاله، فإن أجاز صارت الخمر للمشتري حكماً والمسلم أهل لأن يتملكها حكماً؛ كذا في النهاية. فقد ذكر فيها ثمان مسائل وقد زاد الشارحون مسائل أيضاً ففي فتح القدير : الأولى ما إذا تخمر العصير في بيع مسلمين في مدته فسد البيع عنده لعجزه عن تملكه وعندهما يتم لعجزه عن رده . الثاني اشترى داراً على أنه بالخيار ثلاثة أيام وهو ساكنها بإجارة أو إعارة فاستدام سكنها قال السرخسي : لا يكون اختياراً وهو في ابتداء السكنى وقال خواهر زاده: استدامتها اختيار عندهما لملك العين، وعنده ليس باختيار الثالثة حلال اشترى ظبياً بالخيار فقبضه ثم أحرم والظبي في يده فينقض البيع عنده ويرد إلى البائع وعندهما يلزم المشتري، ولو كان الخيار للبائع ينتقض بالإجماع، ولو كان للمشتري فأحرم المشتري له أن یرده . الرابعة إذا كان الخيار للمشتري وفسخ العقد فالزوائد ترد على البائع عنده لأنها لم تحدث على ملك المشتري، وعندهما للمشتري لأنها حدثت على ملكه اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين: لو اشترى بخيار فدام على السكني لا يبطل خياره، ولو ابتدأها بطل يماثله خيار العيب وخيار الشرط في القسمة لا يبطل بدوام السكنى .اهـ. وفي التتارخانية أن محمداً ذكر في البيوع أن خيار الشرط يبطل بالسكنى وفي القسمة ذكر أنه لا يبطل فاختلف المشايخ؛ فمنهم من حمل ما في البيوع على الابتداء وما في القسمة على الدوام، ومنهم من أبقى ما في البيوع على إطلاقه فيبطل بالابتداء والدوام وأبقى ما في القسمة على إطلاقه فلا يبطل خيار الشرط فيها بالابتداء والدوام. وفيها أيضاً : لو كان الخيار للمشتري فصالحه البائع على مائة يدفعها له على أن يبطل البيع ففسخه انفسخ ولا شيء له اهـ . ثم رأيته في شرح الزيلعي قال : ولو أسلم البائع والخيار للمشتري بقي على خياره بالإجماع، ولو ردها المشتري عادت إلى ملك البائع لأن العقد من جانب البائع بات، فإن أجازه صار له، وإن فسخ صار الخمر للبائع والمسلم من أهل أن يتملك الخمر حكماً كما في الإرث. ثم ذكر ما لو كان الخيار للبائع ثم قال : وهذا كله فيما إذا أسلم أحدهما بعد القبض والخيار لأحدهما، وإن أسلم قبل القبض بطل البيع في الصور كلها سواء كان البيع باتاً أو بشرط الخيار لأحدهما أولهما لأن للقبض شبهاً بالعقد من حيث إنه يفيد ملك التصرف فلا يملكه بعد الإسلام وإن أسلم أحدهما أو كلاهما بعد القبض وكان البيع باتاً لا يبطل لأنه قد تم بالقبض بخلاف ما إذا كان بشرط الخيار على ما مر اهـ. قوله : (وهو في ابتداء (السكنى الضمير للاختيار أي والاختيار إنما يكون في ابتداء السكنى.
Book of Sale, Chapter of Option of Condition. According to him (Abu Hanifa), the sale is void because he did not own it, so he does not own it by dropping the option after him, while he is Muslim etc. And if the option is for the seller, and he becomes Muslim, the sale is void; if the buyer becomes Muslim, it is not void and the seller's option remains, if he approves, the wine becomes owned by the buyer virtually, and the Muslim is fit to own it virtually; as in al-Nihayah. It mentioned eight issues there, and the commentators added more issues. In Fath al-Qadir: First, if grape juice becomes wine in a sale between two Muslims during its period, the sale is void according to him (Abu Hanifa) due to his inability to own it, while according to them (the two) it is complete due to his inability to return it. Second, he bought a house on condition of option for three days while he resided in it by lease or loan, and he continued its residence. al-Sarakhsi said: it is not choice, and it is in starting residence. Khwahrizadeh said: its continuation is choice according to them because he owns the property, according to him it is not choice. Third, a Halal? bought a gazelle with option, took possession, then entered ihram while the gazelle was in his hand; according to him, the sale is invalidated and returned to the seller; according to them, it is binding on the buyer. If the option were for the seller, it is invalidated by consensus; if it were for the buyer and the buyer entered ihram, he may return it. Fourth, if the option is for the buyer and he annuls the contract, the accessories are returned to the seller according to him because they did not occur under the buyer's ownership; according to them, for the buyer because they occurred under his ownership. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: If he bought with option and continued in residence, his option is not invalidated; if he started it, it is invalidated. Similarly, option of defect and option of condition in division are not invalidated by continuation of residence. In al-Tatar Khaniyyah, Muhammad mentioned in al-Buyu' that option of condition is invalidated by residence, and in division he said it is not invalidated; the mashayikh differed: some carried what is in al-Buyu' on initiation and what is in division on continuation, others left what is in al-Buyu' unrestricted so it is invalidated by both, and left what is in division unrestricted so option of condition is not invalidated by initiation or continuation. Also, if the option is for the buyer and the seller settles with him for one hundred that he pays him to void the sale, and he annuls it, it is annulled and nothing is owed to him. Then I saw in Sharh al-Zayla'i he said: If the seller becomes Muslim while the option is for the buyer, he remains on his option by consensus. If the buyer returns it, it reverts to the seller's ownership because the contract from the seller's side is binding; if he approves, it becomes his; if he annuls, the wine becomes for the seller, and the Muslim is fit to own the wine virtually as in inheritance. Then he mentioned the case when the option is for the seller, then said: This is all when one of them becomes Muslim after possession and the option is for one of them. But if he becomes Muslim before possession, the sale is void in all cases, whether the sale is binding or with option for one or both, because possession resembles the contract in that it confers ownership of disposal, so he does not own it after Islam. If one or both become Muslim after possession and the sale is binding, it is not void because it has been completed by possession, unlike when it is with option as mentioned. His saying: (He is in the beginning of) residence: the pronoun is for choice, i.e., choice is only at the beginning of residence.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion probe that discusses several mas'ail related to khiyar al-shart (option of condition) in sales, particularly its interaction with conversion to Islam, continued residence, and entering ihram. It presents the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa (referred to as 'indahu') and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, referred to as 'indahuma') on each case. The first case concerns wine that reverts to vinegar during the option period: Abu Hanifa holds the sale void because the Muslim cannot own it, while the Sahibayn consider it complete due to inability to return. The second case involves continued residence in a house bought with option: al-Sarakhsi and Khwahrizadeh differ, with Abu Hanifa distinguishing initiation from continuation. The third case involves ihram by a buyer of a gazelle: Abu Hanifa says the sale is annulled, but the Sahibayn say it is binding. The fourth case concerns accessories after annulment: Abu Hanifa says they go to seller, Sahibayn to buyer. The passage then discusses additional sources like Jami' al-Fusulayn and al-Tatar Khaniyyah, and analyzes the effect of Islam before or after possession. The commentary concludes with a clarification of the pronoun in the matn regarding 'initiation of residence.' Throughout, the passage maintains the Hanafi internal hierarchy, presenting each view with its reasoning.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in a contract allowing one or both parties to confirm or annul the sale within a specified period
عنده (indahu): Refers to Imam Abu Hanifa's position
عجز عن التملك (ajz 'an al-tamalluk): Inability to own the subject matter (due to its prohibition)
عجز عن الرد (ajz 'an al-radd): Inability to return the subject matter (due to transformation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of grape juice becoming wine during khiyar al-shart, what is the reason for the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn?
A) Abu Hanifa considers the buyer's ability to own; the Sahibayn consider the buyer's ability to return.
B) Abu Hanifa considers the seller's ability to deliver; the Sahibayn consider the seller's consent.
C) Both consider the same factor but differ on its application.
D) The difference is over whether khiyar al-shart is valid at all.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa voids a sale when a Muslim cannot own the subject matter; the Sahibayn uphold it when return is impossible.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Residence (Sukna) and Khiyar al-Shart: Initiation vs. Continuation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-shart and continued residence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between initiation and continuation of residence in khiyar al-shart and state the different views of al-Sarakhsi, Khwahrizadeh, and the commentators.

Core Idea
Initiating residence invalidates the option; continuing does not—according to al-Sarakhsi, but others disagree.

The second dispute in the passage concerns a buyer who takes possession of a house with a khiyar al-shart and continues to reside in it after the contract. Does this continued residence invalidate the option? The passage presents the views of al-Sarakhsi and Khwahrizadeh, and later sources like Jami' al-Fusulayn and al-Tatar Khaniyyah add further layers. This lesson dissects the distinction between starting residence for the first time and continuing a pre-existing residence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
A buyer with khiyar al-shart resides in the house after the contract. Does this act constitute acceptance, thereby ending the option?
The key distinction is between initiation (ibtida') and continuation (istidama).
2
State al-Sarakhsi's view
Al-Sarakhsi holds that continuation of residence is NOT choice; only the initial act of moving in (starting residence) would be.
Al-Sarakhsi's principle: option is only lost by a positive act of acceptance, not by passive continuation.
3
State Khwahrizadeh's view
Khwahrizadeh reports that according to the Sahibayn, continuation of residence IS choice, because the buyer owns the property and his continued occupation implies ownership. According to Abu Hanifa, it is not choice.
This introduces an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the meaning of continued residence.
4
Analyze the later sources (Jami' al-Fusulayn and al-Tatar Khaniyyah)
Jami' al-Fusulayn supports al-Sarakhsi: continuation does not invalidate the option, initiation does. Al-Tatar Khaniyyah reports a difference from Imam Muhammad's own statements: in sales, residence nullifies the option; in division, it does not. The mashayikh reconcile: some restrict the sales ruling to initiation, others apply it absolutely.
The reconciliation effort shows the complexity: the ruling might differ based on context (sales vs. division) and action (initiation vs. continuation).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage does not give a clear tarjih, but the grammatical note at the end ('choice is only at the beginning of residence') suggests that the relied-upon view is that only initiation invalidates the option.
This aligns with the majority of later Hanafi fatwa practice.

Source Text

Key Terms
السكنى (al-sukna): Residence in a property, either as owner or tenant.
الابتداء (al-ibtida'): Initiation or beginning an act.
الاستدامة (al-istidama): Continuation of an act already started.

According to al-Sarakhsi, does continued residence (istidamat al-sukna) by a buyer who already lived in the house as a tenant invalidate the khiyar al-shart?
A) Yes, because residence implies acceptance.
B) No, because only initiating a new residence does.
C) Yes, because the buyer owns the property.
D) No, because khiyar al-shart is never affected by residence.

Key Takeaway
Only initiating a new residence during the option period invalidates khiyar al-shart, not continuing a pre-existing one.

Annulment in Absence: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Khiyar al-Shart
An expansion probe on the intra-Hanafi dispute over faskh in khiyar al-shart in absentia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on the validity of faskh in khiyar al-shart during the other party's absence, and explain the qiyas-based reasoning behind each view.

Core Idea
Annulment (faskh) in khiyar al-shart requires the other party’s knowledge; approval does not, because annulment is harmful.

When a buyer or seller holds an option (khiyar al-shart) and wishes to annul the contract while the other party is absent, does the annulment take effect immediately? The Hanafi masters disagreed. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) against Abu Yusuf, who analogized annulment to approval. You will trace the qiyas used and see how the school’s principles apply to this practical scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The matn states that approval (ijazah) by the option-holder is valid in the other’s absence, but annulment (faskh) is not. Note which imams hold this view and which dissent.
The matn’s position is attributed to ‘indahuma’ (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).
2
Analyze Abu Yusuf’s dissent
Abu Yusuf argues that annulment is valid because the option-holder is authorized by the other party, just as approval is authorized. He compares it to an agent’s actions.
3
Follow the majority’s talil
The majority respond that annulment is a harmful act (ضرر) that can damage the other party’s reliance, so it requires knowledge to avoid harm. They compare it to dismissing an agent.
Harm includes the other party potentially relying on the contract (e.g., selling the item already).
4
Distinguish verbal vs. actual annulment
The passage notes that annulment by action (e.g., physically returning the goods) is effective even in absence by agreement, unlike verbal annulment. This is because actual annulment does not depend on the other’s knowledge.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, if the buyer verbally annuls in the seller’s absence, according to the majority the sale remains until the seller learns; according to Abu Yusuf it is void immediately. The mufta bihi is Abu Yusuf’s view per Fath al-Qadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فلو أجاز من له الخيار بغيبة صاحبه صح ولو فسخ لا) أي لا يصح في غيبة صاحبه وهذا عندهما. وقال أبو يوسف : يجوز الفسخ أيضاً لأنه مسلط على الفسخ من جهة صاحبه فلا يتوقف على علمه كالإجازة ولهذا لا يشترط رضاه فصار كالوكيل. ولهما أنه تصرف في حق الغير وهو العقد بالرفع ولا يعرى عن المضرة لأنه عساه يعتمد تمام البيع السابق فيتصرف فيه فيلزمه غرامة القيمة بالهلاك فيما إذا كان الخيار للبائع أو لا يطلب لسلعته مشترياً فيما إذا كان الخيار للمشتري، وهذا نوع ضرر فيتوقف على علمه وصار كعزل الوكيل بخلاف الإجازة لأنه لا إلزام فيه ولا يقال إنه مسلط وكيف يقال ذلك وصاحبه لا يملك الفسخ ولا تسليط في غير ما يملكه المسلط ؛ كذا في الهداية وفي المعراج : وكذا الخلاف في خيار الرؤية ولا خلاف في خيار العيب أنه لا يملكه والخلاف إنما هو في الفسخ بالقول، أما إذا فسخ بالفعل فإنه ينفسخ حكماً اتفاقاً في الحضرة والغيبة لأنه لا يشترط العلم في الحكمي كعزل الوكيل والمضارب والشريك وحجر المأذون له في التجارة بارتداد ولحوق وجنون. وبحث في فتح القدير بأنه ينبغي أن يكون الفعل الاختياري كالقول. والمراد بالغيبة علمه، وبالحضرة . رة علمه، فلو فسخ في غيبته فبلغه في المدة تم الفسخ لحصول العلم به، عدم العقد ولو بلغه بعد مضي المدة تم بمضي المدة قبل الفسخ ؛ ؛ كذا في الهداية. وكذا إذا أجاز البائع بعد فسخه قبل أن يعلم المشتري جاز وبطل فسخه؛ كذا ذكر الاسبيجابي. وفي الذخيرة : ولو اشترى على أن البائع لو غاب عنه ففسخه عليه جائز فالبيع فاسد في قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن هذا شرط فاسد عندهما . ورجح في فتح القدير قول أبي يوسف قال : فعلى هذا فالمسائل الموردة نقضاً مسلمة لأنها على وفق ما ترجح من قول أبي يوسف لكنا نوردها بناء على تسليم الدليل ؛ فمنها أن المخيرة يتم اختيارها لنفسها بلا علم زوجها ويلزمه حكم ذلك، وأجيب بأن اللزوم بإيجابه على نفسه. ومنها الرجعة ينفرد بها الزوج بلا علمها حتى لو تزوجت بعدها بعد ثلاث حيض فسخ العقد إذا أثبتها وأجيب بأن الطلاق الرجعي لا يرفع النكاح فعليها استكشاف الحال ومنها الطلاق والعتاق والعفو عن القصاص يثبت حكمها بلا علم الآخر، وأجيب بأنها اسقاطات ومنها خيار المعتقة يصح بلا علم زوجها، وأجيب بأنه لا رواية فيه وعلى التقدير فقد أثبته الشرع مطلقاً. ومنها خيار المالك في بيع الفضولي بدون علم المتعاقدين، وأجيب بكون عقدهما لا وجود في حق المالك. ومنها العدة لازمة عليها وإن لم تعلم بالطلاق وأجيب بأنها واجبة في ضمن الطلاق لا بسببه اهـ. وفي جامع الفتح. قوله : فالزوائد ترد على البائع (الخ هذا خاص بالزيادة المنفصلة الغير المتولدة كالكسب أما غيرها فإنه يمنع الفسخ كما قدمه عن التتارخانية عند قول المصنف كتعيبه) فإذا كانت تمنع الفسخ لا يتأتى ثمرة الاختلاف لأنها إنما تظهر بعد الفسخ .
His saying: (If the one who has the option approves in the absence of his companion, it is valid; if he annuls, it is not) i.e., it is not valid in the absence of his companion, and this is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: Annulment is also valid because he is authorized to annul from the side of his companion, so it does not depend on his knowledge, like approval, and for this his consent is not required, so it becomes like an agent. According to the two, it is a disposition in the right of another, i.e., raising the contract, and it is not free from harm because perhaps he relies on the completion of the previous sale and disposes of it, so he incurs a penalty of value upon destruction if the option is for the seller, or he does not seek a buyer for his commodity if the option is for the buyer, and this is a type of harm, so it depends on his knowledge, and it becomes like the dismissal of an agent, unlike approval because there is no compulsion in it. And it is not said that he is authorized, and how can that be said when his companion does not have the right to annul? And authorization is not valid for something the authorizer does not own. As in al-Hidayah and al-Mi'raj: And similarly the disagreement in khiyar al-ru'yah (option of sight), and there is no disagreement in khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) that he does not have it; the disagreement is only in annulment by speech. But if he annuls by action, it is annulled virtually by agreement in presence and absence, because knowledge is not required in the virtual, like dismissal of an agent, mudarib, partner, and placing the minor permitted for trade under restriction by apostasy, joining (the enemy), or insanity. And in Fath al-Qadir he discussed that voluntary action should be like speech. And the meaning of absence is lack of knowledge, and presence is knowledge. So if he annuls in his absence and it reaches him within the period, the annulment is complete due to the attainment of knowledge; if it reaches him after the period has passed, the annulment is complete by the passing of the period before the annulment. As in al-Hidayah. Similarly, if the seller approves after his annulment before the buyer knows, it is valid and his annulment is void. As mentioned by al-Isbījābī. In al-Dhakhirah: If he buys on condition that the seller, if he is absent from him, his annulment is valid, then the sale is void according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because this is an invalid condition according to the two. And in Fath al-Qadir he favored Abu Yusuf's view. He said: According to this, the objections raised are accepted because they are consistent with the preferred view of Abu Yusuf, but we raise them based on accepting the evidence. Among them: the woman given option (mukhayyara) chooses for herself without her husband's knowledge, and his ruling is binding; answered that binding is by his own obligation. Among them: al-raj'ah (return to wife) is done by the husband alone without her knowledge; even if she marries after it after three menstruations, the marriage is annulled if he proves it; answered that revocable divorce does not remove the marriage, so she must investigate. Among them: divorce, manumission, and pardon for qisas are effective without the other's knowledge; answered that they are removals (isqatat). Among them: the option of the freed slave woman is valid without her husband's knowledge; answered that there is no narration on it, and if it is accepted, the Law has established it absolutely. Among them: the owner's option in a fuduli sale without the knowledge of the contracting parties; answered that their contract has no existence regarding the owner. Among them: the waiting period ('iddah) is obligatory on her even if she does not know of the divorce; answered that it is obligatory within the divorce, not due to it. In Jami' al-Fath: His saying: the accessories are returned to the seller etc., this is specific to accessories that are separate and not generated, like earnings; as for others, they prevent annulment as he previously cited from al-Tatar Khaniyyah at the author's saying 'like its defect'. If they prevent annulment, the fruit of the disagreement does not occur because it appears only after annulment.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion probe that addresses the validity of annulment (faskh) by the party holding khiyar al-shart when the other party is absent. It begins by clarifying the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq: approval (ijazah) in absentia is valid, but annulment is not according to the view of the Sahibayn (here meaning Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf disagrees, analogizing the annulment to approval because the party is authorized to do so. The passage then presents the reasoning of the majority: annulment is a unilateral disposal harming the other party, who might have relied on the contract; thus it requires the other's knowledge, like the dismissal of an agent. The commentary extends this to khiyar al-ru'yah, noting that dispute is only in verbal annulment; annulment by action (e.g., returning the goods) is effective by agreement even in absence. The text then discusses various objections and answers, drawing parallels with divorce, manumission, and other areas where unilateral actions are effective. Finally, it clarifies a point about accessories (zawa'id): only separate, non-generated accessories follow the annulment dispute; other accessories prevent annulment entirely.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Unilateral annulment of a contract by the party holding an option
غيبته (ghaybatuhu): Absence of the other party such that he is unaware of the annulment
عندهما (indahuma): In this passage, refers to the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the meaning of 'غيبة' (absence) in the context of khiyar al-shart?
A) Physical absence from the place of contract
B) Lack of knowledge of the annulment
C) Absence from the city
D) Unavailability of witnesses

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the validity of verbal annulment (faskh) in khiyar al-shart during the other party's absence depends on the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad (invalid without knowledge) and Abu Yusuf (valid immediately), with the later mufta bihi favoring Abu Yusuf's view.

Khiyar al-Shart: Why Rescission Requires Knowledge of the Other Party
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-shart rescission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on rescission (faskh) in khiyar al-shart when the other party is absent, and explain the qiyas that supports it.

Core Idea
Faskh in khiyar al-shart requires the other party's knowledge; ijaza does not.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of rescinding a sale during the option period without the other party's knowledge. While acceptance (ijaza) is valid regardless, rescission (faskh) is not, according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf disagrees, analogizing to agency. The debate centers on whether the potential harm to the relying party requires notification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn's ruling
The matn states: ijaza is valid in the other party's absence, but faskh is not. This is the base position to understand.
This is the rule in Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
2
Recognize the ikhtilaf
The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold the matn's view; Abu Yusuf holds that faskh is also valid in absence. Identify each side.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute, not cross-madhhab.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's qiyas
They analogize faskh to the removal of an agent ('azl al-wakil), which requires the agent's knowledge. The common illa is a disposition affecting another's right with potential harm.
Harm examples: seller may have repurchased reliance; buyer may have consumed the item.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's counter-argument
He analogizes faskh to acceptance, which is valid without knowledge, because the party with khiyar is authorized. The Sahibayn respond that authorization cannot be in something the authorizer does not possess.
The other party does not have the right to rescind themselves.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: If the item is destroyed after a unilateral faskh, liability differs. Also, the timing of knowledge affects validity of rescission.
According to Fath al-Qadir, Abu Yusuf's view is preferred, but the commentary does not enforce it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فلو أجاز من له الخيار بغيبة صاحبه صح ولو فسخ لا) أي لا يصح في غيبة صاحبه وهذا عندهما. وقال أبو يوسف : يجوز الفسخ أيضاً لأنه مسلط على الفسخ من جهة صاحبه فلا يتوقف على علمه كالإجازة ولهذا لا يشترط رضاه فصار كالوكيل. ولهما أنه تصرف في حق الغير وهو العقد بالرفع ولا يعرى عن المضرة لأنه عساه يعتمد تمام البيع السابق فيتصرف فيه فيلزمه غرامة القيمة بالهلاك فيما إذا كان الخيار للبائع أو لا يطلب لسلعته مشترياً فيما إذا كان الخيار للمشتري، وهذا نوع ضرر فيتوقف على علمه وصار كعزل الوكيل بخلاف الإجازة لأنه لا إلزام فيه ولا يقال إنه مسلط وكيف يقال ذلك وصاحبه لا يملك الفسخ ولا تسليط في غير ما يملكه المسلط ؛ كذا في الهداية وفي المعراج : وكذا الخلاف في خيار الرؤية ولا خلاف في خيار العيب أنه لا يملكه والخلاف إنما هو في الفسخ بالقول، أما إذا فسخ بالفعل فإنه ينفسخ حكماً اتفاقاً في الحضرة والغيبة لأنه لا يشترط العلم في الحكمي كعزل الوكيل والمضارب والشريك وحجر المأذون له في التجارة بارتداد ولحوق وجنون. وبحث في فتح القدير بأنه ينبغي أن يكون الفعل الاختياري كالقول. والمراد بالغيبة علمه، وبالحضرة علمه، فلو فسخ في غيبته فبلغه في المدة تم الفسخ لحصول العلم به، ولو بلغه بعد مضي المدة تم بمضي المدة قبل الفسخ؛ كذا في الهداية. وكذا إذا أجاز البائع بعد فسخه قبل أن يعلم المشتري جاز وبطل فسخه؛ كذا ذكر الاسبيجابي. وفي الذخيرة : ولو اشترى على أن البائع لو غاب عنه ففسخه عليه جائز فالبيع فاسد في قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن هذا شرط فاسد عندهما . ورجح في فتح القدير قول أبي يوسف قال : فعلى هذا فالمسائل الموردة نقضاً مسلمة لأنها على وفق ما ترجح من قول أبي يوسف لكنا نوردها بناء على تسليم الدليل ؛ فمنها أن المخيرة يتم اختيارها لنفسها بلا علم زوجها ويلزمه حكم ذلك، وأجيب بأن اللزوم بإيجابه على نفسه. ومنها الرجعة ينفرد بها الزوج بلا علمها حتى لو تزوجت بعدها بعد ثلاث حيض فسخ العقد إذا أثبتها وأجيب بأن الطلاق الرجعي لا يرفع النكاح فعليها استكشاف الحال ومنها الطلاق والعتاق والعفو عن القصاص يثبت حكمها بلا علم الآخر، وأجيب بأنها اسقاطات ومنها خيار المعتقة يصح بلا علم زوجها، وأجيب بأنه لا رواية فيه وعلى التقدير فقد أثبته الشرع مطلقاً. ومنها خيار المالك في بيع الفضولي بدون علم المتعاقدين، وأجيب بكون عقدهما لا وجود في حق المالك. ومنها العدة لازمة عليها وإن لم تعلم بالطلاق وأجيب بأنها واجبة في ضمن الطلاق لا بسببه اهـ. وفي جامع الفتح. قوله : فالزوائد ترد على البائع (الخ هذا خاص بالزيادة المنفصلة الغير المتولدة كالكسب أما غيرها فإنه يمنع الفسخ كما قدمه عن التتارخانية عند قول المصنف كتعيبه) فإذا كانت تمنع الفسخ لا يتأتى ثمرة الاختلاف لأنها إنما تظهر بعد الفسخ.
He said: (If the one with the option gives his approval in the absence of his companion, it is valid; and if he rescinds, it is not) i.e., it is not valid in the absence of his companion. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: Rescission is also valid because he is authorized to rescind from his companion's side, so it does not depend on his knowledge, like acceptance; for this reason his consent is not required, so it becomes like an agent. The argument of the two is that it is a disposition concerning the right of another, which is the cancellation of the contract, and it is not free from harm because perhaps he (the other party) relied on the completion of the previous sale and engaged in some transaction, thus incurring a liability for the value if destroyed, in case the option belongs to the seller, or he may not find a buyer for his commodity if the option belongs to the buyer. This is a type of harm, so it depends on his knowledge, and it becomes like the removal of an agent, unlike acceptance because there is no compulsion in it. It cannot be said that he is authorized; how can that be said when his companion does not possess the right to rescind, and authorization cannot be in something that the authorizer does not possess. Thus in al-Hidayah. And in al-Mi'raj: Likewise the disagreement applies to khiyar al-ru'ya; there is no disagreement regarding khiyar al-'ayb that he does not possess it; the disagreement is only regarding rescission by speech. As for rescission by action, it is effectively canceled unanimously whether the other party is present or absent, because knowledge is not required in the case of implicit rescission, like the removal of an agent, a mudarib, a partner, and the interdiction of a minor authorized to trade due to apostasy, joining (an enemy), or insanity. And there is a discussion in Fath al-Qadir that it should be that voluntary action is like speech. What is meant by absence is his knowledge, and by presence is his knowledge. If he rescinds in his absence and the news reaches him within the period, the rescission is completed due to the attainment of knowledge; if it reaches him after the period has passed, it is completed by the passage of the period before the rescission. Thus in al-Hidayah. Similarly, if the seller approves after his rescission before the buyer knows, it is valid and his rescission becomes void; thus reported al-Isbijabi. In al-Dhakhira: If he buys on the condition that if the seller is absent from him and rescinds, it is valid, then the sale is invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because this is an invalid condition according to them. And in Fath al-Qadir, the view of Abu Yusuf is preferred. He said: On this basis, the cases presented as objections are accepted because they are in accordance with the preferred view of Abu Yusuf, but we present them based on accepting the argument. Among them: The woman with an option (mukhayyara) exercises her choice for herself without her husband's knowledge and its ruling is binding on him. The answer: The binding is due to his own obligation. Another: The husband alone effects revocation (ruj'a) without her knowledge; even if she marries after three menstruations, the marriage is annulled if he proves it. The answer: Revocable divorce does not dissolve the marriage; she must investigate the situation. Another: Divorce, emancipation, and pardon from qisas take effect without the other's knowledge. The answer: They are relinquishments. Another: The option of an emancipated slave woman (mu'taqa) is valid without her husband's knowledge. The answer: There is no narration regarding it, and if it is accepted, the Law has established it absolutely. Another: The option of the owner in the sale of a fuduli without the knowledge of the two contractors. The answer: Their contract does not exist as far as the owner is concerned. Another: The waiting period ('idda) is obligatory upon her even if she did not know of the divorce. The answer: It is obligatory as part of the divorce, not because of it. End of quote. And in Jami' al-Fath: He said: The increments are returned to the seller (this is specific to separate non-derived increments like earnings; as for other increments, they prevent rescission as he presented earlier from al-Tatarkhaniyya at the author's statement 'like its defect'). If they prevent rescission, then the fruit of the disagreement does not appear because it only appears after rescission.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute originating from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The matn states a clear ruling: if the person holding a stipulated option (khiyar al-shart) wishes to accept the contract (ijaza), he may do so validly even in the absence of the other party. However, if he wishes to rescind (faskh), it is not valid in the other's absence. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) explains that this is the position of the Sahibayn: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf dissents, arguing that the power to rescind is delegated by the other party, so it does not require their knowledge, analogous to acceptance and agency. The Sahibayn respond that rescission is a disposition affecting another's right (the contract), entailing potential harm: the other party may have relied on the contract's finality and taken actions (e.g., using a purchased item) leading to liability if the item is destroyed, or the seller may lose a buyer if the buyer has the option. Thus, to avoid harm, knowledge is necessary, similar to the removal of an agent (where the agent must be informed). The discussion continues with a distinction between verbal rescission (which requires knowledge) and actual rescission (e.g., physically altering the item), which is effective automatically regardless of knowledge by analogy with implicit rescission in other contexts. Further, the text addresses an objection from Fath al-Qadir preferring Abu Yusuf's view, and then lists several cases that seem to contradict the Sahibayn's position but are explained away (e.g., the woman with option (mukhayyara) choosing herself, ruj'a, divorce, etc.). Finally, the passage notes a subsidiary ruling about increments (zawa'id): separate non-derived increments (like profit) are returned to the seller; they do not prevent rescission if they are independent. This whole passage exhibits classical Hanafi method: a concise matn ruling, commentary with ikhtilaf, dalil, and resolution of apparent contradictions.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated by one or both parties in a contract to either confirm or rescind within a specified period.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission, cancellation, or revocation of a contract by the party holding the option.
إجازة (ijaza): Approval or ratification of the contract by the party holding the option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), why is rescission (faskh) in khiyar al-shart invalid when the other party is absent?
A) Because rescission is a form of divorce that requires witnesses.
B) Because it may cause harm to the other party who might rely on the contract's finality and incur liability.
C) Because the option expires immediately upon the absence.
D) Because it must be done in a court.

Key Takeaway
In khiyar al-shart, rescission (faskh) requires the other party's knowledge to avoid harm, unlike acceptance (ijaza); this is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf disagrees.

Completion of Contract by Death and Inheritance of Khiyar
Explanation of contract finalization via death, period, emancipation, and inheritance of khiyar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which khiyar are inherited in the Hanafi school and apply the rule that death of the option holder completes the contract unless the khiyar is inherently inheritable.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart is not inherited; death completes the contract, but khiyar al-'ayb and al-ta'yin effectively pass to heirs.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies how a sale contract with an option becomes final when the option holder dies, the period expires, or other events occur. The key distinction is whether the option is personal (like khiyar al-shart) or attached to the property (like khiyar al-'ayb). Understanding this helps avoid errors in inheritance of contractual rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the event that completes the contract
The text lists death, passage of period, emancipation, etc. Determine whether the event constitutes approval or rescission depending on the party.
Death always annuls the option for the deceased, regardless of who holds it.
2
Analyze the effect of death on khiyar
Death annuls the option for the deceased. Distinguish between khiyar that are personal (not inherited) and those that are attached to the property.
Khiyar al-shart is purely a matter of will and cannot be transmitted.
3
List the four khiyar discussed
Identify khiyar al-shart, khiyar al-'ayb, khiyar al-ta'yin, and khiyar al-ru'ya. Note which are inherited and why.
Khiyar al-'ayb and al-ta'yin are effectively inherited due to property attachment.
4
Apply the inheritance rule to specific examples
For khiyar al-naqd, if the buyer dies before payment, the sale is void; heirs cannot pay. For khiyar al-ta'zir, similar rulings apply.
These are discussed further in the text with references.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position on khiyar inheritance
Only khiyar attached to the property (like 'ayb and ta'yin) pass to heirs; khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-qabul do not; khiyar al-ru'ya is subject to ikhtilaf with the preferred view of inheritance.
Consult al-Biri and Ibn al-Diyya for the preferred view on khiyar al-ru'ya.

قوله : (وتم العقد بموته ومضي المدة والاعتاق وتوابعه والأخذ بالشفعة) أي تحصل الإجازة بواحد مما ذكر وهو كلام موهم موقع في الغلط فإن في بعضها يكون إجازة، سواء كان الخيار للبائع أو للمشتري وفي بعضها إنما يكون إجازة إذا كان من المشتري، وأما من البائع ففسخ. أما الموت فإنه مبطل الخيار الميت سواء كان بائعاً أو مشترياً، ولا يورث عندنا كخيار الرؤية لأنه ليس إلا مشيئة وإرادة ولا يتصور انتقاله والإرث فيما يقبل الانتقال لا فيما لا يقبله كملك المنكوحة والعقود التي عقدها المورث لا تنتقل وإنما ملك الوارث الإقالة لانتقال الملك إليه ولذا ملكها الموكل وإن لم يكن عاقداً ؛ كذا في المعراج. ولا يرد علينا خيار العيب فإنه موروث لكون المورث استحق المبيع سليماً فكذا الوارث ففي التحقيق الموروث العين بصفة السلامة من العيوب فأما نفس الخيار فلا يورث. وفي المعراج أن خيار العيب يثبت للوارث ابتداء بدليل أنه لو تعيب بعد موت المشتري في يد البائع كان للوارث رده، وأما خيار التعيين فيثبت للوارث ابتداء لاختلاط ملكه بملك الغير لا أن يورث الخيار؛ هكذا ذكروا وزاد في العناية بأن الوارث لا يملك الفسخ ولا يتأقت خياره بخلاف المورث اهـ. ووجهه ظاهر لأن هذين حكماً خيار الشرط ولم يتكلموا فيما رأيت على غير الأربعة من الخيارات هل تورث أو لا إلا خيار فوات الوصف المرغوب فيه فسيأتي أنه يورث. والضمير في قوله «بموته عائد إلى من له الخيار احترازاً عن موت من لا خيار له لأنه إذا مات فالخيار باق لمن شرط له فإن أمضى مضى وإن فسخ انفسخ ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الظهيرية : الوكيل إذا باع بشرط الخيار فمات الوكيل أو الموكل في المدة بطل الخيار وتم البيع اهـ. وفي قوله: (ولم يتكلموا فيما رأيت الخ) نقل البيري في شرح الأشباه عن خزانة الأكمل: لو اشترى عبداً على أنه إن لم ينقد الثمن غداً فلا بيع بينهما فمات المشتري قبل الغد وقبل نقد الثمن بطل البيع وليس للورثة نقد المال .اهـ. وهذا حكم خيار النقد وقد ذكره في النهر بحثاً، وذكر في المنح بحثاً أن خيار التعزير كذلك وسيأتي خلافه عن المحشي الرملي عند قوله «ولو اشترى عبداً على أنه خباز». وقال البيري أيضاً في كتاب الفرائض ما نصه : وفي شرح المجمع لابن الضيا: وأما خيار الرؤية فالصحيح أنه يورث وأجمعوا أن خيار القبول لا يورث، وكذا خيار الإجازة في بيع الفضولي
His statement: (And the contract is completed by his death, the passage of the period, emancipation and its consequences, and taking by pre-emption.) That is, approval is achieved by one of the mentioned means. This statement is ambiguous and may lead to error, for in some of these means it is approval whether the option belongs to the seller or the buyer, and in some it is approval only if it comes from the buyer; as for from the seller, it is rescission. As for death, it annuls the option for the deceased, whether he was a seller or a buyer, and it is not inherited according to us, like khiyar al-ru'ya, because it is nothing but will and intention, and its transmission is inconceivable; inheritance is for what is transmissible, not for what is not, like ownership of the married woman and the contracts that the deceased made do not transfer; rather, the heir owns the right of cancellation (iqala) due to the transfer of ownership to him, so the principal owns it even if he was not the contractor. Thus in al-Mi'raj. And our position is not refuted by khiyar al-'ayb, for it is inherited because the deceased had a right to receive the sold item free of defects; similarly the heir; in reality, what is inherited is the item with the quality of being free from defects; as for the option itself, it is not inherited. And in al-Mi'raj: Khiyar al-'ayb is established for the heir initially, evidence being that if the item becomes defective after the buyer's death while still in the seller's hand, the heir may return it. As for khiyar al-ta'yin, it is established for the heir initially due to the mixing of his property with others' property, not that the option is inherited. Thus they mentioned, and al-'Inaya added that the heir does not possess the right to rescind, and his option is not time-limited, unlike the deceased. Its reasoning is apparent because these two (khiyar al-'ayb and khiyar al-ta'yin) are not khiyar al-shart. And they did not discuss, as far as I have seen, regarding other options beyond these four whether they are inherited or not, except khiyar fawat al-wasf al-marghub fih; it will come that it is inherited. The pronoun in 'his death' refers to the one who has the option, to exclude the death of one who does not have the option; because if he dies, the option remains for the person for whom it was stipulated; if he ratifies, it is ratified; if he rescinds, it is rescinded. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Zahiriyya: If an agent sells with a condition of option, and the agent or the principal dies during the period, the option becomes void and the sale is completed. And in his statement: (And they did not discuss, as far as I have seen...) al-Biri in Sharh al-Ashbah quotes from Khizanat al-Akmal: If one buys a slave on the condition that if he does not pay the price tomorrow there is no sale, and the buyer dies before tomorrow and before paying the price, the sale is void and the heirs may not pay the money. This is the ruling on khiyar al-naqd, and it has been mentioned in al-Nahr as a discussion, and it is mentioned in al-Manh as a discussion that khiyar al-ta'zir is similar, and its contrary will come from al-Muhashi al-Ramli at his statement 'If one buys a slave on the condition that he is a baker'. And al-Biri also said in the book of inheritance: In Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn al-Diyya: As for khiyar al-ru'ya, the correct view is that it is inherited, and they are agreed that khiyar al-qabul is not inherited, and similarly khiyar al-ijaza in the sale of a fuduli.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the matn statement from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: the contract is completed by the death of the party with khiyar, by the passage of the option period, by emancipation (if a slave is sold with khiyar and then emancipated), by related actions, and by the exercise of pre-emption (shuf'a). The commentator clarifies that these events may constitute either actual approval (ijaza) or rescission (faskh) depending on which party triggers them. For example, if the seller with khiyar emancipates the slave, that constitutes rescission (since he is exercising ownership), while if the buyer does so, it constitutes approval. Death is a special case: when the person holding khiyar dies, the option is annulled because it is purely a matter of will and cannot be inherited; the contract becomes final. This is analogous to khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection) which is also not inherited. However, khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) is inheritable, but the commentator explains this is because what is inherited is the right to receive a sound item, not the option itself; similarly, khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification) is established for the heir initially due to confusion of property. The text distinguishes between types of khiyar: khiyar al-shart is not inherited; khiyar al-'ayb and khiyar al-ta'yin are effectively transmitted; khiyar al-ru'ya is debated as to inheritance, with a preferred view that it is inherited, while other khiyar like khiyar al-qabul (option of acceptance) and khiyar al-ijaza in fuduli sales are not inherited. The passage also cites examples from other sources regarding khiyar al-naqd (option of payment) and khiyar al-ta'zir (option of punishment) and notes a forthcoming discussion. The overall message is that the completion of a contract via these events depends on the nature of the event and who performs it.

Key Terms
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): The option to return a purchased item due to a defect present at the time of sale.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): The option to confirm or rescind a sale after inspecting the item if sold sight unseen.
خيار النقد (khiyar al-naqd): An option based on payment of price within a period; if not paid, the sale is void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what happens to khiyar al-shart when the party holding it dies?
A) It passes to the heirs who can exercise it.
B) It becomes void and the contract is completed.
C) It remains until the end of the stipulated period.
D) It must be exercised immediately by the executor.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, khiyar al-shart is not inherited; death completes the contract, but khiyar al-'ayb and al-ta'yin pass to heirs as attached rights.

Khiyar al-Shart Not Inherited: Contract Completed by Death
Commentary on death completing the contract and the non-inheritance of khiyar al-shart.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that khiyar al-shart is not inherited and explain the reasoning, including the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the father/executor.

Core Idea
Death of the option-holder completes the contract; khiyar al-shart, being mere will, cannot be inherited.

This lesson examines a central Hanafi principle: the stipulated option (khiyar al-shart) is a personal right that does not transfer to heirs. When the option-holder dies, the contract becomes binding immediately. We will explore the textual proof from the commentary, the underlying reasoning (mere will and desire), and the important intra-Hanafi variation concerning purchases by a father or executor for an orphan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Find the statement in the passage that directly says khiyar al-shart is not inherited and the contract is completed by death.
2
Understand the rationale
Note the reason given: the option is nothing but will and desire (mashi’ah wa iradah), which cannot be transferred by inheritance.
3
Distinguish from khiyar al-‘ayb
See how the author distinguishes khiyar al-shart from khiyar al-‘ayb: the latter is not inherited but arises anew for the heir because the decedent was entitled to a sound item.
This is a key Ḥanafī nuance.
4
Analyse the intra-Hanafi dispute
Examine the disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad over whether the father/executor’s option transfers to the minor upon majority.
Abu Yusuf’s view (sale binding) is the mu‘tamad.
