قوله : (وتم العقد بموته ومضي المدة والاعتاق وتوابعه والأخذ بالشفعة) أي تحصل الإجازة بواحد مما ذكر وهو كلام موهم موقع في الغلط فإن في بعضها يكون إجازة، سواء كان الخيار للبائع أو للمشتري وفي بعضها إنما يكون إجازة إذا كان من المشتري، وأما من البائع ففسخ. أما الموت فإنه مبطل الخيار الميت سواء كان بائعاً أو مشترياً، ولا يورث عندنا كخيار الرؤية لأنه ليس إلا مشيئة وإرادة ولا يتصور انتقاله والإرث فيما يقبل الانتقال لا فيما لا يقبله كملك المنكوحة والعقود التي عقدها المورث لا تنتقل وإنما ملك الوارث الإقالة لانتقال الملك إليه ولذا ملكها الموكل وإن لم يكن عاقداً ؛ كذا في المعراج. ولا يرد علينا خيار العيب فإنه موروث لكون المورث استحق المبيع سليماً فكذا الوارث ففي التحقيق الموروث العين بصفة السلامة من العيوب فأما نفس الخيار فلا يورث. وفي المعراج أن خيار العيب يثبت للوارث ابتداء بدليل أنه لو تعيب بعد موت المشتري في يد البائع كان للوارث رده، وأما خيار التعيين فيثبت للوارث ابتداء لاختلاط ملكه بملك الغير لا أن يورث الخيار؛ هكذا ذكروا وزاد في العناية بأن الوارث لا يملك الفسخ ولا يتأقت خياره بخلاف المورث اهـ. ووجهه ظاهر لأن هذين حكماً خيار الشرط ولم يتكلموا فيما رأيت على غير الأربعة من الخيارات هل تورث أو لا إلا خيار فوات الوصف المرغوب فيه فسيأتي أنه يورث. والضمير في قوله «بموته عائد إلى من له الخيار احترازاً عن موت من لا خيار له لأنه إذا مات فالخيار باق لمن شرط له فإن أمضى مضى وإن فسخ انفسخ ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الظهيرية : الوكيل إذا باع بشرط الخيار فمات الوكيل أو الموكل في المدة بطل الخيار وتم البيع اهـ.
قوله: (ولم يتكلموا فيما رأيت الخ) نقل البيري في شرح الأشباه عن خزانة الأكمل: لو اشترى عبداً على أنه إن لم ينقد الثمن غداً فلا بيع بينهما فمات المشتري قبل الغد وقبل نقد الثمن بطل البيع وليس للورثة نقد المال .اهـ. وهذا حكم خيار النقد وقد ذكره في النهر بحثاً، وذكر في المنح بحثاً أن خيار التعزير كذلك وسيأتي خلافه عن المحشي الرملي عند قوله «ولو اشترى عبداً على أنه خباز». وقال البيري أيضاً في كتاب الفرائض ما نصه : وفي شرح المجمع لابن الضيا: وأما خيار الرؤية فالصحيح أنه يورث وأجمعوا أن خيار القبول لا يورث، وكذا خيار الإجازة في بيع الفضولي جامع الفصولين وكيل البيع أو الوصي باع بخيار أو المالك بنفسه باع بخيار لغيره فمات الوكيل أو الوصي أو الموكل أو الصبي أو من باع بنفسه أو من شرط له الخيار قال محمد : البيع في كل ذلك لأن لكل منهم حقاً في الخيار والجنون كالموت اهـ. وفي المعراج : ولو كان الخيار لهما فمات أحدهما لزم البيع من جهته والآخر على خياره .اهـ. وقد أفاد كلامه أن الخيار لا ينتقل عمن هو له إلى غيره فلذا قال أبو يوسف : إذا اشترى الأب أو الوصي شيئاً لليتيم وشرط الخيار لنفسه فبلغ الصبي في المدة تم البيع. وقال محمد توقف على إجازة الابن فكأنه باشره بعد بلوغه حتى قيل لا تتأقت بالثلاث وعن محمد أن للوصي أن يفسخ بعد بلوغ الصغير وليس له أن يجيز إلا برضاه. وروي أن الأب أو الوصي إذا اشترى عبداً للصغير بدراهم أو دنانير بشرط الخيار ثم بلغ الصغير في المدة ثم أجاز أنفذ الشراء عليهما إلا أن تكون الإجازة برضا الصغير بعد البلوغ فينفذ عليه. ولو حجر السيد على عبده المأذون تم البيع، وقيل ينتقل الخيار إلى المولى. ولو اشترى المكاتب أو باع بشرط الخيار ثم عجز في الثلاث تم البيع عندهم؛ كذا في الظهيرية. فقد علم أن الخيار لا ينتقل على المعتمد لأن قول أبي يوسف في الأولى هو المعتمد ولكن خرج عنه العبد المأذون إذا باع بشرط الخيار فإن للمولى الإجازة إن لم يكن مديوناً ولا يجوز فسخه عليه إلا أن يجعله لنفسه ثم يفسخ بحضرة المشتري أو بما يكون فسخاً من الأفعال في غيبة المشتري؛ كذا في الظهيرية.
وأما الوكيل إذا عزل وله الخيار فإنه لا يبطل اتفاقاً؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج. وأما مضي فمبطل للخيار، سواء كان للبائع أو للمشتري إذ لم يثبت الخيار إلا فيها فلا بقاء له بعدها كالمخيرة في وقت مقدر وأما الإعتاق وتوابعه وهي التدبير والكتابة فإنما يتم به إذا كان الخيار للمشتري وفعلها، أما إذا كان للبائع وفعلها كان فسخاً. وذكر المصنف السقوط بطريق الضرورة وهو الموت ومضي المدة والسقوط بطريق الدلالة وهو الإعتاق، ولم يذكر ما يكون إجازة بالقول صريحاً ولا ما يكون إجازة بالفعل أما الأول ففي جامع الفصولين : المشتري بالخيار إذا قال أجزت شراءه أو شئت أخذه أو رضيت أخذه بطل خياره، ولو قال هويت أخذه أو أحببت أو أردت أو أعجبني أو وافقني لا يبطل .اهـ. وفيه: لو طلب المشتري الأجر جر من الساكن بطل خياره، ولو دعا الجارية إلى فراشه لا يبطل سواء كان الخيار للبائع أو للمشتري. وأما الثاني ففيه لو حجم العبد أو سقاه دواء أو حلق رأسه كان رضا لا لو أمر وكذا الأجل لا يورث اهـ . لكن ما ذكره من أن خيار الرؤية يورث خلاف ما ذكره المؤلف هنا و خلاف ما في الغرر والوقاية والمنتقى ومختصر النقاية وإصلاح الوقاية لابن كمال، وبه صرح في الهداية والفتح من باب خيار الرؤية علم أن هذا التصحيح غريب قوله : (ولا ما يكون إجازة بالفعل) حكم عليه في النهر بأنه سهو لأنه نبه عليها بقوله والإعتاق». قوله : (بخلاف السكر من
His statement: (And the contract is completed by his death, the passing of the period, emancipation and its consequences, and the taking of shuf'a) means that ratification (ijāzah) occurs through one of the mentioned matters. This wording is potentially misleading, for in some of these matters it is ratification, whether the option is for the seller or the buyer, and in some it is only ratification if it comes from the buyer, whereas from the seller it is rescission. As for death, it nullifies the option of the deceased, whether he is seller or buyer, and it is not inherited according to us, like the option of seeing (khiyār al-ru'yah), because it is nothing but will and desire, and its transfer is inconceivable. Inheritance pertains to what is subject to transfer, not to what is not, like the ownership of a married woman; contracts made by the decedent are not transferred, but the heir only possesses the right of rescission (iqālah) due to the transfer of ownership to him. Hence the agent possesses it even if he was not the contractor. (So in al-Mi'rāj). The option of defect (khiyār al-'ayb) is not an objection to us, for it is inherited because the decedent was entitled to the sold item sound, so too the heir. In reality, what is inherited is the item with the attribute of freedom from defects; the option itself is not inherited. In al-Mi'rāj, the option of defect is established for the heir as a new right, evidenced by the fact that if a defect occurs after the buyer's death while the item is in the seller's hand, the heir may return it. As for the option of specification (khiyār al-ta'yīn), it is established for the heir as a new right due to the intermingling of his property with another's, not that the option is inherited. Thus they mentioned, and in al-'Ināyah he added that the heir does not possess the right of rescission and his option is not bounded by time, unlike the decedent. Its reasoning is apparent, because these are rulings of the option of stipulation (khiyār al-sharṭ). And they did not discuss, as far as I have seen, regarding other than these four options whether they are inherited or not, except the option of lacking a desired attribute (khiyār fawt al-waṣf al-marghūb fīh), which will come that it is inherited. The pronoun in his words 'by his death' (bimawtihī) refers to the one who holds the option, to exclude the death of one who has no option, because if he dies, the option remains for the one for whom it was stipulated; if he ratifies, it is effective, and if he rescinds, it is rescinded. (Thus in Fatḥ al-Qadīr). And in al-Ẓahiriyyah: If the agent sells with a stipulated option and the agent or the principal dies during the period, the option is void and the sale is complete. (end).
His statement: (And they did not discuss, as far as I have seen, ...) al-Bayrī in Sharḥ al-Ashbāh narrated from Khizānat al-Akmal: If one buys a slave on the condition that if he does not pay the price tomorrow there is no sale between them, and the buyer dies before tomorrow and before paying the price, the sale is void and the heirs have no right to pay the money. (end). This is the ruling of the option of payment (khiyār al-naqd), which was mentioned in al-Nahr as a discussion. And in al-Minaḥ it was discussed that the option of ta'zīr (khiyār al-ta'zīr) is likewise, and its contrary will come from al-Muḥashshī al-Ramlī at his statement: 'And if one buys a slave on condition that he is a baker.' Al-Bayrī also said in the Book of Inheritances: In Sharḥ al-Majmaʿ by Ibn al-Ḍiyā: As for the option of seeing (khiyār al-ru'yah), the correct view is that it is inherited, and they agreed that the option of acceptance (khiyār al-qabūl) is not inherited, and likewise the option of ratification in the sale of a fudūlī. Jāmiʿ al-Fuṣūlayn: The agent of the sale or the executor sells with an option, or the owner himself sells with an option for someone else, then the agent, executor, principal, minor, or the one who sold himself, or the one for whom the option was stipulated dies. Muḥammad said: The sale stands in all these cases because each of them has a right in the option, and insanity is like death. (end). And in al-Miʿrāj: If the option belongs to both of them and one of them dies, the sale becomes binding from his side, and the other remains with his option. (end). His statement indicates that the option does not transfer from the one who holds it to another. Hence Abū Yūsuf said: If the father or executor buys something for the orphan and stipulates the option for himself, and the minor reaches majority during the period, the sale is complete. Muḥammad said: It is suspended on the ratification of the son, as if he performed it after majority, so it was said it is not bounded by three days. And from Muḥammad: The executor may rescind after the minor reaches majority, but he may not ratify except with his consent. It is narrated that if the father or executor buys a slave for the minor with dirhams or dinars with a stipulated option, then the minor reaches majority during the period and then ratifies, the purchase is effective upon both, unless the ratification is with the minor's consent after majority, in which case it is binding on him. And if the master restricts his authorized slave, the sale is complete, and it is said the option transfers to the master. And if a mukātab buys or sells with a stipulated option then becomes unable during the three days, the sale is complete according to them. (Thus in al-Ẓahiriyyah). So it is known that the option does not transfer according to the relied-upon view, because the saying of Abū Yūsuf in the first case is the relied-upon, but the case of the authorized slave when he sells with a stipulated option is excepted; the master has the right to ratify if he is not in debt, and his rescission is not permissible unless he stipulates it for himself and then rescinds in the presence of the buyer or by an act that constitutes rescission in the buyer's absence. (Thus in al-Ẓahiriyyah).
As for the agent if he is dismissed and he had the option, it is not void by consensus. (Thus in al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj). As for the passing of time, it nullifies the option, whether it is for the seller or the buyer, because the option was only established within the period, so it does not remain after it, like the option of the woman given choice (mukhayyarah) in a specified time. As for emancipation and its consequences, i.e., tadbīr and kitābah, it completes the contract if done when the option is for the buyer; if done when the option is for the seller, it is rescission. The author mentioned termination by necessary implication (ḍarūrah) i.e., death and passage of time, and termination by indication (dalālah) i.e., emancipation, and he did not mention what constitutes ratification by explicit statement nor what constitutes ratification by act. As for the first: In Jāmiʿ al-Fuṣūlayn: The buyer with an option, if he says 'I ratify the purchase' or 'I wish to take it' or 'I accept to take it', his option becomes void. If he says 'I desire to take it' or 'I love' or 'I intend' or 'it pleases me' or 'it agrees with me', it does not become void. (end). And in it: If the buyer demands rent from the tenant, his option becomes void; if he calls the slave-girl to his bed, it does not become void, whether the option is for the buyer or the seller. As for the second: In it, if he cupped the slave, or gave him medicine, or shaved his head, it is consent, but not if he ordered it. Likewise the term is not inherited. (end). But what he mentioned that the option of seeing is inherited contradicts what the author mentioned here and what is in al-Ghurar, al-Wiqāyah, al-Muntaqā, Mukhtaṣar al-Niqāyah, and Iṣlāḥ al-Wiqāyah by Ibn Kamāl, and it is explicitly stated in al-Hidāyah and al-Fatḥ in the chapter of the option of seeing. It is known that this correction is strange. His statement: (And he did not mention what is ratification by act) was ruled in al-Nahr as an oversight because he indicated it by his words 'and emancipation'. Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq is a commentary (sharḥ) on the statement of the author of Kanz al-Daqā'iq regarding the completion of the contract through death, passage of time, emancipation, and taking of shuf'a. The commentator begins by clarifying that the author's words may be misleading: while death, passage of time, and emancipation all cause the contract to become binding, their effect differs depending on who holds the option. Death nullifies the option of the deceased entirely, and the option is not inherited (except for khiyar al-'ayb and khiyar al-ta'yin, which are established anew for the heir). The commentator explains the rationale: khiyar al-shart is merely a matter of will and desire, which cannot be transferred by inheritance. He distinguishes from khiyar al-'ayb, where the right to a sound item passes to the heir. The text then discusses various scenarios: the death of the agent vs. principal, the effect of declaring the buyer's option (even if the seller dies), and the inheritance of different types of khiyar. A dispute is noted regarding khiyar al-ru'yah: some sources claim it is inherited, but the majority of Hanafi authorities, including the author of Kanz, maintain it is not. The passage also covers actions that constitute acceptance or revocation of the option, such as explicit words like 'I ratify' versus mere expressions of desire, and physical acts like cupping or shaving the slave's head. The commentator critiques the author's omission of ratification by explicit statement and act, noting that the author's mention of emancipation serves to indicate ratification by act. Overall, this lesson provides a detailed analysis of the conditions under which an option is terminated and whether it transfers to heirs, with special attention to the various types of khiyar in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyār al-sharṭ): The option stipulated in a contract by which one or both parties can rescind within a specified period.
خيار العيب (khiyār al-'ayb): The option to return a defective item; it is established for the heir as a new right because the decedent deserved a sound item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to a sale with a stipulated option (khiyar al-shart) if the buyer dies during the option period?
A) The sale becomes void because the option is inherited by the heirs.
B) The sale becomes binding because khiyar al-shart is not inherited.
C) The heirs have the option to either complete or rescind the sale.
D) The sale is suspended until the heirs decide.

Key Takeaway
Death of the option-holder immediately completes a sale with a stipulated option, as the option is not inheritable.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Inheritance of Other Options: 'Ayb, Ta'yin, and Ru'yah
Commentary on inheritance and establishment of various options for heirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between khiyar al-'ayb, khiyar al-ta'yin, and khiyar al-ru'yah regarding their inheritance or establishment for heirs, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-ru'yah.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-'ayb and khiyar al-ta'yin arise anew for the heir; khiyar al-ru'yah is not inherited per the majority.

In the previous lesson, we learned that khiyar al-shart is not inherited. This lesson expands to other options: the option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb), the option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin), and the option of seeing (khiyar al-ru'yah). The commentary clarifies that while khiyar al-'ayb and khiyar al-ta'yin are established for the heir as new rights, khiyar al-ru'yah is not inherited according to the authoritative position, despite a minority claim. We will also see how the passage addresses khiyar al-naqd (payment option) and actions that constitute ratification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for khiyar al-‘ayb
Find the statement that the option of defect is not inherited per se but the heir gets a new right because the decedent was entitled to a sound item.
2
Identify the ruling for khiyar al-ta‘yīn
Note that the option of specification is also established for the heir as a new right due to intermingled ownership.
3
Analyse the dispute on khiyar al-ru’yah
The commentator rejects the view that khiyar al-ru’yah is inherited, citing al-Hidāyah and other authoritative texts. Some later sources claim it is inherited, but this is called 'strange' (gharīb).
4
Examine other options mentioned
Look at khiyar al-naqd (payment option) mentioned via al-Bayrī, where death of the buyer voids the sale and heirs cannot pay. Also note khiyar al-ta'zīr mentioned similarly.
5
Review actions constituting ratification
The passage lists explicit words like 'I ratify' that void the option, and acts like cupping or shaving that indicate consent, but not mere desire statements.

قوله : (وتم العقد بموته ومضي المدة والاعتاق وتوابعه والأخذ بالشفعة) أي تحصل الإجازة بواحد مما ذكر وهو كلام موهم موقع في الغلط فإن في بعضها يكون إجازة، سواء كان الخيار للبائع أو للمشتري وفي بعضها إنما يكون إجازة إذا كان من المشتري، وأما من البائع ففسخ. أما الموت فإنه مبطل الخيار الميت سواء كان بائعاً أو مشترياً، ولا يورث عندنا كخيار الرؤية لأنه ليس إلا مشيئة وإرادة ولا يتصور انتقاله والإرث فيما يقبل الانتقال لا فيما لا يقبله كملك المنكوحة والعقود التي عقدها المورث لا تنتقل وإنما ملك الوارث الإقالة لانتقال الملك إليه ولذا ملكها الموكل وإن لم يكن عاقداً ؛ كذا في المعراج. ولا يرد علينا خيار العيب فإنه موروث لكون المورث استحق المبيع سليماً فكذا الوارث ففي التحقيق الموروث العين بصفة السلامة من العيوب فأما نفس الخيار فلا يورث. وفي المعراج أن خيار العيب يثبت للوارث ابتداء بدليل أنه لو تعيب بعد موت المشتري في يد البائع كان للوارث رده، وأما خيار التعيين فيثبت للوارث ابتداء لاختلاط ملكه بملك الغير لا أن يورث الخيار؛ هكذا ذكروا وزاد في العناية بأن الوارث لا يملك الفسخ ولا يتأقت خياره بخلاف المورث اهـ. ووجهه ظاهر لأن هذين حكماً خيار الشرط ولم يتكلموا فيما رأيت على غير الأربعة من الخيارات هل تورث أو لا إلا خيار فوات الوصف المرغوب فيه فسيأتي أنه يورث. والضمير في قوله «بموته عائد إلى من له الخيار احترازاً عن موت من لا خيار له لأنه إذا مات فالخيار باق لمن شرط له فإن أمضى مضى وإن فسخ انفسخ ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الظهيرية : الوكيل إذا باع بشرط الخيار فمات الوكيل أو الموكل في المدة بطل الخيار وتم البيع اهـ.
قوله: (ولم يتكلموا فيما رأيت الخ) نقل البيري في شرح الأشباه عن خزانة الأكمل: لو اشترى عبداً على أنه إن لم ينقد الثمن غداً فلا بيع بينهما فمات المشتري قبل الغد وقبل نقد الثمن بطل البيع وليس للورثة نقد المال .اهـ. وهذا حكم خيار النقد وقد ذكره في النهر بحثاً، وذكر في المنح بحثاً أن خيار التعزير كذلك وسيأتي خلافه عن المحشي الرملي عند قوله «ولو اشترى عبداً على أنه خباز». وقال البيري أيضاً في كتاب الفرائض ما نصه : وفي شرح المجمع لابن الضيا: وأما خيار الرؤية فالصحيح أنه يورث وأجمعوا أن خيار القبول لا يورث، وكذا خيار الإجازة في بيع الفضولي جامع الفصولين وكيل البيع أو الوصي باع بخيار أو المالك بنفسه باع بخيار لغيره فمات الوكيل أو الوصي أو الموكل أو الصبي أو من باع بنفسه أو من شرط له الخيار قال محمد : البيع في كل ذلك لأن لكل منهم حقاً في الخيار والجنون كالموت اهـ. وفي المعراج : ولو كان الخيار لهما فمات أحدهما لزم البيع من جهته والآخر على خياره .اهـ. وقد أفاد كلامه أن الخيار لا ينتقل عمن هو له إلى غيره فلذا قال أبو يوسف : إذا اشترى الأب أو الوصي شيئاً لليتيم وشرط الخيار لنفسه فبلغ الصبي في المدة تم البيع. وقال محمد توقف على إجازة الابن فكأنه باشره بعد بلوغه حتى قيل لا تتأقت بالثلاث وعن محمد أن للوصي أن يفسخ بعد بلوغ الصغير وليس له أن يجيز إلا برضاه. وروي أن الأب أو الوصي إذا اشترى عبداً للصغير بدراهم أو دنانير بشرط الخيار ثم بلغ الصغير في المدة ثم أجاز أنفذ الشراء عليهما إلا أن تكون الإجازة برضا الصغير بعد البلوغ فينفذ عليه. ولو حجر السيد على عبده المأذون تم البيع، وقيل ينتقل الخيار إلى المولى. ولو اشترى المكاتب أو باع بشرط الخيار ثم عجز في الثلاث تم البيع عندهم؛ كذا في الظهيرية. فقد علم أن الخيار لا ينتقل على المعتمد لأن قول أبي يوسف في الأولى هو المعتمد ولكن خرج عنه العبد المأذون إذا باع بشرط الخيار فإن للمولى الإجازة إن لم يكن مديوناً ولا يجوز فسخه عليه إلا أن يجعله لنفسه ثم يفسخ بحضرة المشتري أو بما يكون فسخاً من الأفعال في غيبة المشتري؛ كذا في الظهيرية.
وأما الوكيل إذا عزل وله الخيار فإنه لا يبطل اتفاقاً؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج. وأما مضي فمبطل للخيار، سواء كان للبائع أو للمشتري إذ لم يثبت الخيار إلا فيها فلا بقاء له بعدها كالمخيرة في وقت مقدر وأما الإعتاق وتوابعه وهي التدبير والكتابة فإنما يتم به إذا كان الخيار للمشتري وفعلها، أما إذا كان للبائع وفعلها كان فسخاً. وذكر المصنف السقوط بطريق الضرورة وهو الموت ومضي المدة والسقوط بطريق الدلالة وهو الإعتاق، ولم يذكر ما يكون إجازة بالقول صريحاً ولا ما يكون إجازة بالفعل أما الأول ففي جامع الفصولين : المشتري بالخيار إذا قال أجزت شراءه أو شئت أخذه أو رضيت أخذه بطل خياره، ولو قال هويت أخذه أو أحببت أو أردت أو أعجبني أو وافقني لا يبطل .اهـ. وفيه: لو طلب المشتري الأجر جر من الساكن بطل خياره، ولو دعا الجارية إلى فراشه لا يبطل سواء كان الخيار للبائع أو للمشتري. وأما الثاني ففيه لو حجم العبد أو سقاه دواء أو حلق رأسه كان رضا لا لو أمر وكذا الأجل لا يورث اهـ . لكن ما ذكره من أن خيار الرؤية يورث خلاف ما ذكره المؤلف هنا و خلاف ما في الغرر والوقاية والمنتقى ومختصر النقاية وإصلاح الوقاية لابن كمال، وبه صرح في الهداية والفتح من باب خيار الرؤية علم أن هذا التصحيح غريب قوله : (ولا ما يكون إجازة بالفعل) حكم عليه في النهر بأنه سهو لأنه نبه عليها بقوله والإعتاق». قوله : (بخلاف السكر من
His statement: (And the contract is completed by his death, the passing of the period, emancipation and its consequences, and the taking of shuf'a) means that ratification (ijāzah) occurs through one of the mentioned matters. This wording is potentially misleading, for in some of these matters it is ratification, whether the option is for the seller or the buyer, and in some it is only ratification if it comes from the buyer, whereas from the seller it is rescission. As for death, it nullifies the option of the deceased, whether he is seller or buyer, and it is not inherited according to us, like the option of seeing (khiyār al-ru'yah), because it is nothing but will and desire, and its transfer is inconceivable. Inheritance pertains to what is subject to transfer, not to what is not, like the ownership of a married woman; contracts made by the decedent are not transferred, but the heir only possesses the right of rescission (iqālah) due to the transfer of ownership to him. Hence the agent possesses it even if he was not the contractor. (So in al-Mi'rāj). The option of defect (khiyār al-'ayb) is not an objection to us, for it is inherited because the decedent was entitled to the sold item sound, so too the heir. In reality, what is inherited is the item with the attribute of freedom from defects; the option itself is not inherited. In al-Mi'rāj, the option of defect is established for the heir as a new right, evidenced by the fact that if a defect occurs after the buyer's death while the item is in the seller's hand, the heir may return it. As for the option of specification (khiyār al-ta'yīn), it is established for the heir as a new right due to the intermingling of his property with another's, not that the option is inherited. Thus they mentioned, and in al-'Ināyah he added that the heir does not possess the right of rescission and his option is not bounded by time, unlike the decedent. Its reasoning is apparent, because these are rulings of the option of stipulation (khiyār al-sharṭ). And they did not discuss, as far as I have seen, regarding other than these four options whether they are inherited or not, except the option of lacking a desired attribute (khiyār fawt al-waṣf al-marghūb fīh), which will come that it is inherited. The pronoun in his words 'by his death' (bimawtihī) refers to the one who holds the option, to exclude the death of one who has no option, because if he dies, the option remains for the one for whom it was stipulated; if he ratifies, it is effective, and if he rescinds, it is rescinded. (Thus in Fatḥ al-Qadīr). And in al-Ẓahiriyyah: If the agent sells with a stipulated option and the agent or the principal dies during the period, the option is void and the sale is complete. (end).
His statement: (And they did not discuss, as far as I have seen, ...) al-Bayrī in Sharḥ al-Ashbāh narrated from Khizānat al-Akmal: If one buys a slave on the condition that if he does not pay the price tomorrow there is no sale between them, and the buyer dies before tomorrow and before paying the price, the sale is void and the heirs have no right to pay the money. (end). This is the ruling of the option of payment (khiyār al-naqd), which was mentioned in al-Nahr as a discussion. And in al-Minaḥ it was discussed that the option of ta'zīr (khiyār al-ta'zīr) is likewise, and its contrary will come from al-Muḥashshī al-Ramlī at his statement: 'And if one buys a slave on condition that he is a baker.' Al-Bayrī also said in the Book of Inheritances: In Sharḥ al-Majmaʿ by Ibn al-Ḍiyā: As for the option of seeing (khiyār al-ru'yah), the correct view is that it is inherited, and they agreed that the option of acceptance (khiyār al-qabūl) is not inherited, and likewise the option of ratification in the sale of a fudūlī. Jāmiʿ al-Fuṣūlayn: The agent of the sale or the executor sells with an option, or the owner himself sells with an option for someone else, then the agent, executor, principal, minor, or the one who sold himself, or the one for whom the option was stipulated dies. Muḥammad said: The sale stands in all these cases because each of them has a right in the option, and insanity is like death. (end). And in al-Miʿrāj: If the option belongs to both of them and one of them dies, the sale becomes binding from his side, and the other remains with his option. (end). His statement indicates that the option does not transfer from the one who holds it to another. Hence Abū Yūsuf said: If the father or executor buys something for the orphan and stipulates the option for himself, and the minor reaches majority during the period, the sale is complete. Muḥammad said: It is suspended on the ratification of the son, as if he performed it after majority, so it was said it is not bounded by three days. And from Muḥammad: The executor may rescind after the minor reaches majority, but he may not ratify except with his consent. It is narrated that if the father or executor buys a slave for the minor with dirhams or dinars with a stipulated option, then the minor reaches majority during the period and then ratifies, the purchase is effective upon both, unless the ratification is with the minor's consent after majority, in which case it is binding on him. And if the master restricts his authorized slave, the sale is complete, and it is said the option transfers to the master. And if a mukātab buys or sells with a stipulated option then becomes unable during the three days, the sale is complete according to them. (Thus in al-Ẓahiriyyah). So it is known that the option does not transfer according to the relied-upon view, because the saying of Abū Yūsuf in the first case is the relied-upon, but the case of the authorized slave when he sells with a stipulated option is excepted; the master has the right to ratify if he is not in debt, and his rescission is not permissible unless he stipulates it for himself and then rescinds in the presence of the buyer or by an act that constitutes rescission in the buyer's absence. (Thus in al-Ẓahiriyyah).
As for the agent if he is dismissed and he had the option, it is not void by consensus. (Thus in al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj). As for the passing of time, it nullifies the option, whether it is for the seller or the buyer, because the option was only established within the period, so it does not remain after it, like the option of the woman given choice (mukhayyarah) in a specified time. As for emancipation and its consequences, i.e., tadbīr and kitābah, it completes the contract if done when the option is for the buyer; if done when the option is for the seller, it is rescission. The author mentioned termination by necessary implication (ḍarūrah) i.e., death and passage of time, and termination by indication (dalālah) i.e., emancipation, and he did not mention what constitutes ratification by explicit statement nor what constitutes ratification by act. As for the first: In Jāmiʿ al-Fuṣūlayn: The buyer with an option, if he says 'I ratify the purchase' or 'I wish to take it' or 'I accept to take it', his option becomes void. If he says 'I desire to take it' or 'I love' or 'I intend' or 'it pleases me' or 'it agrees with me', it does not become void. (end). And in it: If the buyer demands rent from the tenant, his option becomes void; if he calls the slave-girl to his bed, it does not become void, whether the option is for the buyer or the seller. As for the second: In it, if he cupped the slave, or gave him medicine, or shaved his head, it is consent, but not if he ordered it. Likewise the term is not inherited. (end). But what he mentioned that the option of seeing is inherited contradicts what the author mentioned here and what is in al-Ghurar, al-Wiqāyah, al-Muntaqā, Mukhtaṣar al-Niqāyah, and Iṣlāḥ al-Wiqāyah by Ibn Kamāl, and it is explicitly stated in al-Hidāyah and al-Fatḥ in the chapter of the option of seeing. It is known that this correction is strange. His statement: (And he did not mention what is ratification by act) was ruled in al-Nahr as an oversight because he indicated it by his words 'and emancipation'. Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq is a commentary (sharḥ) on the statement of the author of Kanz al-Daqā'iq regarding the completion of the contract through death, passage of time, emancipation, and taking of shuf'a. The commentator begins by clarifying that the author's words may be misleading: while death, passage of time, and emancipation all cause the contract to become binding, their effect differs depending on who holds the option. Death nullifies the option of the deceased entirely, and the option is not inherited (except for khiyar al-'ayb and khiyar al-ta'yin, which are established anew for the heir). The commentator explains the rationale: khiyar al-shart is merely a matter of will and desire, which cannot be transferred by inheritance. He distinguishes from khiyar al-'ayb, where the right to a sound item passes to the heir. The text then discusses various scenarios: the death of the agent vs. principal, the effect of declaring the buyer's option (even if the seller dies), and the inheritance of different types of khiyar. A dispute is noted regarding khiyar al-ru'yah: some sources claim it is inherited, but the majority of Hanafi authorities, including the author of Kanz, maintain it is not. The passage also covers actions that constitute acceptance or revocation of the option, such as explicit words like 'I ratify' versus mere expressions of desire, and physical acts like cupping or shaving the slave's head. The commentator critiques the author's omission of ratification by explicit statement and act, noting that the author's mention of emancipation serves to indicate ratification by act. Overall, this lesson provides a detailed analysis of the conditions under which an option is terminated and whether it transfers to heirs, with special attention to the various types of khiyar in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Key Terms
خيار العيب (khiyār al-'ayb): The option to return a defective item; it is established for the heir as a new right because the decedent deserved a sound item.
خيار التعيين (khiyār al-ta'yīn): The option to specify which of several items to take; it is established for the heir as a new right due to intermingled ownership.
خيار الرؤية (khiyār al-ru'yah): The option to confirm or rescind a sale after seeing the item; the author states it is not inherited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of khiyar al-ru'yah upon the death of the buyer?
A) It is inherited by the heirs.
B) It is not inherited; the contract becomes binding.
C) It is established as a new right for the heir.
D) It is suspended indefinitely.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-‘ayb and khiyar al-ta‘yīn give heirs a new right, while khiyar al-ru’yah is not inherited; the majority Hanafi view is definitive.

Khiyar al-Shart: Non-Transferability on Death and Guardian's Role
Explains khiyar not transferring on death with intra-Hanafi dispute on guardian-minor case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the non-transferability of khiyar al-shart upon death and apply the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in the guardian-minor scenario.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart is a personal right that dies with its holder — it never transfers to heirs or representatives.

This lesson examines a fundamental principle in Hanafi contract law: khiyar al-shart (option of condition) is a personal right that extinguishes upon the death of the holder. The source text from Jami' al-Fusulayn and al-Mi'raj establishes that the sale becomes binding if the option-holder dies. It also presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding a guardian who stipulates khiyar for himself when buying for a minor: does the option continue when the minor reaches majority? We will analyze the ruling and the underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
What happens to khiyar al-shart upon death of the holder? The text states that in all cases of death (agent, guardian, principal, minor, etc.) the sale becomes binding. Khiyar is a personal right that does not transfer.
Insanity is analogized to death as it removes legal capacity.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Consider the scenario: a guardian buys for a minor with khiyar for himself, and the minor attains majority during the option period. Abu Yusuf says sale becomes binding immediately; Muhammad says it is suspended pending ratification. Understand the basis for each view.
Abu Yusuf emphasizes the personal nature of khiyar; Muhammad emphasizes the guardian's protective role.
3
Determine the relied-upon view
The text explicitly states that the mu'tamad is Abu Yusuf's view. The option does not transfer. The sale is binding upon majority.
This is the position for fatwa.
4
Note the exception for the licensed slave
The case of a licensed slave (ma'dhun) who sells with khiyar is excepted: the master may ratify but cannot rescind unless the option was stipulated for himself. This exception reinforces the general rule.
This is not a transfer of khiyar, but a separate right of the master.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جامع الفصولين وكيل البيع أو الوصي باع بخيار أو المالك بنفسه باع بخيار لغيره فمات الوكيل أو الوصي أو الموكل أو الصبي أو من باع بنفسه أو من شرط له الخيار قال محمد : البيع في كل ذلك لأن لكل منهم حقاً في الخيار والجنون كالموت اهـ. وفي المعراج : ولو كان الخيار لهما فمات أحدهما لزم البيع من جهته والآخر على خياره .اهـ. وقد أفاد كلامه أن الخيار لا ينتقل عمن هو له إلى غيره فلذا قال أبو يوسف : إذا اشترى الأب أو الوصي شيئاً لليتيم وشرط الخيار لنفسه فبلغ الصبي في المدة تم البيع. وقال محمد توقف على إجازة الابن فكأنه باشره بعد بلوغه حتى قيل لا تتأقت بالثلاث وعن محمد أن للوصي أن يفسخ بعد بلوغ الصغير وليس له أن يجيز إلا برضاه. وروي أن الأب أو الوصي إذا اشترى عبداً للصغير بدراهم أو دنانير بشرط الخيار ثم بلغ الصغير في المدة ثم أجاز أنفذ الشراء عليهما إلا أن تكون الإجازة برضا الصغير بعد البلوغ فينفذ عليه. ولو حجر السيد على عبده المأذون تم البيع، وقيل ينتقل الخيار إلى المولى. ولو اشترى المكاتب أو باع بشرط الخيار ثم عجز في الثلاث تم البيع عندهم؛ كذا في الظهيرية. فقد علم أن الخيار لا ينتقل على المعتمد لأن قول أبي يوسف في الأولى هو المعتمد ولكن خرج عنه العبد المأذون إذا باع بشرط الخيار فإن للمولى الإجازة إن لم يكن مديوناً ولا يجوز فسخه عليه إلا أن يجعله لنفسه ثم يفسخ بحضرة المشتري أو بما يكون فسخاً من الأفعال في غيبة المشتري؛ كذا في الظهيرية.
From Jami' al-Fusulayn: If an agent for sale or a guardian sold with an option, or the owner himself sold with an option for another, and then the agent, guardian, principal, minor, or the one who sold himself or the one for whom the option was stipulated died, Muhammad said: The sale is binding in all these cases because each of them has a right to the option, and insanity is like death. In al-Mi'raj: If the option belonged to both and one of them died, the sale becomes binding from his side, and the other retains his option. His statement indicates that the option does not transfer from the one who has it to another. Hence Abu Yusuf said: If a father or guardian bought something for an orphan and stipulated the option for himself, and the minor attained majority during the term, the sale is binding. Muhammad said: It is suspended upon the son's ratification, as if he had personally conducted it after puberty, so it is said it is not limited to three [days]. And from Muhammad: The guardian may rescind after the minor reaches majority, but he may not ratify except with his consent. It is narrated that if the father or guardian bought a slave for the minor with dirhams or dinars with the option, then the minor attained majority during the term, then ratified, the purchase is executed upon both, unless the ratification was with the minor's consent after puberty, then it is binding upon him. If the master placed a restriction on his licensed slave, the sale is binding; and it is said the option transfers to the master. If a mukatab bought or sold with an option then became incapable within the three [days], the sale is binding according to them; as in al-Zahiriyyah. Thus it is known that the option does not transfer according to the relied-upon view, because the statement of Abu Yusuf in the first case is the relied-upon view. However, the case of the licensed slave when he sells with an option is excepted: the master may ratify if he is not indebted, and the master cannot rescind his sale unless he makes the option for himself and then rescinds in the presence of the buyer, or by actions that constitute rescission in the absence of the buyer; as in al-Zahiriyyah.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage from Jami' al-Fusulayn addresses the effect of death, insanity, and majority on khiyar al-shart (option of condition). The core principle established is that khiyar is a personal right that does not transfer to heirs or representatives upon death. Muhammad ibn al-Hasan states that if any party holding the option dies, the sale becomes binding because their right to the option was personal and terminates with them. Insanity is analogized to death as it removes legal capacity. The text then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a guardian who stipulates khiyar for himself when buying for a minor. Abu Yusuf holds that if the minor attains majority during the option period, the sale becomes binding automatically; the guardian's option does not continue. Muhammad holds that the sale remains suspended pending the now-adult's ratification, suggesting the option effectively transfers to the minor. The relied-upon position (mu'tamad) is that of Abu Yusuf: the option does not transfer. However, an exception is made for a licensed slave (ma'dhun): if he sells with khiyar, the master may ratify the sale, but cannot rescind it unless he stipulates the option for himself. The passage also clarifies that a mukatab's sale with khiyar becomes binding if he fails to pay installments within three days. The overall ruling confirms that khiyar is non-transferable, with the exception of the master's right to ratify in the case of a licensed slave.

Key Terms
خيار (khiyar): Option or choice given to a party in a contract, here specifically khiyar al-shart (option of condition) stipulated in the sale.
إجازة (ijazah): Ratification or approval of a contract, making it binding. In the context, the minor's or master's acceptance of the sale.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or cancellation of the sale, exercising the option to annul the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A guardian buys a property for an orphan with khiyar al-shart stipulated for himself. The orphan reaches puberty during the option period. What is the ruling according to the relied-upon view (mu'tamad) in the Hanafi school?
A) The sale becomes binding immediately; the orphan cannot rescind.
B) The sale remains suspended until the orphan, now an adult, ratifies it.
C) The guardian retains the option to rescind or confirm.
D) The option transfers to the orphan automatically.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart is a personal right that does not transfer upon death or change of authority; the sale becomes binding, except for specific cases like the licensed slave where the master may ratify.

The Principle of Ijazah: Ownership-Specific Acts Void Khiyar
Establishes the general rule distinguishing ownership-specific acts from permissible non-ownership acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that only acts exclusively dependent on ownership (like emancipation, sale, consumption) constitute acceptance (ijazah) and void khiyar al-shart, and distinguish them from permissible non-ownership acts (like employment, riding once).

Core Idea
An act that is only valid in ownership voids the option; an act permissible without ownership does not.

In khiyar al-shart, the option holder must not treat the subject matter as his own until the option period ends. The Hanafi school has a precise criterion: any action that is legally permissible only for the owner (like freeing a slave or selling the item) constitutes acceptance and nullifies the option. In contrast, actions that a non-owner could also perform (like employing a servant or riding a horse once) do not void the option. This lesson establishes the foundational rule and its basis in the reasoning of the Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the option holder and the act
Determine who has the option (buyer or seller) and what specific action was performed on the subject matter of the sale.
Only the option holder's actions matter; the other party's actions do not affect the option.
2
Classify the act as ownership-specific or not
Ask: Is this act legally permissible only for the owner? Examples: freeing, selling, consuming, gifting with delivery. If yes, it is ijazah. If the act is permissible for a non-owner (e.g., employing, riding without damaging), it is not ijazah.
The act must be something that would be invalid if done by a non-owner.
3
Check for repetition or intention
Some acts are borderline: using the item once (e.g., wearing a garment once) does not void, but doing it twice indicates ownership intent and voids.
Repetition is a sign of ownership; the default rule for non-ownership acts is that a single use is acceptable.
4
Apply the rule to the case at hand
Once you determine the nature of the act, conclude whether the option is voided or remains. If voided, the sale becomes binding immediately.
If the act is ambiguous, refer to the detailed examples in the text.

Source Text

بمشط أو دهن أو لبس ولو اشترى أرضاً مع حرثه فسقى الحرث أو فعل منه شيئاً أو حصده أو عرض المبيع للبيع بطل خياره لا لو عرضه ليقوم ومشتري الدار لو أسكنه بأجر أو بلا أجر أو رم منه شيئاً أو بني أو جصص أو طين والدنانير. ولو باع جارية بعبد على أنه بالخيار في الجارية فهبة العبد أو عرضه على البيع إجازة وعرضها على البنج ) قال في التتارخانية : حتى لو طال السكر لم يكن له أن يتصرف بحكم الخيار : هكذا حكي عن الشيخ أحمد الطواويسي والصحيح أنه يبطل قوله : (ولو ارتد فعلى خياره إجماعاً) قال في التتارخانية : وإن ارتد إن عاد إلى الإسلام في المدة فهو على خياره إجماعاً، وإن مات أو قتل على الردة يبطل خياره إجماعاً وإن تصرف بحكم الخيار الخ. قوله : (وليس منه ما إذا قبض الثمن من البائع) كذا في عامة النسخ ، وفي نسخة من المشتري وهو الظاهر لكن الذي رأيته في المعراج ما في عامة النسخ ذكره بعد مسائل تصرفات البائع وهذا يشير إلى أن البائع فاعل القبض. وعليه فقوله «من البائع صفة لمصدر محذوف لا صلة «قبض» ويقرأ «قُبض بالبناء للمجهول و«الثمن» نائب الفاعل قوله : (وعرضها على البيع ليس بفسخ على الأصح مخالف لما قدمه قريباً في قوله «أو عرض المبيع
The term: As for the agent if he is dismissed while having the option, it is not invalidated by consensus; as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. As for the lapse [of the option period], it nullifies the option, whether it is for the seller or buyer, because the option is only established within it, so it does not remain after it, like the option given to a woman in a fixed time. As for emancipation and its consequences — tadbir and kitabah — they are executed [as ratification] if the option belongs to the buyer and he does them; but if the option belongs to the seller and he does them, it is a rescission. The author mentioned nullification by necessity: death and lapse of the period, and nullification by indication: emancipation. He did not mention what constitutes acceptance by explicit statement nor what constitutes acceptance by action. As for the first: in Jami' al-Fusulayn: The buyer with an option, if he says 'I have ratified its purchase' or 'I wanted to take it' or 'I am pleased to take it', his option is void. If he says 'I desired to take it' or 'I loved it' or 'I intended it' or 'I admired it' or 'it pleases me', it does not void. In it: If the buyer demands rent from the resident, his option is void. If he calls a slave-girl to his bed, it does not void, whether the option is for the seller or buyer. As for the second: In it, if he cupped a slave, or gave him medicine, or shaved his head, it is consent; not if he ordered [someone else to do so]. Similarly, the term is not inherited. But what he mentioned about khiyar al-ru'yah being inherited contradicts what the author stated here and differs from what is in al-Ghurar, al-Wiqayah, al-Muntaqa, Mukhtasar al-Niqayah, and Islah al-Wiqayah by Ibn Kamal Pasha. It is clearly stated in al-Hidayah and al-Fath in the chapter of khiyar al-ru'yah, so know that this correction is strange. His statement: (and not what constitutes acceptance by action) was ruled in al-Nahr to be an oversight, because he alluded to it by his statement 'and emancipation'. His statement: (different from intoxication from... a woman with a comb, oil, or clothing. If he bought land with its crop and watered the crop, or did something from it, or harvested it, or offered the sold item for sale, his option is void; not if he offered it for valuation. The buyer of a house, if he houses someone in it with or without rent, or repaired something from it, or built, plastered, mudded, or demolished something from it, it is consent. If he ground in the mill to know its grinding capacity, if he ground more than a day and night, his option is void; not for less. If he trimmed the hoofs of the animal or cut from its mane, it is not consent. If he cut its jugular vein or bled it, it is consent. Al-Tawdij is slitting the jugular veins completely. If he employed the servant once, or wore the garment once, or rode the animal once, his option is not void. If he did it twice, it is void. If he bought a slave-girl with an option and saw her cupping people for payment and remained silent, it is consent; not if without payment, because it is like employing. Do you not see that if he said to him 'cup me' and he cupped him, it is not consent. He bought a female slave and ordered her to breastfeed his child, it is not consent because it is employment. If he rode an animal to water it or to return it to the seller, his option is void by qiyas, not by istihsan. Then he said: He bought a cow with an option and milked it; Abu Hanifa said: His option is void. Abu Yusuf said: Not until he drinks the milk or destroys it. The commentator said: Every action that is not permissible except in ownership is acceptance, like intercourse and kissing; not that which is permissible without it, like employment. Al-Mi'raj added to what we mentioned: unconsciousness of the one who has the option; if he regains consciousness within the term, he has the option. Al-Asbajabi mentioned the sound opinion is that he retains his option. The verification is that unconsciousness and insanity do not void; rather, what voids is the lapse of the term without choice. Hence if he regains consciousness and rescinds within it, it is valid. If he becomes intoxicated from wine, his option is not void, unlike intoxication from banj. If he apostatizes, he retains his option by consensus; if he acts by virtue of his option, it is suspended according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. He was absolute in emancipation, so it includes if he suspended it on a condition and it occurred within the term, as in al-Mi'raj. By emancipation he indicated every action that is not done except in ownership, such as if he sold it, gifted it with delivery, mortgaged it, or leased it, even if he did not deliver it, according to the sound opinion as in al-Mi'raj. It does not include if he received the price from the seller, similarly gifting it and spending it, unless he borrowed it for something else like dirhams and dinars. If he sold a slave-girl for a slave with the stipulation that he has the option regarding the slave-girl, then gifting the slave or offering him for sale is acceptance, and offering her for... (end)
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a comprehensive discussion of what actions nullify or confirm khiyar al-shart. It begins by establishing that the option period is strictly fixed: once it expires, the sale becomes binding regardless of the party's consent. This is likened to the fixed waiting period for a woman given a choice. The commentator then outlines the author's classification of causes that nullify khiyar: by necessity (death, lapse of time) and by implication (emancipation of a slave). He notes that the author omitted explicit verbal acceptance and actions that imply acceptance, which are then detailed. For verbal acceptance, only unequivocal words like 'ratified' or 'agreed' void the option; expressions of desire or inclination do not. For actions, the key principle is that any act that is only permissible if one owns the item (e.g., selling, gifting, freeing, using in a way that consumes or alters it) constitutes acceptance and voids the option. Acts that are permissible even without ownership (e.g., employing a slave, riding a horse without consuming it) do not void the option unless done repeatedly (twice) or with the intent of consumption. The text provides numerous examples: cupping a slave for payment if silent is consent; demanding rent from a tenant voids the option; milking a cow voids it according to Abu Hanifa but not Abu Yusuf unless the milk is consumed. It also discusses unusual states: unconsciousness, insanity, intoxication (from wine does not void, from banj does), and apostasy (option remains unless death occurs in apostasy). The passage ends with technical commentary on variant readings of the matn regarding who received the price, and a note that offering the sold item for valuation (not for sale) does not void the option. The overall rule is clear: the khiyar holder cannot treat the item as his own without losing the option, unless the act is one permissible for a non-owner.

Key Terms
إعتاق (i'taq): Freeing a slave; it is considered an act that constitutes acceptance (ijazah) when done by the buyer during the option period, because it is only permissible in ownership.
استخدام (istikhdam): Employing or using a slave/servant for service; it is permissible even for a non-owner (e.g., a borrower or hiree), so it does not void the option unless done repeatedly or with payment demanded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer purchases a cow with khiyar al-shart for three days. During the first day, he milks the cow but does not drink or discard the milk. According to Abu Hanifa, what is the effect?
A) The option is void because milking is an act of ownership.
B) The option remains until the milk is consumed.
C) The option remains because milking does not consume the cow.
D) The option is void only if the buyer drinks the milk.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule for khiyar al-shart: any act that is legally permissible only for the owner constitutes acceptance and voids the option; acts permissible without ownership do not.

Verbal and Tacit Acceptance: Explicit Words and Repeated Actions
Lists specific verbal and action-based examples of ijazah from authoritative Hanafi sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which verbal statements and physical actions during the option period ratify or cancel the sale, and apply the Hanafi rules for when a single vs repeated use constitutes acceptance.

Core Idea
Unequivocal acceptance words void the option; ambiguous words do not. Actions that are not ownership-specific void only if done twice.

In addition to the general principle, the Hanafi school provides detailed guidance on specific verbal and tacit expressions of acceptance. This lesson delves into the text's examples of explicit statements (from Jami' al-Fusulayn) and physical actions like cupping, shaving, wearing, and riding. Understanding these specifics is crucial for accurately determining when the option is voided.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish explicit from equivocal words
Words like 'I ratified its purchase' or 'I am pleased to take it' are clear acceptance; words like 'I desired it' or 'I liked it' are not.
The test is whether the words indicate a firm commitment to the sale.
2
Identify actions that are permissible for non-owners
These include single uses like wearing a garment once, riding a horse once, or employing a servant once. They do not void the option.
The rationale is that such uses could be done by a borrower or hirer.
3
Apply the 'twice' rule for borderline actions
If the same non-ownership act is done twice (e.g., wearing the garment twice, riding twice), it indicates ownership intent and voids the option.
The key is repetition, not the act itself.
4
Evaluate actions that imply ownership indirectly
Examples: offering the item for sale (voids), but offering for valuation does not. Silent acceptance of benefit (e.g., seeing a slave cupping for pay) is consent.
The context and intent matter.

المدة وأما الوكيل إذا عزل وله الخيار فإنه لا يبطل اتفاقاً؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج. وأما مضي فمبطل للخيار، سواء كان للبائع أو للمشتري إذ لم يثبت الخيار إلا فيها فلا بقاء له بعدها كالمخيرة في وقت مقدر وأما الإعتاق وتوابعه وهي التدبير والكتابة فإنما يتم به إذا كان الخيار للمشتري وفعلها، أما إذا كان للبائع وفعلها كان فسخاً. وذكر المصنف السقوط بطريق الضرورة وهو الموت ومضي المدة والسقوط بطريق الدلالة وهو الإعتاق، ولم يذكر ما يكون إجازة بالقول صريحاً ولا ما يكون إجازة بالفعل أما الأول ففي جامع الفصولين : المشتري بالخيار إذا قال أجزت شراءه أو شئت أخذه أو رضيت أخذه بطل خياره، ولو قال هويت أخذه أو أحببت أو أردت أو أعجبني أو وافقني لا يبطل .اهـ. وفيه: لو طلب المشتري الأجر جر من الساكن بطل خياره، ولو دعا الجارية إلى فراشه لا يبطل سواء كان الخيار للبائع أو للمشتري. وأما الثاني ففيه لو حجم العبد أو سقاه دواء أو حلق رأسه كان رضا لا لو أمر وكذا الأجل لا يورث اهـ . لكن ما ذكره من أن خيار الرؤية يورث خلاف ما ذكره المؤلف هنا و خلاف ما في الغرر والوقاية والمنتقى ومختصر النقاية وإصلاح الوقاية لابن كمال، وبه صرح في الهداية والفتح من باب خيار الرؤية علم أن هذا التصحيح غريب قوله : (ولا ما يكون إجازة بالفعل) حكم عليه في النهر بأنه سهو لأنه نبه عليها بقوله والإعتاق». قوله : (بخلاف السكر من امرأة بمشط أو دهن أو لبس ولو اشترى أرضاً مع حرثه فسقى الحرث أو فعل منه شيئاً أو حصده أو عرض المبيع للبيع بطل خياره لا لو عرضه ليقوم ومشتري الدار لو أسكنه بأجر أو بلا أجر أو رم منه شيئاً أو بني أو جصص أو طين أو هدم منه شيئاً فهو رضا. ولو طحن في الرحا ليعرف قدر طحنه إن طحن أكثر من يوم وليلة بطل خياره لا فيما دونه. ولو قص حوافر الدابة أو أخذ من عرفها لم يكن رضا، ولو ودجها أو بزغها فهو رضا. والتوديج شق الأوداج جملة. ولو استخدم الخادم مرة أو لبس الثوب مرة أو ركب الدابة مرة لم يبطل خياره، ولو فعله مرتين بطل ولو شرى قناً بخيار فرآه يحجم الناس بأجر فسكت كان رضاً لا لو بلا أجر لأنه كالاستخدام ألا ترى أنه لو قال له احجمني فحجمه لم يكن رضا. شرى أمة فأمرها بإرضاع ولده لم يكن رضا لأنه استخدام ولو ركب دابة ليسقيها أو ليردها على البائع بطل خياره قياساً لا استحساناً اهـ. ثم قال : شرى بقرة بخيار فحلبها قال أبو حنيفة : بطل خياره. وقال أبو يوسف : لا حتى يشرب اللبن أو يتلفه اهـ. وذكر الشارح أن كل تصرف لا يحل إلا في الملك فإنه اجازة كالوطء والتقبيل لا ما يحل في غيره كالاستخدام. وزاد في المعراج على ما ذكرناه إغماء من له الخيار، ولو أفاق في المدة فله الخيار. وذكر الاسبيجابي الأصح أنه على خياره والتحقيق أن الإغماء والجنون لا يسقطان إنما المسقط له مضي المدة من غير اختيار، ولذا لو أفاق فيها وفسخ جاز، ولو سكر من الخمر لا يبطل بخلاف السكر من البنج ، ولو ارتد فعلى خياره اجماعاً فلو تصرف بحكم خياره توقف عنده خلافاً لهما .اهـ. وأطلق في الإعتاق فشمل ما إذا علقه بشرط فوحد في المدة كما في المعراج وأشار بالإعتاق إلى كل تصرف لا يفعل إلا في الملك كما إذا باعه أو وهبه وسلمه أو رهن أو آجر وإن لم يسلم على الأصح كما في المعراج. وليس منه ما إذا قبض الثمن من البائع وكذا هبته وانفاقه إلا إذا استدانه لغيره كالدراهم والدنانير. ولو باع جارية بعبد على أنه بالخيار في الجارية فهبة العبد أو عرضه على البيع إجازة وعرضها على البنج ) قال في التتارخانية : حتى لو طال السكر لم يكن له أن يتصرف بحكم الخيار : هكذا حكي عن الشيخ أحمد الطواويسي والصحيح أنه يبطل قوله : (ولو ارتد فعلى خياره إجماعاً) قال في التتارخانية : وإن ارتد إن عاد إلى الإسلام في المدة فهو على خياره إجماعاً، وإن مات أو قتل على الردة يبطل خياره إجماعاً وإن تصرف بحكم الخيار الخ. قوله : (وليس منه ما إذا قبض الثمن من البائع) كذا في عامة النسخ ، وفي نسخة من المشتري وهو الظاهر لكن الذي رأيته في المعراج ما في عامة النسخ ذكره بعد مسائل تصرفات البائع وهذا يشير إلى أن البائع فاعل القبض. وعليه فقوله «من البائع صفة لمصدر محذوف لا صلة «قبض» ويقرأ «قُبض بالبناء للمجهول و«الثمن» نائب الفاعل قوله : (وعرضها على البيع ليس بفسخ على الأصح مخالف لما قدمه قريباً في قوله «أو عرض المبيع
The term: As for the agent if he is dismissed while having the option, it is not invalidated by consensus; as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. As for the lapse [of the option period], it nullifies the option, whether it is for the seller or buyer, because the option is only established within it, so it does not remain after it, like the option given to a woman in a fixed time. As for emancipation and its consequences — tadbir and kitabah — they are executed [as ratification] if the option belongs to the buyer and he does them; but if the option belongs to the seller and he does them, it is a rescission. The author mentioned nullification by necessity: death and lapse of the period, and nullification by indication: emancipation. He did not mention what constitutes acceptance by explicit statement nor what constitutes acceptance by action. As for the first: in Jami' al-Fusulayn: The buyer with an option, if he says 'I have ratified its purchase' or 'I wanted to take it' or 'I am pleased to take it', his option is void. If he says 'I desired to take it' or 'I loved it' or 'I intended it' or 'I admired it' or 'it pleases me', it does not void. In it: If the buyer demands rent from the resident, his option is void. If he calls a slave-girl to his bed, it does not void, whether the option is for the seller or buyer. As for the second: In it, if he cupped a slave, or gave him medicine, or shaved his head, it is consent; not if he ordered [someone else to do so]. Similarly, the term is not inherited. But what he mentioned about khiyar al-ru'yah being inherited contradicts what the author stated here and differs from what is in al-Ghurar, al-Wiqayah, al-Muntaqa, Mukhtasar al-Niqayah, and Islah al-Wiqayah by Ibn Kamal Pasha. It is clearly stated in al-Hidayah and al-Fath in the chapter of khiyar al-ru'yah, so know that this correction is strange. His statement: (and not what constitutes acceptance by action) was ruled in al-Nahr to be an oversight, because he alluded to it by his statement 'and emancipation'. His statement: (different from intoxication from... a woman with a comb, oil, or clothing. If he bought land with its crop and watered the crop, or did something from it, or harvested it, or offered the sold item for sale, his option is void; not if he offered it for valuation. The buyer of a house, if he houses someone in it with or without rent, or repaired something from it, or built, plastered, mudded, or demolished something from it, it is consent. If he ground in the mill to know its grinding capacity, if he ground more than a day and night, his option is void; not for less. If he trimmed the hoofs of the animal or cut from its mane, it is not consent. If he cut its jugular vein or bled it, it is consent. Al-Tawdij is slitting the jugular veins completely. If he employed the servant once, or wore the garment once, or rode the animal once, his option is not void. If he did it twice, it is void. If he bought a slave-girl with an option and saw her cupping people for payment and remained silent, it is consent; not if without payment, because it is like employing. Do you not see that if he said to him 'cup me' and he cupped him, it is not consent. He bought a female slave and ordered her to breastfeed his child, it is not consent because it is employment. If he rode an animal to water it or to return it to the seller, his option is void by qiyas, not by istihsan. Then he said: He bought a cow with an option and milked it; Abu Hanifa said: His option is void. Abu Yusuf said: Not until he drinks the milk or destroys it. The commentator said: Every action that is not permissible except in ownership is acceptance, like intercourse and kissing; not that which is permissible without it, like employment. Al-Mi'raj added to what we mentioned: unconsciousness of the one who has the option; if he regains consciousness within the term, he has the option. Al-Asbajabi mentioned the sound opinion is that he retains his option. The verification is that unconsciousness and insanity do not void; rather, what voids is the lapse of the term without choice. Hence if he regains consciousness and rescinds within it, it is valid. If he becomes intoxicated from wine, his option is not void, unlike intoxication from banj. If he apostatizes, he retains his option by consensus; if he acts by virtue of his option, it is suspended according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. He was absolute in emancipation, so it includes if he suspended it on a condition and it occurred within the term, as in al-Mi'raj. By emancipation he indicated every action that is not done except in ownership, such as if he sold it, gifted it with delivery, mortgaged it, or leased it, even if he did not deliver it, according to the sound opinion as in al-Mi'raj. It does not include if he received the price from the seller, similarly gifting it and spending it, unless he borrowed it for something else like dirhams and dinars. If he sold a slave-girl for a slave with the stipulation that he has the option regarding the slave-girl, then gifting the slave or offering him for sale is acceptance, and offering her for... (end)
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a comprehensive discussion of what actions nullify or confirm khiyar al-shart. It begins by establishing that the option period is strictly fixed: once it expires, the sale becomes binding regardless of the party's consent. This is likened to the fixed waiting period for a woman given a choice. The commentator then outlines the author's classification of causes that nullify khiyar: by necessity (death, lapse of time) and by implication (emancipation of a slave). He notes that the author omitted explicit verbal acceptance and actions that imply acceptance, which are then detailed. For verbal acceptance, only unequivocal words like 'ratified' or 'agreed' void the option; expressions of desire or inclination do not. For actions, the key principle is that any act that is only permissible if one owns the item (e.g., selling, gifting, freeing, using in a way that consumes or alters it) constitutes acceptance and voids the option. Acts that are permissible even without ownership (e.g., employing a slave, riding a horse without consuming it) do not void the option unless done repeatedly (twice) or with the intent of consumption. The text provides numerous examples: cupping a slave for payment if silent is consent; demanding rent from a tenant voids the option; milking a cow voids it according to Abu Hanifa but not Abu Yusuf unless the milk is consumed. It also discusses unusual states: unconsciousness, insanity, intoxication (from wine does not void, from banj does), and apostasy (option remains unless death occurs in apostasy). The passage ends with technical commentary on variant readings of the matn regarding who received the price, and a note that offering the sold item for valuation (not for sale) does not void the option. The overall rule is clear: the khiyar holder cannot treat the item as his own without losing the option, unless the act is one permissible for a non-owner.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijazah): Ratification of the sale by the option holder through explicit words or actions that imply ownership, thereby voiding the option and confirming the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer with an option on a garment wears it once and then says 'I loved it'. According to the passage, what is the status of the option?
A) Voided because wearing it once is use.
B) Voided because 'I loved it' is acceptance.
C) Not voided because wearing once does not void and 'I loved it' is equivocal.
D) Not voided unless he wears it twice.

Key Takeaway
Explicit words like 'I ratified' void the option; ambiguous words do not. A single non-ownership act does not void, but repeating it twice does.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf: Milking, Apostasy, and Unusual States
Presents two intra-Hanafi disputes: milking a cow and apostasy during khiyar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreements between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on milking a cow and between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on apostasy, and state the mufta bihi position for each.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa voids the option immediately on milking; Abu Yusuf waits for consumption. On apostasy, Abu Hanifa suspends actions; the Sahibayn consider them effective.

Within the Hanafi school, there are notable disagreements on specific applications of the ijazah rule. This lesson examines two key disputes: the effect of milking a cow during the option period, and the validity of actions during khiyar if the option holder apostatizes. Understanding these ikhtilafat sharpens your ability to identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed case and the positions
For milking: Abu Hanifa says option voids immediately upon milking; Abu Yusuf says it remains until the milk is consumed or destroyed. For apostasy: Abu Hanifa says actions done during khiyar are suspended; the Sahibayn say they are effective.
Both disputes are about timing and finality of acceptance.
2
Analyze the underlying reasoning
Abu Hanifa sees milking as an ownership benefit (taking milk) that is immediate; Abu Yusuf views the milk as still not fully appropriated until consumption. For apostasy, Abu Hanifa sees the option holder's legal capacity as compromised; the Sahibayn see the act itself as valid regardless of faith state.
The reasoning reflects different interpretations of the illa (effective cause).
3
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The text indicates that for milking, Abu Hanifa's view is the relied-upon (since it is mentioned first and the commentator confirms). For apostasy, the view of Abu Hanifa (suspended) is also the standard Hanafi position, as indicated by 'at his (Abu Hanifa's) view it is suspended, contrary to the two (Sahibayn)'.
Consult later Hanafi fatwa works for confirmation.

إلى أن البائع فاعل القبض. وعليه فقوله «من البائع صفة لمصدر محذوف لا صلة «قبض» ويقرأ «قُبض بالبناء للمجهول و«الثمن» نائب الفاعل قوله : (وعرضها على البيع ليس بفسخ على الأصح مخالف لما قدمه قريباً في قوله «أو عرض المبيع
The term: As for the agent if he is dismissed while having the option, it is not invalidated by consensus; as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. As for the lapse [of the option period], it nullifies the option, whether it is for the seller or buyer, because the option is only established within it, so it does not remain after it, like the option given to a woman in a fixed time. As for emancipation and its consequences — tadbir and kitabah — they are executed [as ratification] if the option belongs to the buyer and he does them; but if the option belongs to the seller and he does them, it is a rescission. The author mentioned nullification by necessity: death and lapse of the period, and nullification by indication: emancipation. He did not mention what constitutes acceptance by explicit statement nor what constitutes acceptance by action. As for the first: in Jami' al-Fusulayn: The buyer with an option, if he says 'I have ratified its purchase' or 'I wanted to take it' or 'I am pleased to take it', his option is void. If he says 'I desired to take it' or 'I loved it' or 'I intended it' or 'I admired it' or 'it pleases me', it does not void. In it: If the buyer demands rent from the resident, his option is void. If he calls a slave-girl to his bed, it does not void, whether the option is for the seller or buyer. As for the second: In it, if he cupped a slave, or gave him medicine, or shaved his head, it is consent; not if he ordered [someone else to do so]. Similarly, the term is not inherited. But what he mentioned about khiyar al-ru'yah being inherited contradicts what the author stated here and differs from what is in al-Ghurar, al-Wiqayah, al-Muntaqa, Mukhtasar al-Niqayah, and Islah al-Wiqayah by Ibn Kamal Pasha. It is clearly stated in al-Hidayah and al-Fath in the chapter of khiyar al-ru'yah, so know that this correction is strange. His statement: (and not what constitutes acceptance by action) was ruled in al-Nahr to be an oversight, because he alluded to it by his statement 'and emancipation'. His statement: (different from intoxication from... a woman with a comb, oil, or clothing. If he bought land with its crop and watered the crop, or did something from it, or harvested it, or offered the sold item for sale, his option is void; not if he offered it for valuation. The buyer of a house, if he houses someone in it with or without rent, or repaired something from it, or built, plastered, mudded, or demolished something from it, it is consent. If he ground in the mill to know its grinding capacity, if he ground more than a day and night, his option is void; not for less. If he trimmed the hoofs of the animal or cut from its mane, it is not consent. If he cut its jugular vein or bled it, it is consent. Al-Tawdij is slitting the jugular veins completely. If he employed the servant once, or wore the garment once, or rode the animal once, his option is not void. If he did it twice, it is void. If he bought a slave-girl with an option and saw her cupping people for payment and remained silent, it is consent; not if without payment, because it is like employing. Do you not see that if he said to him 'cup me' and he cupped him, it is not consent. He bought a female slave and ordered her to breastfeed his child, it is not consent because it is employment. If he rode an animal to water it or to return it to the seller, his option is void by qiyas, not by istihsan. Then he said: He bought a cow with an option and milked it; Abu Hanifa said: His option is void. Abu Yusuf said: Not until he drinks the milk or destroys it. The commentator said: Every action that is not permissible except in ownership is acceptance, like intercourse and kissing; not that which is permissible without it, like employment. Al-Mi'raj added to what we mentioned: unconsciousness of the one who has the option; if he regains consciousness within the term, he has the option. Al-Asbajabi mentioned the sound opinion is that he retains his option. The verification is that unconsciousness and insanity do not void; rather, what voids is the lapse of the term without choice. Hence if he regains consciousness and rescinds within it, it is valid. If he becomes intoxicated from wine, his option is not void, unlike intoxication from banj. If he apostatizes, he retains his option by consensus; if he acts by virtue of his option, it is suspended according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. He was absolute in emancipation, so it includes if he suspended it on a condition and it occurred within the term, as in al-Mi'raj. By emancipation he indicated every action that is not done except in ownership, such as if he sold it, gifted it with delivery, mortgaged it, or leased it, even if he did not deliver it, according to the sound opinion as in al-Mi'raj. It does not include if he received the price from the seller, similarly gifting it and spending it, unless he borrowed it for something else like dirhams and dinars. If he sold a slave-girl for a slave with the stipulation that he has the option regarding the slave-girl, then gifting the slave or offering him for sale is acceptance, and offering her for... (end)
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a comprehensive discussion of what actions nullify or confirm khiyar al-shart. It begins by establishing that the option period is strictly fixed: once it expires, the sale becomes binding regardless of the party's consent. This is likened to the fixed waiting period for a woman given a choice. The commentator then outlines the author's classification of causes that nullify khiyar: by necessity (death, lapse of time) and by implication (emancipation of a slave). He notes that the author omitted explicit verbal acceptance and actions that imply acceptance, which are then detailed. For verbal acceptance, only unequivocal words like 'ratified' or 'agreed' void the option; expressions of desire or inclination do not. For actions, the key principle is that any act that is only permissible if one owns the item (e.g., selling, gifting, freeing, using in a way that consumes or alters it) constitutes acceptance and voids the option. Acts that are permissible even without ownership (e.g., employing a slave, riding a horse without consuming it) do not void the option unless done repeatedly (twice) or with the intent of consumption. The text provides numerous examples: cupping a slave for payment if silent is consent; demanding rent from a tenant voids the option; milking a cow voids it according to Abu Hanifa but not Abu Yusuf unless the milk is consumed. It also discusses unusual states: unconsciousness, insanity, intoxication (from wine does not void, from banj does), and apostasy (option remains unless death occurs in apostasy). The passage ends with technical commentary on variant readings of the matn regarding who received the price, and a note that offering the sold item for valuation (not for sale) does not void the option. The overall rule is clear: the khiyar holder cannot treat the item as his own without losing the option, unless the act is one permissible for a non-owner.

Key Terms
توقف (tawaquf): Suspension of the legal effect of an action pending a future condition. Here, the apostate's actions under khiyar are suspended until he returns to Islam or dies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer with a 3-day option on a cow milks it but does not use the milk. He then apostatizes. According to Abu Hanifa, what is the status of the sale?
A) The option is voided by milking, so the sale is confirmed immediately.
B) The option is suspended until he returns to Islam.
C) The option remains until the milk is consumed.
D) The option is voided only if he also drinks the milk.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, intra-school disputes are resolved by identifying the mufta bihi: on milking, Abu Hanifa's immediate nullification prevails; on apostasy, the option is suspended.
