Actions That Void the Option of Stipulation
Listing actions that void the option of stipulation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which actions by a buyer constitute acceptance (rida) and void the option of stipulation, and distinguish between single and repeated use.

Core Idea
Using the purchased item in a way exclusive to ownership voids the option; mere testing does not.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi rulings on when a buyer's actions during the option period are considered acceptance (rida). The key principle is that any act that is only permissible after ownership – such as using the item beyond inspection, building, or deriving benefit – indicates consent and renders the sale binding. We will explore specific scenarios from the text and the intra-Hanafi dispute on milking.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of action
Determine if the action is 'testing' (single use, inspection) or 'ownership-like' (full usage, disposal). Only actions that only an owner can perform void the option.
For example, cutting the hooves is merely grooming, not ownership-like; slaughtering is ownership-like.
2
Apply the general principle
Any action that only an owner can do (e.g., slaughtering, building, selling) voids the option. Actions that a mere custodian could do (e.g., touching, light use) do not.
Offering for valuation is not a sale, so it does not void.
3
Check for repetition
Single use of a servant, garment, or animal does NOT void; repeating the same act twice voids because it indicates continuous benefit.
One ride is testing; two rides is using.
4
Note exceptions based on benefit to the buyer
If the buyer receives direct benefit (e.g., hiring out the slave for a fee), it voids. If no direct benefit (e.g., slave cupping for free), it does not void because it is like mere use.
Silence when seeing the slave earn a fee implies acceptance.
5
Understand the milking dispute
Abu Hanifa held that milking alone voids the option because it is a usufruct exclusive to ownership. Abu Yusuf held that the option remains until the milk is consumed or destroyed.
This is a legitimate intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب خيار الشرط . امرأة بمشط أو دهن أو لبس ولو اشترى أرضاً مع حرثه فسقى الحرث أو فعل منه شيئاً أو حصده أو عرض المبيع للبيع بطل خياره لا لو عرضه ليقوم ومشتري الدار لو أسكنه بأجر أو بلا أجر أو رم منه شيئاً أو بني أو جصص أو طين أو هدم منه شيئاً فهو رضا. ولو طحن في الرحا ليعرف قدر طحنه إن طحن أكثر من يوم وليلة بطل خياره لا فيما دونه. ولو قص حوافر الدابة أو أخذ من عرفها لم يكن رضا، ولو ودجها أو بزغها فهو رضا. والتوديج شق الأوداج جملة. ولو استخدم الخادم مرة أو لبس الثوب مرة أو ركب الدابة مرة لم يبطل خياره، ولو فعله مرتين بطل ولو شرى قناً بخيار فرآه يحجم الناس بأجر فسكت كان رضاً لا لو بلا أجر لأنه كالاستخدام ألا ترى أنه لو قال له احجمني فحجمه لم يكن رضا. شرى أمة فأمرها بإرضاع ولده لم يكن رضاً لأنه استخدام ولو ركب دابة ليسقيها أو ليردها على البائع بطل خياره قياساً لا استحساناً اهـ. ثم قال : شرى بقرة بخيار فحلبها قال أبو حنيفة : بطل خياره. وقال أبو يوسف : لا حتى يشرب اللبن أو يتلفه اهـ.
Book of Sale, Chapter of Option of Stipulation. [If a woman] buys a comb or oil or clothing... and if he buys land with its cultivation and waters the cultivation or does something from it or harvests it or offers the sold item for sale, his option becomes void, but not if he offers it for valuation. And the buyer of a house if he makes someone live in it with or without rent, or repairs something from it, or builds, or plasters, or muddies, or demolishes something from it, it is acceptance. And if he grinds in a mill to know the amount of its grinding, if he grinds more than a day and night his option becomes void, not less than that. And if he cuts the hooves of the animal or takes from its forelock, it is not acceptance; and if he slits its jugular veins or bleeds it, it is acceptance. And [the meaning of] al-tawdij is cutting the jugular veins entirely. And if he employs the servant once, or wears the garment once, or rides the animal once, his option does not become void; if he does it twice, it becomes void. And if he buys a slave with an option and sees him cupping people for a fee and remains silent, it is acceptance; if [the slave does it] without a fee, it is not, because it is like employing. Do you not see that if he says to him 'cup me' and he cups him, it is not acceptance. [If] he buys a female slave and orders her to breastfeed his child, it is not acceptance because it is employing. And if he rides an animal to water it or to return it to the seller, his option becomes void by qiyas, not by istihsan. Then he said: [If] he buys a cow with an option and milks it, Abu Hanifa said: His option becomes void. Abu Yusuf said: No, until he drinks the milk or destroys it.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings from the Hanafi school regarding actions by the buyer that constitute acceptance (رضا) and thereby void the option of stipulation (خيار الشرط). The opening phrase 'امرأة بمشط' appears to be a continuation from the previous page, likely referring to a woman purchasing items like a comb or oil. The rulings progress through various scenarios: if the buyer cultivates the land, builds, or offers the item for sale (except for valuation), the option is void. Similarly, using the property (grinding, cutting hair/healing) or possessing it in a way that goes beyond mere inspection voids the option. The key principle is that any action that is only permissible after ownership (such as slaughtering, employing, or incurring harm) constitutes acceptance. The passage also distinguishes between one-time use (does not void) and repeated use (voids). Notable is the case of a buyer who sees the slave cupping people for a fee: if he remains silent while the slave receives payment, it is acceptance; if the slave does it for free, it is not, as it resembles mere use. The milking case involves an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that milking alone voids the option, while Abu Yusuf requires the milk to be consumed or destroyed. The text concludes with the remark that the ruling on riding to water or return is by qiyas (analogy) not istihsan (preference), indicating a departure from the preferred view in some contexts.

Key Terms
رضا (rida): Acceptance of the sale by the buyer through actions that indicate consent, thereby voiding the option.
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in a sale contract allowing one or both parties to cancel within a specified period.
قياس (qiyas): Legal analogy used to derive a ruling for a new case from an existing case sharing the same effective cause.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas in specific cases for practical or equitable reasons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer rides a horse once to test it, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The option becomes void immediately.
B) The option remains valid.
C) The sale is automatically cancelled.
D) The buyer must pay the price at once.

Key Takeaway
Acceptance (rida) is determined by actions exclusive to ownership, not by mere testing or single use.

The Principle of Ownership-Restricted Actions in Khiyar al-Shart
Stating the legal principle and its exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that only actions exclusive to ownership constitute acceptance (ijazah) during the option period, and apply it to exceptional cases such as unconsciousness, intoxication, and apostasy.

Core Idea
Only ownership-exclusive actions void the option; other permissible actions do not.

In the Hanafi school, the option period (khiyar al-shart) allows a party to confirm or rescind a sale. But what counts as 'acceptance' that makes the sale binding? This lesson explores the decisive principle: only acts that are legally permissible only after ownership constitute acceptance. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands this principle with key exceptions and an intra-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the General Rule
Identify the core statement: any action that is only lawful in ownership (e.g., sexual intercourse, slaughtering) is acceptance. Actions lawful without ownership (e.g., employment, riding for test) are not acceptance.
This is based on the idea that such actions imply dominion over the object.
2
Examine the Exceptions
The passage adds cases: unconsciousness, insanity, intoxication, and apostasy. The principle holds that only complete lack of choice ends the option. Unconsciousness and insanity do not by themselves void the option; rather the passing of the period without choice does.
Intoxication from wine vs. bhang: the distinction likely based on the degree of intoxication impact on reason.
3
Analyze the Apostasy Dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that the apostate's action during the option is suspended; the two disciples (Sahibayn) hold it takes effect immediately. Understand the different legal capacity assumptions.
This affects practical scenarios of apostasy and subsequent return.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر الشارح أن كل تصرف لا يحل إلا في الملك فإنه اجازة كالوطء والتقبيل لا ما يحل في غيره كالاستخدام. وزاد في المعراج على ما ذكرناه إغماء من له الخيار، ولو أفاق في المدة فله الخيار. وذكر الاسبيجابي الأصح أنه على خياره والتحقيق أن الإغماء والجنون لا يسقطان إنما المسقط له مضي المدة من غير اختيار، ولذا لو أفاق فيها وفسخ جاز، ولو سكر من الخمر لا يبطل بخلاف السكر من البنج ، ولو ارتد فعلى خياره اجماعاً فلو تصرف بحكم خياره توقف عنده خلافاً لهما .اهـ.
And the commentator mentioned that every action that is not lawful except in ownership is acceptance, like intercourse and kissing; not what is lawful in other than it, like employment. And he added in al-Mi'raj to what we mentioned: unconsciousness of the one who has the option; if he regains consciousness during the period, he has the option. And al-Isbijabi mentioned the most correct [view] that he is on his option; and the verified [position] is that unconsciousness and insanity do not drop it; rather what drops it is the passing of the period without choice. Hence if he regains consciousness during it and revokes [the sale], it is valid. And if he becomes intoxicated from wine, it does not become void, unlike intoxication from bhang (hashish). And if he apostatizes, he is on his option by consensus. Then if he acts by virtue of his option, it is suspended according to him (Abu Hanifa?), contrary to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad].
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the general principle underlying the rulings on khiyar al-shart: any action that is only permissible after ownership (e.g., sexual intercourse, slaughter, selling) constitutes acceptance (ijazah) and voids the option. In contrast, actions that are permissible even without ownership, such as employing a slave or riding an animal for testing, do not constitute acceptance. The commentary then addresses exceptional cases: fainting or insanity during the option period does not invalidate the option unless the entire period passes without conscious choice. Intoxication from wine does not void the option, but intoxication from hashish (bhang) does, likely because the latter is considered more severe in Islamic law. Apostasy (riddah) does not affect the option by consensus, but any action taken by the apostate during the period is suspended until his return to Islam, according to Abu Hanifa, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the action takes effect immediately.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijazah): Acceptance of the sale that makes the contract binding; occurs through actions exclusive to ownership.
إغماء (ighma'): Unconsciousness; it does not void the option unless it covers the entire period without consciousness.
بنج (banj): A psychoactive substance (hashish bhang); intoxication from it voids the option, unlike from wine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The buyer retains the option.
B) The option is lost because the period passed without choice.
C) The sale is automatically void.
D) The buyer must pay the price regardless.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle for khiyar al-shart: only actions that are only lawful in ownership constitute acceptance and bind the sale; exceptions involve loss of conscious choice or legal capacity.

Acts of Ownership that Void the Option
Explaining acts that void the option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify acts of ownership that void the option of stipulation and explain the exception for receiving the price from the seller.

Core Idea
Emancipation, selling, or any ownership-exclusive act during the option period constitutes acceptance and voids the option.

This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the principle that any act that can only be done by an owner (like freeing a slave or selling the item) voids the option of stipulation. However, receiving the price from the seller does not void it, unless the buyer borrows the price for others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule
State the general rule: any act exclusive to ownership (e.g., emancipation, sale, gift, pawn, lease) done by the buyer during the option period constitutes acceptance and voids the option.
The rule is derived from the principle that such acts indicate final consent.
2
List Ownership Acts
List the acts mentioned: emancipation (i'taq), sale, gift with delivery, pawn, lease (even without delivery according to the most correct view).
Delivery not required for lease; the most correct view is that the act itself voids the option.
3
Note the Exception
Understand that receiving the price from the seller does not void the option, nor does gifting or spending the price, unless the buyer borrows it for others (like dirhams and dinars).
Borrowing for personal use is not acceptance; borrowing for third parties indicates finality.
4
Understand the Borrowing Distinction
Distinguish between borrowing for oneself and borrowing for others. The latter is considered acceptance.
The text specifies 'if he borrows it for others' as an exception that voids the option.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلق في الإعتاق فشمل ما إذا علقه بشرط فوحد في المدة كما في المعراج وأشار بالإعتاق إلى كل تصرف لا يفعل إلا في الملك كما إذا باعه أو وهبه وسلمه أو رهن أو آجر وإن لم يسلم على الأصح كما في المعراج. وليس منه ما إذا قبض الثمن من البائع وكذا هبته وانفاقه إلا إذا استدانه لغيره كالدراهم والدنانير. ولو باع جارية بعبد على أنه بالخيار في الجارية فهبة العبد أو عرضه على البيع إجازة وعرضها على البنج ) قال في التتارخانية : حتى لو طال السكر لم يكن له أن يتصرف بحكم الخيار : هكذا حكي عن الشيخ أحمد الطواويسي والصحيح أنه يبطل قوله : (ولو ارتد فعلى خياره إجماعاً) قال في التتارخانية : وإن ارتد إن عاد إلى الإسلام في المدة فهو على خياره إجماعاً، وإن مات أو قتل على الردة يبطل خياره إجماعاً وإن تصرف بحكم الخيار الخ. قوله : (وليس منه ما إذا قبض الثمن من البائع) كذا في عامة النسخ ، وفي نسخة من المشتري وهو الظاهر لكن الذي رأيته في المعراج ما في عامة النسخ ذكره بعد مسائل تصرفات البائع وهذا يشير إلى أن البائع فاعل القبض. وعليه فقوله «من البائع صفة لمصدر محذوف لا صلة «قبض» ويقرأ «قُبض بالبناء للمجهول و«الثمن» نائب الفاعل قوله : (وعرضها على البيع ليس بفسخ على الأصح مخالف لما قدمه قريباً في قوله «أو عرض المبيع البائع ليس بفسخ على الأصح ولو أبرأه من الثمن أو اشترى منه به شيئاً أو ساومه به فهو إجازة؛ كذا في المعراج . وقيد الاستخدام ثانياً من المشتري بأن لا يكون في نوع آخر والركوب امتحاناً ليس إجازة لا ثانياً كركوبها لحاجة أو شغل أو حمل عليها إلا علفها عند محمد، والركوب للرد والسقي والإعلاف إجازة، ولو نسخ من الكتاب لنفسه أو لغيره لا يبطل، وإن قلب الأوراق وبالدرس منه يبطل، وقيل على عكسه وبه أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث اهـ. وفي الظهيرية : لو سقى من نهرها أرضاً له أخرى سقط وكرى النهر وكبس البئر يسقط خياره، ولو انهدمت البئر ثم بناها لم يعد خياره، ولو وقعت فيها فأرة أو نجاسة سقط وروي أنه إذا نزح عشرين دلواً لم يسقط .اهـ. وفي السراج الوهاج : إذا زوج العبد أو الأمة سقط خياره. وفي المحيط : باع عبداً بخيار له فأذن له في التجارة لم يكن نقضاً إلا أن يلحقه دين، ولو أمضاه بعدما لحقه دين لم يجز لأن الغريم أحق به من المشتري.
And he made the emancipation general, including if he suspends it on a condition and it occurs within the period, as in al-Mi'raj. And by emancipation he indicates every action that is done only in ownership, such as if he sells it, gifts it, delivers it, pawns it, or leases it, even if he does not deliver it according to the most correct [view], as in al-Mi'raj. And not from it is if he receives the price from the seller, and likewise his gift and spending, unless he borrows it for others like dirhams and dinars. And if he buys a slave-girl with a slave on the condition that he has the option in the slave-girl, then gifting the slave or offering him for sale is acceptance; and offering her [the slave-girl] for [؟]... [bhang?] He said in al-Tatarkhaniyya: even if the intoxication lasts long, he may not act by virtue of the option; thus it is narrated from Sheikh Ahmad al-Tawawisi, and the correct [view] is that it becomes void. His statement: 'And if he apostatizes, he is on his option by consensus.' He said in al-Tatarkhaniyya: If he apostatizes and returns to Islam within the period, he is on his option by consensus; if he dies or is killed on apostasy, his option becomes void by consensus. And if he acts by virtue of the option... etc. His statement: 'And not from it is when he receives the price from the seller.' Thus in most copies, and in one copy 'from the buyer' and that is apparent, but what I saw in al-Mi'raj is what is in most copies, and he mentioned it after matters of the seller's acts. This indicates that the seller is the one who takes the receipt. Accordingly, his phrase 'from the seller' is an attribute of an omitted verbal noun, not a connection of 'receipt'; and it is read as 'qubida' in the passive voice, with 'al-thaman' as the agent. His statement: 'And offering her for sale is not a rescission according to the most correct [view], contrary to what he mentioned recently in his statement 'or offering the sold item for sale; [for] the seller, offering for sale is not a rescission according to the most correct [view]. And if he releases him from the price, or buys something from him with it, or bargains with him about it, it is acceptance; thus in al-Mi'raj. And he restricted employment, secondarily from the buyer, by not being in another type; and riding for testing is not acceptance, not secondarily, like riding it for need or work or carrying [something] on it, except feeding it according to Muhammad. And riding for return, watering, and feeding is acceptance. And if he copies from the book for himself or others, it does not become void; and if he turns the pages and studies from it, it becomes void; and it is said the opposite, and al-Faqih Abu al-Layth adopted this. And in al-Zahiriyya: If he waters from its river another land of his, it drops [the option]; and digging the river and cupping the well drop his option; and if the well collapses and he rebuilds it, his option does not return; and if a mouse or impurity falls into it, it drops; and it is narrated that if he draws twenty buckets, it does not drop. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If he marries off the male slave or female slave, his option drops. And in al-Muhit: [If] he sells a slave with an option and gives him permission to trade, it is not a rescission, unless debt attaches to him; and if he ratifies it after debt attaches, it is not valid because the creditor has more right to him than the buyer.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This extensive passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq continues the discussion on actions that void the option of stipulation. It begins by stating that emancipating the slave (or any action that can only be done after ownership, like selling, gifting, leasing) constitutes acceptance and voids the option. However, receiving the price from the seller is not acceptance, nor is gifting or spending the price, unless the buyer borrows it on credit. The passage then delves into various scenarios: if the buyer buys a slave-girl with another slave conditionally, gifting the slave or offering him for sale is acceptance. There is a debate about intoxication (hashish) and its effect on actions during the option. The text also addresses the buyer copying from a book, turning pages, or studying: the first does not void the option, the second does (with an opposite view quoted). Irrigation, digging wells, and cleaning wells are discussed: once the buyer uses the water or repairs the well, the option drops, but if the well collapses after repair, the option does not return. Marrying off the slave voids the option. Giving the slave permission to trade does not void unless debt is incurred. The passage cites multiple sources: al-Mi'raj, al-Tatarkhaniyya, al-Zahiriyya, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and al-Muhit, showing the depth of the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
إعتاق (i'taq): Emancipation of a slave; it is an act exclusive to ownership and thus voids the option.
إجازة (ijazah): Acceptance that makes the sale binding; here used for acts that indicate final consent.
أبرأه من الثمن (abara'ahu min al-thaman): To release the seller from the price; this is considered acceptance of the sale.
استدان (istadana): To borrow; if the buyer borrows the price from a third party, that does not void the option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following acts by a buyer with an option of stipulation will void the option?
A) Receiving the price from the seller.
B) Gifting the price to a friend.
C) Emancipating the purchased slave.
D) Borrowing the price from a bank for personal use.

Key Takeaway
Any act that can only be done by an owner, performed by the buyer during the option period, voids the option; simple receipt of the price does not.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Specific Acts and Their Effect on the Option
Detailing various actions and their effect on the option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the effect of specific actions (such as riding, studying, irrigating, and marrying off a slave) on the option of stipulation and identify intra-Hanafi differences.

Core Idea
Not all uses of the item void the option; only those indicating final acceptance or ownership-exclusive acts drop the option.

This lesson continues the detailed discussion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, examining specific scenarios: offering an item for sale, releasing the seller from the price, riding for test vs. need, copying and studying a book, irrigating land, maintaining a well, and marrying off a slave. Each action is analyzed, and some have differing opinions among Hanafi authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify Acceptance Acts
List actions that clearly indicate acceptance: releasing the seller from the price, buying something from the seller with the same price, bargaining with the price (all considered acceptance).
Also, offering for sale is acceptance according to the correct view.
2
Distinguish Test from Benefit
For riding an animal: riding to test (no acceptance); riding for a need, work, or carrying something is acceptance (unless feeding, which is not acceptance according to Muhammad).
Riding for return, watering, and feeding is acceptance.
3
Analyze Book Actions
Copying from a book does not void the option; turning pages and studying does (with an opposite view attributed to al-Faqih Abu al-Layth).
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: some say studying does not void.
4
Evaluate Land and Well Changes
Watering another land from the irrigation ditch of the purchased land voids the option; digging the river or cupping the well voids it; if the well collapses and is rebuilt, option does not return; if a mouse or impurity falls into the well, option drops (but drawing twenty buckets may not).
These are considered beneficial uses indicating acceptance.
5
Apply Marriage and Trade Rules
Marrying off a male or female slave voids the option. Giving the slave permission to trade does not void unless debt attaches to the slave; if debt attaches, ratification of the permission is invalid because creditors have priority.
Trade permission is not an ownership act per se, but debt changes the situation.

According to the passage, what is the ruling if a buyer with an option waters another land from the irrigation ditch of the purchased land?

Defects and Increases During the Option Period
Effect of defects and increases on the option period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the effect of defects and categories of increases on the option to rescind a sale, including the intra-Hanafi differences.

Core Idea
An attached or generated increase prevents rescission; a separate non-generated increase does not, unless the buyer accepts.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq expands on the original matn by addressing what happens when the sold item changes during the option period. It distinguishes between defects that void the option, and four categories of increases that either bind the sale or leave it open. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for determining whether a buyer can still return the item.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers defects (nuqsan) and increases (ziyada) in the sold item during the option period. Separate these clearly before proceeding.
Defects and increases have different rules.
2
Analyze defects
Determine who holds the option (buyer or seller) and who caused the defect. For buyer's option: if defect occurs, option becomes void (sale binding) according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; however, Muhammad disagrees if the seller caused it. For seller's option: buyer can choose to take or reject the defective item. If seller caused defect, sale is rescinded.
The buyer recovers arsh (compensation) for defects according to the two.
3
Classify increases into four types
Increases are categorized by being attached vs. separate, and generated vs. non-generated. Memorize the four types from Jami' al-Fusulayn: attached generated, attached non-generated, separate generated, separate non-generated.
Examples: fatness (attached generated), dyeing (attached non-generated), milk (separate generated), profit (separate non-generated).
4
Apply the ruling to each type
For attached generated: prevents return, sale binding, except according to Muhammad. For attached non-generated: prevents return by consensus. For separate generated: prevents return by consensus. For separate non-generated: does not prevent return; buyer may accept or return; Abu Hanifa says the increase is returned with the item.
Intra-Hanafi differences exist on attached generated and on separate non-generated.
5
Note additional cases
The passage mentions a hen laying an egg (separate generated) – option drops. Also actions like gifting or offering for sale by the seller may affect the option, with differing opinions.
These cases illustrate the application of the categories.

ولم يذكر المصنف هنا حكم ما إذا زاد المبيع أو نقص في المدة وذكر فيما قبله حكم ما إذا تعيب. أما الثاني ففي المعراج ولو حدث به عيب في خيار المشتري بطل خياره، سواء حدث بفعل البائع أو بغير فعله، لكونه في ضمان المشتري حيث كان في يده عندهما. وقال محمد: لا يلزمه العقد بجناية البائع. وعلى قولهما يرجع المشتري بالأرش على البائع، ولو كان الخيار للبائع فحدث به عيب فهو على خياره لكنه يتخير المشتري، ولو حدث بفعل البائع انتقض البيع لأن ما انتقص مضمون عليه ؛ كذا في المعراج وقدمناه وأما الأول أعني الزيادة ففي جامع الفصولين: شرى بخيار فزاد المبيع في يد المشتري زيادة متصلة متولدة كسمن وجمال وبرء وانجلاء بياض عن العين يمنع الرد ويلزم البيع إلا عند محمد، وإن كانت متصلة لم تتولد كصبغ وخياطة ولت سويق بسمن وثني أرض وغرس شجر يمنع الفسخ وفاقاً. ولو كانت منفصلة متولدة كعقر وولد وأرش ولبن وثمر وصوف تمنع ،وفاقاً، وإن كانت منفصلة لم تتولد كغلة وكسب وهبة وصدقة لا يمنع وفاقاً، فإن أجاز المشتري فهو له وإلا فكذلك عندهما، وعند أبي حنيفة ترد على البائع .اهـ. وفي السراج : إذا باضت الدجاجة في المدة سقط الخيار للبيع بطل خياره وقد ذكر مسألة الجارية هذه في التتارخانية وذكر أن هبة العبد الذي اشتراه بها أو عرضه على البيع امضاء للبيع ثم قال بعض صفحة : وإذا كان الخيار للبائع فعرض المبيع على البيع ذكر شمس الأئمة الحلواني إن كان بمحضر من صاحبه ينفسخ البيع، وإن كان بغير محضر من صاحبه لا ينفسخ البيع، وبعض مشايخنا قالوا العرض على البيع من البائع ليس بفسخ على كل حال وإليه مال الإمام أحمد الطواويسي. وذكر شيخ الإسلام في شرحه أن فيه روايتين. وفي المنتقى عن محمد: البائع إذا عرض المبيع على البيع لا يبطل خياره. قوله: (ولو وهب العبد أم ولد المشتري) هنا سقط فيما رأيناه من النسخ والذي رأيته في
And the author did not mention here the ruling on if the sold item increases or decreases during the period, and he mentioned previously the ruling on if it becomes defective. As for the second [i.e., defects], in al-Mi'raj: If a defect occurs during the buyer's option, his option becomes void, whether it occurs by the seller's act or not, because it is in the buyer's guarantee while it is in his hand according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. And Muhammad said: The contract does not become binding due to the seller's trespass. And according to the two, the buyer recovers the reduction in price from the seller. And if the option is for the seller and a defect occurs, he is on his option but the buyer has a choice; and if it occurs by the seller's act, the sale is rescinded because what is decreased is guaranteed by him. Thus in al-Mi'raj and we preceded it. And as for the first, i.e., increase, in Jami' al-Fusulayn: [If] he buys with an option and the sold item increases in the buyer's hand with an attached generated increase like fatness, beauty, recovery, and clearing of whiteness from the eye, it prevents return and makes the sale binding, except according to Muhammad. And if [the increase] is attached but not generated, like dyeing, sewing, mixing saliq with clarified butter, tilling land, and planting trees, it prevents rescission by agreement. And if it is separate generated increase like hire, offspring, diyah [blood money], milk, fruit, and wool, it prevents [rescission] by agreement. And if it is separate not generated like profit, earning, gift, and charity, it does not prevent by agreement. If the buyer accepts, it is his; otherwise, it is likewise according to the two; and according to Abu Hanifa, it is returned to the seller. And in al-Siraj: If a hen lays an egg during the period, the option drops; for the sale, the option becomes void. And he mentioned this matter about the slave-girl in al-Tatarkhaniyya and mentioned that gifting the slave he bought with her or offering him for sale is ratification of the sale. Then a certain page said: And if the option is for the seller and he offers the sold item for sale, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said if it is in the presence of his partner [the buyer], the sale is rescinded; if not, it is not rescinded. And some of our shaykhs said offering for sale by the seller is not a rescission under any circumstance, and Imam Ahmad al-Tawawisi inclined to this. And Shaykh al-Islam mentioned in his commentary that there are two narrations. And in al-Muntaqa from Muhammad: The seller, if he offers the sold item for sale, his option does not become void. His statement: 'And if he gifts the slave, the mother of the buyer's child' here is missing in the copies we saw, and what I saw in...
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This final lesson addresses the effect of defects and increases on the sold item during the option period. The author notes that the original text (matn) did not cover these, but the commentary does. The first part discusses defects: if a defect occurs while the buyer has the option, his option is voided (sale becomes binding) because the item is in his guarantee, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Muhammad disagrees if the defect is caused by the seller. If the option belongs to the seller, he retains the option but the buyer can choose to take the defective item or cancel. Then the passage discusses increases, citing Jami' al-Fusulayn. It categorizes increases into four types: (1) attached generated (e.g., fattening) – prevents return and binds the sale, except according to Muhammad; (2) attached non-generated (e.g., dyeing) – prevents return by consensus; (3) separate generated (e.g., offspring, milk) – prevents return by consensus; (4) separate non-generated (e.g., profit, gift) – does not prevent return. However, if the buyer accepts, he keeps the increase. Abu Hanifa holds that the increase is returned to the seller. The text then mentions a specific case: if a hen lays an egg during the option period, the option drops. It ends with a note on the seller offering the item for sale, citing various opinions: Shams al-A'imma distinguishes whether the buyer is present; some shaykhs hold it is never a rescission. The passage concludes with a note that a portion is missing in the copies regarding gifting a slave who is the mother of the buyer's child.

Key Terms
زيادة متصلة متولدة (ziyadatan muttasilatan mutawallidatan): An increase physically attached to the item and naturally generated from it (e.g., fatness, growth).
زيادة منفصلة متولدة (ziyadatan munfasilatan mutawallidatan): A separate increase generated from the item (e.g., milk, fruit, hire).
أرش (arsh): Compensation paid by the seller to the buyer for a defect in the sold item, proportional to the reduction in value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a buyer with an option purchases a cow and the cow gives birth to a calf during the option period, what is the ruling?
A) The buyer can return both the cow and the calf.
B) The buyer must keep the cow and calf; the return is prevented.
C) The buyer can return the cow but keep the calf.
D) The buyer can return only the calf.

Key Takeaway
The fourfold classification of increases (attached/separate × generated/non-generated) is essential for determining the effect on the option to rescind a sale.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Actions That Constitute Acceptance (Ijaza) and Annul Khiyar al-Shart
Actions that annul khiyar al-shart

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which actions by the seller or buyer constitute acceptance (ijaza) and annul the option, and distinguish them from actions that do not annul.

Core Idea
Not every use of the object annuls the option; only actions that indicate final consent count as ijaza.

In khiyar al-shart, the party with the option may accept or annul. However, certain actions by either party can be interpreted as implicit acceptance, ending the option. Hanafi jurists have delineated these actions, distinguishing between those that clearly indicate finality and those that are exploratory or incidental.

Guided Path
1
Identify the party and action
First, determine whether the action was performed by the seller or the buyer, and describe the specific act (e.g., acquitting the price, riding the animal, copying a book).
The ruling may differ depending on the party.
2
Judge the nature of the action
Is the action purely for testing or examination, or does it imply acceptance of the sale? Actions that dispose of the item's benefit or value usually indicate acceptance.
For example, riding for a test is not acceptance, but riding to water the animal is.
3
Apply the precedent rulings
Match the action against the specific examples given in the text (e.g., acquitting price, bargaining, second riding for need, etc.) to see if it is listed as annulling or not.
The text provides many examples; use them as a reference.
4
Account for intra-Hanafi differences
Note any differences among the Hanafi imams (e.g., Muhammad differs on fodder for riding). Determine the mufta bihi.
The relied-upon view is generally the majority.

الدجاجة في المدة سقط الخيار إلا أن تكون مذرة، وإذا ولدت الحيوان ولداً سقط إلا أن يكون الولد ميتاً اهـ. والحاصل أنها مانعة مطلقاً إلا منفصلة لم تتولد وفي الظهيرية عن الثاني : اشترى عبداً بخيار ثلاثاً المشتري بشرط الخيار بالشفعة لأنه لا يكون إلا بالملك فكان دليل الإجازة فتضمن سقوط الخيار، وقدمنا الاعتذار لأبي حنيفة عنه عند قوله ولا يملك المشتري ولو قال المؤلف وطلب الشفعة بها بدل الأخذ لكان أولى لأن أو نقض صح) لأن شرط الخيار لغيره جائز استحساناً لا قياساً وهو قول زفر لأنه من مواجب العقد فلا يجوز اشتراطه لغيره كاشتراط الثمن على غير المشتري. ولنا أن الخيار لغير العاقد لا يثبت إلا نيابة عن العاقد فيقدم الخيار له اقتضاء ثم يجعل هو نائباً عنه تصحيحاً لتصرفه، وحينئذ يكون لكل منهما الخيار فأيهما أجاز جاز وأيهما نقض انتقض . ولو قال المصنف ولو شرط أحد المتعاقدين الخيار الأجنبي صح لكان أولى ليشمل ما إذا كان الشارط البائع أو المشتري، وليخرج اشتراط أحدهما للآخر فإن قوله لغيره» صادق بالبائع وليس بمراد ولذا قال في المعراج : والمراد من الغير هنا غير العاقدين ليتأتى فيه خلاف زفر قيد بخيار الشرط لأن خيار العيب والرؤية لا يثبت لغير العاقدين كما في المعراج وأفاد كلامه أن أحدهما لو أجاز فقال الآخر لا أرضى فالبيع لازم. ولو أمر وكيله بالبيع بشرط الخيار فباعه بلا شرط لم يجز، ولو باع واشترط كما أمره فليس له أن يجيز على الآمر وللآمر الإجازة، ولو وكله بشراء بشرط للآمر فاشترى ولم يشترطه نفذ عليه ؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج قوله : (فإن أجاز أحدهما ونقض الآخر فالاسبق أحق) لوجوده في زمان لا يزاحمه فيه غيره. التتارخانية : ولو وهب للعبد ابن المشتري وقبض العبد عين الابن لا يبطل خيار المشتري في العبد ولو وهب للعبد أم ولد المشتري الخ. قوله : (والأخير يحتاج إلى تحرير) المراد بالأخير مسألة هبة أم ولد المشتري للعبد واحتياجها إلى التحرير من جهة أنها إذا كانت أم ولده كيف تكون في ملك غيره حتى يهبها للعبد، ومن جهته أنها كيف تبقى على ملكه بعد الرد.
Book of Sales, Chapter of Option of Condition. The seller does not [nullify] by [merely] nullifying according to the most correct [view]. If he acquits him of the price or buys something from him with it or bargains with him about it, that is acceptance; thus in al-Mi'raj. And the restriction of using [the item] a second time by the buyer is that it not be in another type, and riding as a test is not acceptance, [but] a second time like riding for a need or work or loading upon it, except its fodder according to Muhammad, and riding for return and watering and feeding is acceptance. And if he copies from the book for himself or another, it does not void [the option]. And if he turns the pages and [studies] from it, it voids. And it is said the opposite, and the jurist Abu al-Layth took that. End. In al-Zahiriyya: If he waters from its [the purchased animal's] river another land of his, [the option] lapses; and digging the river and tamping the well causes his option to lapse. And if the well collapses then he rebuilds it, his option does not return. And if a mouse or impurity falls into it, [the option] lapses. And it is narrated that if he draws twenty buckets, it does not lapse. End. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If he marries off the slave or slave-girl, his option lapses. In al-Muhit: He sold a slave with an option for him, then he permitted him to trade; that is not a rescission unless a debt attaches to him. And if he ratifies it after a debt attaches to him, it is not valid because the creditor has more right to it than the buyer. The author did not mention here the ruling when the sold item increases or decreases during the period, and he mentioned before the ruling when it becomes defective. As for the second, in al-Mi'raj: If a defect occurs [to the item] during the buyer's option, his option is voided, whether the defect occurred by the seller's act or not, because it is under the buyer's liability since it was in his hand according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. And Muhammad said: The contract is not binding for the seller's tort. And according to the two, the buyer recourse for the reduction [in price] against the seller. And if the option was for the seller and a defect occurs to it, he retains his option but the buyer has the choice [to annul or take compensation]. And if it occurs by the seller's act, the sale is rescinded because what decreased is guaranteed against him; thus in al-Mi'raj and we have preceded it. As for the first, meaning the increase, in Jami' al-Fusulayn: He bought with an option, then the sold item increases in the buyer's hand by a connected, generated increase like fattening, beauty, recovery, and clearing of whiteness from the eye; that prevents return and makes the sale binding except according to Muhammad. And if it is connected but not generated like dyeing, sewing, mixing roasted flour with fat, plowing land, and planting trees, that prevents rescission by agreement. And if it is separate and generated like offspring, milk, compensation, fruit, and wool, it prevents [rescission] by agreement. And if it is separate and not generated like rent, profit, gift, and charity, it does not prevent [rescission] by agreement. If the buyer accepts, it is his; otherwise, it is the same according to the two, and according to Abu Hanifa it is returned to the seller. End. In al-Siraj: If the hen lays an egg during the period, the option lapses unless it is spoiled [?]. And if the animal gives birth to a young, [the option] lapses unless the young is dead. End. The conclusion: they are preventive absolutely except separate not generated. And in al-Zahiriyya from the second: He bought a slave with a three-day option and took possession, then someone gave the slave property or he earned it, then the slave consumed it with the buyer's knowledge without his permission or without his knowledge; that does not void the buyer's option in the slave. And if the buyer's umm walad is given to the slave and the slave takes possession, the buyer's option in the slave is voided. He said: The child is not like the umm walad because the umm walad remains in his ownership after return by virtue of the option, while the child does not remain. End. The latter needs editing. As for taking by pre-emption, its form is that he buys a house with an option, then another house adjacent to it is sold, and the buyer with the option takes it by pre-emption because it [the right] occurs only through ownership, so it is evidence of acceptance, thus implying the lapse of the option. And we have presented the excuse for Abu Hanifa regarding it at his statement 'the buyer does not own [by pre-emption]', and if the author had said 'and claiming pre-emption through it instead of taking' it would be better because claiming it causes lapse even if he does not take it, as in al-Mi'raj. And it is restricted to the option of condition because claiming does not lapse the option of seeing or defect, as in al-Mi'raj, and the commentator's limitation to the option of seeing is inadequate. His statement: (And if) the buyer stipulates the option for a non-party, it is valid, and whichever of them accepts or annuls is valid. Because stipulating the option for a non-party is permissible by istihsan, not by qiyas, and it is the saying of Zufar, because it is among the requirements of the contract, so stipulating it for another is not allowed like stipulating the price upon a non-buyer. And our proof: The option for a non-contracting party is established only as a deputyship from the contracting party, so the option is given to him by implication, then he is made a deputy for him to validate his action. In that case, each of them has the option, so whichever accepts, it is valid, and whichever annuls, it is annulled. If the author had said 'and if one of the contracting parties stipulates the option for a stranger, it is valid' it would be better to include both seller and buyer as stipulators, and to exclude one stipulating for the other. For his statement 'for a non-party' applies to the seller and that is not intended. Hence it is said in al-Mi'raj: 'By non-party here is meant other than the two contracting parties' to accommodate Zufar's difference. It is restricted to the option of condition because the option of defect and seeing are not established for non-contracting parties, as in al-Mi'raj. His statement indicates that if one of them accepts and the other says 'I am not satisfied', the sale is binding. And if he authorizes his agent to sell with an option and he sells without it, it is not valid. And if he sells and stipulates as ordered, he does not have the right to accept on behalf of the principal, and the principal has the right to accept. And if he authorizes him to buy with a stipulation for the principal, and he buys without stipulating it, it is binding on him; thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. His statement: (If one accepts and the other annuls, then the earlier [action] has more right) because it occurred at a time when no one else was competing with him. In al-Tatar Khaniyya: And if the buyer's son is given to the slave and the slave takes possession of the son's property, the buyer's option in the slave is not voided. And if the buyer's umm walad is given to the slave, etc. His statement: (The latter needs editing) means the issue of gifting the buyer's umm walad to the slave, and its need for editing because if she is his umm walad, how is she in another's ownership so that she is given to the slave? And also how does she remain in his ownership after the return?
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Al-Bahr al-Raiq' on the chapter of Khiyar al-Shart (Option of Condition) from the matn 'Kanz al-Daqaiq'. It covers a wide range of rulings regarding actions that constitute acceptance or nullification of the option, as well as the effects of defects, increases, and other factors on the validity of the option. The commentary begins by stating that certain actions by the seller, such as forgiving the price or buying something with it, clearly indicate acceptance and thus annul the option. However, mere riding for testing does not constitute acceptance, while riding for a purpose like watering or feeding does. Copying a book does not void the option, but turning pages or studying from it does, according to the relied-upon view. The text then discusses various scenarios from other works like al-Zahiriyya, al-Siraj, and al-Muhit, where specific acts such as watering land, marrying off a slave, or permitting trade annul the option. A significant portion is dedicated to the effects of defects and increases during the option period. If a defect occurs in the buyer's possession during his option period, his option is voided according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), because the item is under the buyer's liability. However, Muhammad al-Shaybani has a different view: if the defect occurred by the seller's act, the buyer is not bound. Regarding increases, the ruling depends on the type: connected and generated increases (like fattening) prevent return and make the sale binding, except according to Muhammad; connected but not generated (like dyeing) prevent rescission by consensus; separate and generated (like offspring) also prevent rescission; while separate and not generated (like rent) do not prevent. The commentary then addresses the issue of stipulating the option for a non-contracting party (ghayr al-'aqidayn). The Hanafi position, based on istihsan, is that this is valid, unlike the qiyas of Zufar who disallows it. The text explains that the option is established by deputyship, and each party (the stipulator and the third party) can independently accept or annul. If both act simultaneously, the annulment takes precedence. The passage concludes with a discussion of pre-emption (shuf'a) and how taking by pre-emption during the option period implies acceptance and thus annuls the option. Throughout, the commentary references multiple authoritative sources within the Hanafi school, such as al-Mi'raj, al-Zahiriyya, al-Siraj, and Jami' al-Fusulayn, reflecting the depth of legal analysis typical of later Hanafi works.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): Option of condition: a stipulation allowing a party to decide within a fixed period whether to confirm or annul the sale.
إجازة (ijazah): Acceptance or ratification of the sale, which annuls the option.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following actions by a buyer does NOT annul the option of condition according to the Hanafi school?
A) Riding the animal for watering.
B) Copying a few pages from a book.
C) Using the animal to plow a field.
D) Marrying off a purchased slave.

Key Takeaway
Actions that clearly indicate final consent, such as using the item for profit or disposing of its benefit, annul the option; acts of mere examination do not.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Defects During Khiyar al-Shart: Dispute Between Muhammad and the Sahibayn
Rulings on defects during khiyar al-shart

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between the view of Muhammad and the view of the Sahibayn on the effect of a defect occurring during the buyer's option, and state the practical consequence (thamarah).

Core Idea
When a defect occurs during the buyer's option, his option is voided (Sahibayn) unless the defect was caused by the seller (Muhammad).

What happens if the purchased item is damaged or develops a defect while in the buyer's possession during the option period? The Hanafi school has a nuanced position, with a key ikhtilaf between Muhammad al-Shaybani and the two masters (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). This lesson explores that khilaf and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of option (buyer's or seller's)
First, determine whether the defect occurred during the buyer's option period or the seller's option period.
The ruling differs: if buyer's option, see the dispute; if seller's, see separate ruling.
2
Apply the Sahibayn's position
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), if a defect occurs during the buyer's option, the buyer's option is voided, regardless of the cause, because the item is under the buyer's liability (damān) while in his possession.
The buyer can recover the difference (arsh) from the seller.
3
Apply Muhammad's alternative position
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that if the defect was caused by the seller's act, the buyer is not bound by the contract; the option is not voided.
This is based on the principle that the seller should not benefit from his own tort.
4
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to Sahibayn, the sale stands (with arsh); according to Muhammad, the buyer can annul if seller caused defect.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.

أنه إذا نزح عشرين دلواً لم يسقط .اهـ. وفي السراج الوهاج : إذا زوج العبد أو الأمة سقط خياره. وفي المحيط : باع عبداً بخيار له فأذن له في التجارة لم يكن نقضاً إلا أن يلحقه دين، ولو أمضاه بعدما لحقه دين لم يجز لأن الغريم أحق به من المشتري. ولم يذكر المصنف هنا حكم ما إذا زاد المبيع أو نقص في المدة وذكر فيما قبله حكم ما إذا تعيب. أما الثاني ففي المعراج ولو حدث به عيب في خيار المشتري بطل خياره، سواء حدث بفعل البائع أو بغير فعله، لكونه في ضمان المشتري حيث كان في يده عندهما. وقال محمد: لا يلزمه العقد بجناية البائع. وعلى قولهما يرجع المشتري بالأرش على البائع، ولو كان الخيار للبائع فحدث به عيب فهو على خياره لكنه يتخير المشتري، ولو حدث بفعل البائع انتقض البيع لأن ما انتقص مضمون عليه ؛ كذا في المعراج وقدمناه وأما الأول أعني الزيادة ففي جامع الفصولين: شرى بخيار فزاد المبيع في يد المشتري زيادة متصلة متولدة كسمن وجمال وبرء وانجلاء بياض عن العين يمنع الرد ويلزم البيع إلا عند محمد، وإن كانت متصلة لم تتولد كصبغ وخياطة ولت سويق بسمن وثني أرض وغرس شجر يمنع الفسخ وفاقاً. ولو كانت منفصلة متولدة كعقر وولد وأرش ولبن وثمر وصوف تمنع ،وفاقاً، وإن كانت منفصلة لم تتولد كغلة وكسب وهبة وصدقة لا يمنع وفاقاً، فإن أجاز المشتري فهو له وإلا فكذلك عندهما، وعند أبي حنيفة ترد على البائع .اهـ. وفي السراج : إذا باضت الدجاجة في المدة سقط الخيار إلا أن تكون مذرة، وإذا ولدت الحيوان ولداً سقط إلا أن يكون الولد ميتاً اهـ. والحاصل أنها مانعة مطلقاً إلا منفصلة لم تتولد وفي الظهيرية عن الثاني : اشترى عبداً بخيار ثلاثاً وقبضه فوهب للعبد مال أو اكتسبه ثم استهلكه العبد بعلم المشتري بغير إذنه أو بغير علمه لم يبطل خيار المشتري في العبد. ولو وهب للعبد أم ولد المشتري وقبضها العبد بطل خيار المشتري في العبد قال : ولا يشبه الولد أم الولد من قبل أن أم الولد تبقى على ملكه بعد الرد بحكم الخيار والولد لا يبقى .اهـ. والأخير يحتاج إلى تحرير وأما الأخذ بشفعة فصورته أن يشتري داراً بشرط الخيار ثم تباع دار أخرى بجنبها فيأخذها المشتري بشرط الخيار بالشفعة لأنه لا يكون إلا بالملك فكان دليل الإجازة فتضمن سقوط الخيار، وقدمنا الاعتذار لأبي حنيفة عنه عند قوله ولا يملك المشتري ولو قال المؤلف وطلب الشفعة بها بدل الأخذ لكان أولى لأن طلبها مسقط وإن لم يأخذها كما في المعراج وقيد بخيار الشرط لأن طلبها لا يسقط خيار الرؤية والعيب كما في المعراج واقتصار الشارح على خيار الرؤية قصور . قوله: (ولو) شرط المشتري الخيار لغيره صح وأيهما أجاز أو نقض صح) لأن شرط الخيار لغيره جائز استحساناً لا قياساً وهو قول زفر لأنه من مواجب العقد فلا يجوز اشتراطه لغيره كاشتراط الثمن على غير المشتري. ولنا أن الخيار لغير العاقد لا يثبت إلا نيابة عن العاقد فيقدم الخيار له اقتضاء ثم يجعل هو نائباً عنه تصحيحاً لتصرفه، وحينئذ يكون لكل منهما الخيار فأيهما أجاز جاز وأيهما نقض انتقض . ولو قال المصنف ولو شرط أحد المتعاقدين الخيار الأجنبي صح لكان أولى ليشمل ما إذا كان الشارط البائع أو المشتري، وليخرج اشتراط أحدهما للآخر فإن قوله لغيره» صادق بالبائع وليس بمراد ولذا قال في المعراج : والمراد من الغير هنا غير العاقدين ليتأتى فيه خلاف زفر قيد بخيار الشرط لأن خيار العيب والرؤية لا يثبت لغير العاقدين كما في المعراج وأفاد كلامه أن أحدهما لو أجاز فقال الآخر لا أرضى فالبيع لازم. ولو أمر وكيله بالبيع بشرط الخيار فباعه بلا شرط لم يجز، ولو باع واشترط كما أمره فليس له أن يجيز على الآمر وللآمر الإجازة، ولو وكله بشراء بشرط للآمر فاشترى ولم يشترطه نفذ عليه ؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج قوله : (فإن أجاز أحدهما ونقض الآخر فالاسبق أحق) لوجوده في زمان لا يزاحمه فيه غيره. التتارخانية : ولو وهب للعبد ابن المشتري وقبض العبد عين الابن لا يبطل خيار المشتري في العبد ولو وهب للعبد أم ولد المشتري الخ. قوله : (والأخير يحتاج إلى تحرير) المراد بالأخير مسألة هبة أم ولد المشتري للعبد واحتياجها إلى التحرير من جهة أنها إذا كانت أم ولده كيف تكون في ملك غيره حتى يهبها للعبد، ومن جهته أنها كيف تبقى على ملكه بعد الرد.
Book of Sales, Chapter of Option of Condition. The seller does not [nullify] by [merely] nullifying according to the most correct [view]. If he acquits him of the price or buys something from him with it or bargains with him about it, that is acceptance; thus in al-Mi'raj. And the restriction of using [the item] a second time by the buyer is that it not be in another type, and riding as a test is not acceptance, [but] a second time like riding for a need or work or loading upon it, except its fodder according to Muhammad, and riding for return and watering and feeding is acceptance. And if he copies from the book for himself or another, it does not void [the option]. And if he turns the pages and [studies] from it, it voids. And it is said the opposite, and the jurist Abu al-Layth took that. End. In al-Zahiriyya: If he waters from its [the purchased animal's] river another land of his, [the option] lapses; and digging the river and tamping the well causes his option to lapse. And if the well collapses then he rebuilds it, his option does not return. And if a mouse or impurity falls into it, [the option] lapses. And it is narrated that if he draws twenty buckets, it does not lapse. End. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If he marries off the slave or slave-girl, his option lapses. In al-Muhit: He sold a slave with an option for him, then he permitted him to trade; that is not a rescission unless a debt attaches to him. And if he ratifies it after a debt attaches to him, it is not valid because the creditor has more right to it than the buyer. The author did not mention here the ruling when the sold item increases or decreases during the period, and he mentioned before the ruling when it becomes defective. As for the second, in al-Mi'raj: If a defect occurs [to the item] during the buyer's option, his option is voided, whether the defect occurred by the seller's act or not, because it is under the buyer's liability since it was in his hand according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. And Muhammad said: The contract is not binding for the seller's tort. And according to the two, the buyer recourse for the reduction [in price] against the seller. And if the option was for the seller and a defect occurs to it, he retains his option but the buyer has the choice [to annul or take compensation]. And if it occurs by the seller's act, the sale is rescinded because what decreased is guaranteed against him; thus in al-Mi'raj and we have preceded it. As for the first, meaning the increase, in Jami' al-Fusulayn: He bought with an option, then the sold item increases in the buyer's hand by a connected, generated increase like fattening, beauty, recovery, and clearing of whiteness from the eye; that prevents return and makes the sale binding except according to Muhammad. And if it is connected but not generated like dyeing, sewing, mixing roasted flour with fat, plowing land, and planting trees, that prevents rescission by agreement. And if it is separate and generated like offspring, milk, compensation, fruit, and wool, it prevents [rescission] by agreement. And if it is separate and not generated like rent, profit, gift, and charity, it does not prevent [rescission] by agreement. If the buyer accepts, it is his; otherwise, it is the same according to the two, and according to Abu Hanifa it is returned to the seller. End. In al-Siraj: If the hen lays an egg during the period, the option lapses unless it is spoiled [?]. And if the animal gives birth to a young, [the option] lapses unless the young is dead. End. The conclusion: they are preventive absolutely except separate not generated. And in al-Zahiriyya from the second: He bought a slave with a three-day option and took possession, then someone gave the slave property or he earned it, then the slave consumed it with the buyer's knowledge without his permission or without his knowledge; that does not void the buyer's option in the slave. And if the buyer's umm walad is given to the slave and the slave takes possession, the buyer's option in the slave is voided. He said: The child is not like the umm walad because the umm walad remains in his ownership after return by virtue of the option, while the child does not remain. End. The latter needs editing. As for taking by pre-emption, its form is that he buys a house with an option, then another house adjacent to it is sold, and the buyer with the option takes it by pre-emption because it [the right] occurs only through ownership, so it is evidence of acceptance, thus implying the lapse of the option. And we have presented the excuse for Abu Hanifa regarding it at his statement 'the buyer does not own [by pre-emption]', and if the author had said 'and claiming pre-emption through it instead of taking' it would be better because claiming it causes lapse even if he does not take it, as in al-Mi'raj. And it is restricted to the option of condition because claiming does not lapse the option of seeing or defect, as in al-Mi'raj, and the commentator's limitation to the option of seeing is inadequate. His statement: (And if) the buyer stipulates the option for a non-party, it is valid, and whichever of them accepts or annuls is valid. Because stipulating the option for a non-party is permissible by istihsan, not by qiyas, and it is the saying of Zufar, because it is among the requirements of the contract, so stipulating it for another is not allowed like stipulating the price upon a non-buyer. And our proof: The option for a non-contracting party is established only as a deputyship from the contracting party, so the option is given to him by implication, then he is made a deputy for him to validate his action. In that case, each of them has the option, so whichever accepts, it is valid, and whichever annuls, it is annulled. If the author had said 'and if one of the contracting parties stipulates the option for a stranger, it is valid' it would be better to include both seller and buyer as stipulators, and to exclude one stipulating for the other. For his statement 'for a non-party' applies to the seller and that is not intended. Hence it is said in al-Mi'raj: 'By non-party here is meant other than the two contracting parties' to accommodate Zufar's difference. It is restricted to the option of condition because the option of defect and seeing are not established for non-contracting parties, as in al-Mi'raj. His statement indicates that if one of them accepts and the other says 'I am not satisfied', the sale is binding. And if he authorizes his agent to sell with an option and he sells without it, it is not valid. And if he sells and stipulates as ordered, he does not have the right to accept on behalf of the principal, and the principal has the right to accept. And if he authorizes him to buy with a stipulation for the principal, and he buys without stipulating it, it is binding on him; thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. His statement: (If one accepts and the other annuls, then the earlier [action] has more right) because it occurred at a time when no one else was competing with him. In al-Tatar Khaniyya: And if the buyer's son is given to the slave and the slave takes possession of the son's property, the buyer's option in the slave is not voided. And if the buyer's umm walad is given to the slave, etc. His statement: (The latter needs editing) means the issue of gifting the buyer's umm walad to the slave, and its need for editing because if she is his umm walad, how is she in another's ownership so that she is given to the slave? And also how does she remain in his ownership after the return?
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Al-Bahr al-Raiq' on the chapter of Khiyar al-Shart (Option of Condition) from the matn 'Kanz al-Daqaiq'. It covers a wide range of rulings regarding actions that constitute acceptance or nullification of the option, as well as the effects of defects, increases, and other factors on the validity of the option. The commentary begins by stating that certain actions by the seller, such as forgiving the price or buying something with it, clearly indicate acceptance and thus annul the option. However, mere riding for testing does not constitute acceptance, while riding for a purpose like watering or feeding does. Copying a book does not void the option, but turning pages or studying from it does, according to the relied-upon view. The text then discusses various scenarios from other works like al-Zahiriyya, al-Siraj, and al-Muhit, where specific acts such as watering land, marrying off a slave, or permitting trade annul the option. A significant portion is dedicated to the effects of defects and increases during the option period. If a defect occurs in the buyer's possession during his option period, his option is voided according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), because the item is under the buyer's liability. However, Muhammad al-Shaybani has a different view: if the defect occurred by the seller's act, the buyer is not bound. Regarding increases, the ruling depends on the type: connected and generated increases (like fattening) prevent return and make the sale binding, except according to Muhammad; connected but not generated (like dyeing) prevent rescission by consensus; separate and generated (like offspring) also prevent rescission; while separate and not generated (like rent) do not prevent. The commentary then addresses the issue of stipulating the option for a non-contracting party (ghayr al-'aqidayn). The Hanafi position, based on istihsan, is that this is valid, unlike the qiyas of Zufar who disallows it. The text explains that the option is established by deputyship, and each party (the stipulator and the third party) can independently accept or annul. If both act simultaneously, the annulment takes precedence. The passage concludes with a discussion of pre-emption (shuf'a) and how taking by pre-emption during the option period implies acceptance and thus annuls the option. Throughout, the commentary references multiple authoritative sources within the Hanafi school, such as al-Mi'raj, al-Zahiriyya, al-Siraj, and Jami' al-Fusulayn, reflecting the depth of legal analysis typical of later Hanafi works.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): Option of condition.
ضمان (daman): Liability for loss or damage; during option, the item is under the buyer's daman if in his possession.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for reduction in value due to a defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what happens if a defect occurs in the purchased item during the buyer's option period?
A) The buyer's option is voided and the sale is binding; buyer may claim arsh.
B) The buyer's option remains; he can return the item.
C) The option is transferred to the seller.
D) The sale is automatically rescinded.

Key Takeaway
During the buyer's option, any defect voids the option according to the Sahibayn; the buyer's remedy is arsh, not return.

Increases During Khiyar: Classification and Ruling
Rulings on increases during khiyar al-shart

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify increases into four types (connected generated, connected not generated, separate generated, separate not generated) and state whether each prevents return or not, including Muhammad's exception.

Core Idea
Connected generated increases prevent return and make the sale binding, except according to Muhammad; separate not generated increases do not prevent return.

When the purchased item increases in value or yields benefit during the option period, does that affect the right to return? Hanafi fiqh distinguishes increases by two criteria: connected vs. separate, and generated vs. not generated. Each combination yields a different ruling.

Guided Path
1
Classify the increase as connected or separate
Determine whether the increase is physically attached to the item (e.g., fattening, dyeing) or separate (e.g., offspring, rent).
2
Classify as generated or not generated
Determine whether the increase naturally arises from the item (e.g., growth, offspring) or is added externally (e.g., dyeing, sewing).
3
Apply the ruling for the category
Match the increase to one of four categories and apply the rule: connected generated prevents return (except Muhammad), connected not generated prevents by consensus, separate generated prevents by consensus, separate not generated does not prevent.
The text from Jami' al-Fusulayn lists examples for each.
4
Account for intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Muhammad disagrees on connected generated increases: he holds they do not prevent return.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب خيار الشرط البائع ليس بفسخ على الأصح ولو أبرأه من الثمن أو اشترى منه به شيئاً أو ساومه به فهو إجازة؛ كذا في المعراج . وقيد الاستخدام ثانياً من المشتري بأن لا يكون في نوع آخر والركوب امتحاناً ليس إجازة لا ثانياً كركوبها لحاجة أو شغل أو حمل عليها إلا علفها عند محمد، والركوب للرد والسقي والإعلاف إجازة، ولو نسخ من الكتاب لنفسه أو لغيره لا يبطل، وإن قلب الأوراق وبالدرس منه يبطل، وقيل
