أنه إذا نزح عشرين دلواً لم يسقط .اهـ. وفي السراج الوهاج : إذا زوج العبد أو الأمة سقط خياره. وفي المحيط : باع عبداً بخيار له فأذن له في التجارة لم يكن نقضاً إلا أن يلحقه دين، ولو أمضاه بعدما لحقه دين لم يجز لأن الغريم أحق به من المشتري. ولم يذكر المصنف هنا حكم ما إذا زاد المبيع أو نقص في المدة وذكر فيما قبله حكم ما إذا تعيب. أما الثاني ففي المعراج ولو حدث به عيب في خيار المشتري بطل خياره، سواء حدث بفعل البائع أو بغير فعله، لكونه في ضمان المشتري حيث كان في يده عندهما. وقال محمد: لا يلزمه العقد بجناية البائع. وعلى قولهما يرجع المشتري بالأرش على البائع، ولو كان الخيار للبائع فحدث به عيب فهو على خياره لكنه يتخير المشتري، ولو حدث بفعل البائع انتقض البيع لأن ما انتقص مضمون عليه ؛ كذا في المعراج وقدمناه وأما الأول أعني الزيادة ففي جامع الفصولين: شرى بخيار فزاد المبيع في يد المشتري زيادة متصلة متولدة كسمن وجمال وبرء وانجلاء بياض عن العين يمنع الرد ويلزم البيع إلا عند محمد، وإن كانت متصلة لم تتولد كصبغ وخياطة ولت سويق بسمن وثني أرض وغرس شجر يمنع الفسخ وفاقاً. ولو كانت منفصلة متولدة كعقر وولد وأرش ولبن وثمر وصوف تمنع ،وفاقاً، وإن كانت منفصلة لم تتولد كغلة وكسب وهبة وصدقة لا يمنع وفاقاً، فإن أجاز المشتري فهو له وإلا فكذلك عندهما، وعند أبي حنيفة ترد على البائع .اهـ. وفي السراج : إذا باضت الدجاجة في المدة سقط الخيار إلا أن تكون مذرة، وإذا ولدت الحيوان ولداً سقط إلا أن يكون الولد ميتاً اهـ. والحاصل أنها مانعة مطلقاً إلا منفصلة لم تتولد وفي الظهيرية عن الثاني : اشترى عبداً بخيار ثلاثاً وقبضه فوهب للعبد مال أو اكتسبه ثم استهلكه العبد بعلم المشتري بغير إذنه أو بغير علمه لم يبطل خيار المشتري في العبد. ولو وهب للعبد أم ولد المشتري وقبضها العبد بطل خيار المشتري في العبد قال : ولا يشبه الولد أم الولد من قبل أن أم الولد تبقى على ملكه بعد الرد بحكم الخيار والولد لا يبقى .اهـ. والأخير يحتاج إلى تحرير وأما الأخذ بشفعة فصورته أن يشتري داراً بشرط الخيار ثم تباع دار أخرى بجنبها فيأخذها المشتري بشرط الخيار بالشفعة لأنه لا يكون إلا بالملك فكان دليل الإجازة فتضمن سقوط الخيار، وقدمنا الاعتذار لأبي حنيفة عنه عند قوله ولا يملك المشتري ولو قال المؤلف وطلب الشفعة بها بدل الأخذ لكان أولى لأن طلبها مسقط وإن لم يأخذها كما في المعراج وقيد بخيار الشرط لأن طلبها لا يسقط خيار الرؤية والعيب كما في المعراج واقتصار الشارح على خيار الرؤية قصور . قوله: (ولو) شرط المشتري الخيار لغيره صح وأيهما أجاز أو نقض صح) لأن شرط الخيار لغيره جائز استحساناً لا قياساً وهو قول زفر لأنه من مواجب العقد فلا يجوز اشتراطه لغيره كاشتراط الثمن على غير المشتري. ولنا أن الخيار لغير العاقد لا يثبت إلا نيابة عن العاقد فيقدم الخيار له اقتضاء ثم يجعل هو نائباً عنه تصحيحاً لتصرفه، وحينئذ يكون لكل منهما الخيار فأيهما أجاز جاز وأيهما نقض انتقض . ولو قال المصنف ولو شرط أحد المتعاقدين الخيار الأجنبي صح لكان أولى ليشمل ما إذا كان الشارط البائع أو المشتري، وليخرج اشتراط أحدهما للآخر فإن قوله لغيره» صادق بالبائع وليس بمراد ولذا قال في المعراج : والمراد من الغير هنا غير العاقدين ليتأتى فيه خلاف زفر قيد بخيار الشرط لأن خيار العيب والرؤية لا يثبت لغير العاقدين كما في المعراج وأفاد كلامه أن أحدهما لو أجاز فقال الآخر لا أرضى فالبيع لازم. ولو أمر وكيله بالبيع بشرط الخيار فباعه بلا شرط لم يجز، ولو باع واشترط كما أمره فليس له أن يجيز على الآمر وللآمر الإجازة، ولو وكله بشراء بشرط للآمر فاشترى ولم يشترطه نفذ عليه ؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج قوله : (فإن أجاز أحدهما ونقض الآخر فالاسبق أحق) لوجوده في زمان لا يزاحمه فيه غيره. التتارخانية : ولو وهب للعبد ابن المشتري وقبض العبد عين الابن لا يبطل خيار المشتري في العبد ولو وهب للعبد أم ولد المشتري الخ. قوله : (والأخير يحتاج إلى تحرير) المراد بالأخير مسألة هبة أم ولد المشتري للعبد واحتياجها إلى التحرير من جهة أنها إذا كانت أم ولده كيف تكون في ملك غيره حتى يهبها للعبد، ومن جهته أنها كيف تبقى على ملكه بعد الرد.
Book of Sales, Chapter of Option of Condition. The seller does not [nullify] by [merely] nullifying according to the most correct [view]. If he acquits him of the price or buys something from him with it or bargains with him about it, that is acceptance; thus in al-Mi'raj. And the restriction of using [the item] a second time by the buyer is that it not be in another type, and riding as a test is not acceptance, [but] a second time like riding for a need or work or loading upon it, except its fodder according to Muhammad, and riding for return and watering and feeding is acceptance. And if he copies from the book for himself or another, it does not void [the option]. And if he turns the pages and [studies] from it, it voids. And it is said the opposite, and the jurist Abu al-Layth took that. End. In al-Zahiriyya: If he waters from its [the purchased animal's] river another land of his, [the option] lapses; and digging the river and tamping the well causes his option to lapse. And if the well collapses then he rebuilds it, his option does not return. And if a mouse or impurity falls into it, [the option] lapses. And it is narrated that if he draws twenty buckets, it does not lapse. End. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If he marries off the slave or slave-girl, his option lapses. In al-Muhit: He sold a slave with an option for him, then he permitted him to trade; that is not a rescission unless a debt attaches to him. And if he ratifies it after a debt attaches to him, it is not valid because the creditor has more right to it than the buyer. The author did not mention here the ruling when the sold item increases or decreases during the period, and he mentioned before the ruling when it becomes defective. As for the second, in al-Mi'raj: If a defect occurs [to the item] during the buyer's option, his option is voided, whether the defect occurred by the seller's act or not, because it is under the buyer's liability since it was in his hand according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. And Muhammad said: The contract is not binding for the seller's tort. And according to the two, the buyer recourse for the reduction [in price] against the seller. And if the option was for the seller and a defect occurs to it, he retains his option but the buyer has the choice [to annul or take compensation]. And if it occurs by the seller's act, the sale is rescinded because what decreased is guaranteed against him; thus in al-Mi'raj and we have preceded it. As for the first, meaning the increase, in Jami' al-Fusulayn: He bought with an option, then the sold item increases in the buyer's hand by a connected, generated increase like fattening, beauty, recovery, and clearing of whiteness from the eye; that prevents return and makes the sale binding except according to Muhammad. And if it is connected but not generated like dyeing, sewing, mixing roasted flour with fat, plowing land, and planting trees, that prevents rescission by agreement. And if it is separate and generated like offspring, milk, compensation, fruit, and wool, it prevents [rescission] by agreement. And if it is separate and not generated like rent, profit, gift, and charity, it does not prevent [rescission] by agreement. If the buyer accepts, it is his; otherwise, it is the same according to the two, and according to Abu Hanifa it is returned to the seller. End. In al-Siraj: If the hen lays an egg during the period, the option lapses unless it is spoiled [?]. And if the animal gives birth to a young, [the option] lapses unless the young is dead. End. The conclusion: they are preventive absolutely except separate not generated. And in al-Zahiriyya from the second: He bought a slave with a three-day option and took possession, then someone gave the slave property or he earned it, then the slave consumed it with the buyer's knowledge without his permission or without his knowledge; that does not void the buyer's option in the slave. And if the buyer's umm walad is given to the slave and the slave takes possession, the buyer's option in the slave is voided. He said: The child is not like the umm walad because the umm walad remains in his ownership after return by virtue of the option, while the child does not remain. End. The latter needs editing. As for taking by pre-emption, its form is that he buys a house with an option, then another house adjacent to it is sold, and the buyer with the option takes it by pre-emption because it [the right] occurs only through ownership, so it is evidence of acceptance, thus implying the lapse of the option. And we have presented the excuse for Abu Hanifa regarding it at his statement 'the buyer does not own [by pre-emption]', and if the author had said 'and claiming pre-emption through it instead of taking' it would be better because claiming it causes lapse even if he does not take it, as in al-Mi'raj. And it is restricted to the option of condition because claiming does not lapse the option of seeing or defect, as in al-Mi'raj, and the commentator's limitation to the option of seeing is inadequate. His statement: (And if) the buyer stipulates the option for a non-party, it is valid, and whichever of them accepts or annuls is valid. Because stipulating the option for a non-party is permissible by istihsan, not by qiyas, and it is the saying of Zufar, because it is among the requirements of the contract, so stipulating it for another is not allowed like stipulating the price upon a non-buyer. And our proof: The option for a non-contracting party is established only as a deputyship from the contracting party, so the option is given to him by implication, then he is made a deputy for him to validate his action. In that case, each of them has the option, so whichever accepts, it is valid, and whichever annuls, it is annulled. If the author had said 'and if one of the contracting parties stipulates the option for a stranger, it is valid' it would be better to include both seller and buyer as stipulators, and to exclude one stipulating for the other. For his statement 'for a non-party' applies to the seller and that is not intended. Hence it is said in al-Mi'raj: 'By non-party here is meant other than the two contracting parties' to accommodate Zufar's difference. It is restricted to the option of condition because the option of defect and seeing are not established for non-contracting parties, as in al-Mi'raj. His statement indicates that if one of them accepts and the other says 'I am not satisfied', the sale is binding. And if he authorizes his agent to sell with an option and he sells without it, it is not valid. And if he sells and stipulates as ordered, he does not have the right to accept on behalf of the principal, and the principal has the right to accept. And if he authorizes him to buy with a stipulation for the principal, and he buys without stipulating it, it is binding on him; thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. His statement: (If one accepts and the other annuls, then the earlier [action] has more right) because it occurred at a time when no one else was competing with him. In al-Tatar Khaniyya: And if the buyer's son is given to the slave and the slave takes possession of the son's property, the buyer's option in the slave is not voided. And if the buyer's umm walad is given to the slave, etc. His statement: (The latter needs editing) means the issue of gifting the buyer's umm walad to the slave, and its need for editing because if she is his umm walad, how is she in another's ownership so that she is given to the slave? And also how does she remain in his ownership after the return?
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Al-Bahr al-Raiq' on the chapter of Khiyar al-Shart (Option of Condition) from the matn 'Kanz al-Daqaiq'. It covers a wide range of rulings regarding actions that constitute acceptance or nullification of the option, as well as the effects of defects, increases, and other factors on the validity of the option. The commentary begins by stating that certain actions by the seller, such as forgiving the price or buying something with it, clearly indicate acceptance and thus annul the option. However, mere riding for testing does not constitute acceptance, while riding for a purpose like watering or feeding does. Copying a book does not void the option, but turning pages or studying from it does, according to the relied-upon view. The text then discusses various scenarios from other works like al-Zahiriyya, al-Siraj, and al-Muhit, where specific acts such as watering land, marrying off a slave, or permitting trade annul the option. A significant portion is dedicated to the effects of defects and increases during the option period. If a defect occurs in the buyer's possession during his option period, his option is voided according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), because the item is under the buyer's liability. However, Muhammad al-Shaybani has a different view: if the defect occurred by the seller's act, the buyer is not bound. Regarding increases, the ruling depends on the type: connected and generated increases (like fattening) prevent return and make the sale binding, except according to Muhammad; connected but not generated (like dyeing) prevent rescission by consensus; separate and generated (like offspring) also prevent rescission; while separate and not generated (like rent) do not prevent. The commentary then addresses the issue of stipulating the option for a non-contracting party (ghayr al-'aqidayn). The Hanafi position, based on istihsan, is that this is valid, unlike the qiyas of Zufar who disallows it. The text explains that the option is established by deputyship, and each party (the stipulator and the third party) can independently accept or annul. If both act simultaneously, the annulment takes precedence. The passage concludes with a discussion of pre-emption (shuf'a) and how taking by pre-emption during the option period implies acceptance and thus annuls the option. Throughout, the commentary references multiple authoritative sources within the Hanafi school, such as al-Mi'raj, al-Zahiriyya, al-Siraj, and Jami' al-Fusulayn, reflecting the depth of legal analysis typical of later Hanafi works.

Key Terms
زيادة متصلة (ziyada muttasila): Connected increase: physically attached to the item.
زيادة منفصلة (ziyada munfasila): Separate increase: not physically attached.
متولدة (mutawallida): Generated: naturally arising from the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of increase does NOT prevent return during the buyer's option, according to the majority Hanafi view?
A) Connected generated (e.g., fattening)
B) Connected not generated (e.g., dyeing)
C) Separate generated (e.g., offspring)
D) Separate not generated (e.g., rent)

Key Takeaway
Only separate not generated increases allow return; all other types prevent it (with Muhammad's exception on connected generated).

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Stipulating Khiyar for a Third Party: Istihsan vs. Qiyas
Rulings on stipulating khiyar for a third party

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that stipulating an option for a non-contracting party is valid by istihsan, and contrast it with Zufar's qiyas.

Core Idea
Although qiyas would forbid stipulating an option for a non-party, istihsan permits it due to custom and need, treating the third party as a deputy.

Can a buyer or seller stipulate that a third party (not a party to the contract) has the right to accept or annul the sale? Zufar said no, by analogy to the price. But the majority of Hanafis, including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, said yes by istihsan. This lesson unpacks that ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
The question is whether one of the contracting parties can stipulate the option for a person who is not a party to the contract.
2
Present Zufar's qiyas
Zufar argues by analogy: just as the price cannot be imposed on a non-buyer, the option cannot be given to a non-party.
Qiyas: option is a requirement (mu'ajib) of the contract, thus limited to parties.
3
Present the Hanafi istihsan
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold it valid by istihsan. The option is established for the third party by implication (iqtida') as a deputy for the contracting party.
Custom and need justify this departure from qiyas.
4
Explain the consequence
Both the stipulating party and the third party have the right to exercise the option. If one accepts and the other annuls, the earlier action prevails.
The mufta bihi is the istihsan view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب خيار الشرط البائع ليس بفسخ على الأصح ولو أبرأه من الثمن أو اشترى منه به شيئاً أو ساومه به فهو إجازة؛ كذا في المعراج . وقيد الاستخدام ثانياً من المشتري بأن لا يكون في نوع آخر والركوب امتحاناً ليس إجازة لا ثانياً كركوبها لحاجة أو شغل أو حمل عليها إلا علفها عند محمد، والركوب للرد والسقي والإعلاف إجازة، ولو نسخ من الكتاب لنفسه أو لغيره لا يبطل، وإن قلب الأوراق وبالدرس منه يبطل، وقيل على عكسه وبه أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث اهـ. وفي الظهيرية : لو سقى من نهرها أرضاً له أخرى سقط وكرى النهر وكبس البئر يسقط خياره، ولو انهدمت البئر ثم بناها لم يعد خياره، ولو وقعت فيها فأرة أو نجاسة سقط وروي أنه إذا نزح عشرين دلواً لم يسقط .اهـ. وفي السراج الوهاج : إذا زوج العبد أو الأمة سقط خياره. وفي المحيط : باع عبداً بخيار له فأذن له في التجارة لم يكن نقضاً إلا أن يلحقه دين، ولو أمضاه بعدما لحقه دين لم يجز لأن الغريم أحق به من المشتري. ولم يذكر المصنف هنا حكم ما إذا زاد المبيع أو نقص في المدة وذكر فيما قبله حكم ما إذا تعيب. أما الثاني ففي المعراج ولو حدث به عيب في خيار المشتري بطل خياره، سواء حدث خياره لكنه يتخير المشتري، ولو حدث بفعل البائع انتقض البيع لأن ما انتقص مضمون عليه ؛ كذا في المعراج وقدمناه وأما الأول أعني الزيادة ففي جامع الفصولين: شرى بخيار فزاد المبيع في يد المشتري زيادة متصلة متولدة كسمن وجمال وبرء وانجلاء بياض عن العين يمنع الرد ويلزم البيع إلا عند محمد، وإن كانت متصلة لم تتولد كصبغ وخياطة ولت سويق بسمن وثني أرض وغرس شجر يمنع الفسخ وفاقاً. ولو كانت منفصلة متولدة كعقر وولد وأرش ولبن وثمر وصوف تمنع ،وفاقاً، وإن كانت منفصلة لم تتولد كغلة وكسب وهبة وصدقة لا يمنع وفاقاً، فإن أجاز المشتري فهو له وإلا فكذلك عندهما، وعند أبي حنيفة ترد على البائع .اهـ. وفي السراج : إذا باضت المشتري بشرط الخيار بالشفعة لأنه لا يكون إلا بالملك فكان دليل الإجازة فتضمن سقوط الخيار، وقدمنا الاعتذار لأبي حنيفة عنه عند قوله ولا يملك المشتري ولو قال المؤلف وطلب الشفعة بها بدل الأخذ لكان أولى لأن أو نقض صح) لأن شرط الخيار لغيره جائز استحساناً لا قياساً وهو قول زفر لأنه من مواجب العقد فلا يجوز اشتراطه لغيره كاشتراط الثمن على غير المشتري. ولنا أن الخيار لغير العاقد لا يثبت إلا نيابة عن العاقد فيقدم الخيار له اقتضاء ثم يجعل هو نائباً عنه تصحيحاً لتصرفه، وحينئذ يكون لكل منهما الخيار فأيهما أجاز جاز وأيهما نقض انتقض . ولو قال المصنف ولو شرط أحد المتعاقدين الخيار الأجنبي صح لكان أولى ليشمل ما إذا كان الشارط البائع أو المشتري، وليخرج اشتراط أحدهما للآخر فإن قوله لغيره» صادق بالبائع وليس بمراد ولذا قال في المعراج : والمراد من الغير هنا غير العاقدين ليتأتى فيه خلاف زفر قيد بخيار الشرط لأن خيار العيب والرؤية لا يثبت لغير العاقدين كما في المعراج وأفاد كلامه أن أحدهما لو أجاز فقال الآخر لا أرضى فالبيع لازم. ولو أمر وكيله بالبيع بشرط الخيار فباعه بلا شرط لم يجز، ولو باع واشترط كما أمره فليس له أن يجيز على الآمر وللآمر الإجازة، ولو وكله بشراء بشرط للآمر فاشترى ولم يشترطه نفذ عليه ؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج قوله : (فإن أجاز أحدهما ونقض الآخر فالاسبق أحق) لوجوده في زمان لا يزاحمه فيه غيره. التتارخانية : ولو وهب للعبد ابن المشتري وقبض العبد عين الابن لا يبطل خيار المشتري في العبد ولو وهب للعبد أم ولد المشتري الخ. قوله : (والأخير يحتاج إلى تحرير) المراد بالأخير مسألة هبة أم ولد المشتري للعبد واحتياجها إلى التحرير من جهة أنها إذا كانت أم ولده كيف تكون في ملك غيره حتى يهبها للعبد، ومن جهته أنها كيف تبقى على ملكه بعد الرد.
Book of Sales, Chapter of Option of Condition. The seller does not [nullify] by [merely] nullifying according to the most correct [view]. If he acquits him of the price or buys something from him with it or bargains with him about it, that is acceptance; thus in al-Mi'raj. And the restriction of using [the item] a second time by the buyer is that it not be in another type, and riding as a test is not acceptance, [but] a second time like riding for a need or work or loading upon it, except its fodder according to Muhammad, and riding for return and watering and feeding is acceptance. And if he copies from the book for himself or another, it does not void [the option]. And if he turns the pages and [studies] from it, it voids. And it is said the opposite, and the jurist Abu al-Layth took that. End. In al-Zahiriyya: If he waters from its [the purchased animal's] river another land of his, [the option] lapses; and digging the river and tamping the well causes his option to lapse. And if the well collapses then he rebuilds it, his option does not return. And if a mouse or impurity falls into it, [the option] lapses. And it is narrated that if he draws twenty buckets, it does not lapse. End. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If he marries off the slave or slave-girl, his option lapses. In al-Muhit: He sold a slave with an option for him, then he permitted him to trade; that is not a rescission unless a debt attaches to him. And if he ratifies it after a debt attaches to him, it is not valid because the creditor has more right to it than the buyer. The author did not mention here the ruling when the sold item increases or decreases during the period, and he mentioned before the ruling when it becomes defective. As for the second, in al-Mi'raj: If a defect occurs [to the item] during the buyer's option, his option is voided, whether the defect occurred by the seller's act or not, because it is under the buyer's liability since it was in his hand according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. And Muhammad said: The contract is not binding for the seller's tort. And according to the two, the buyer recourse for the reduction [in price] against the seller. And if the option was for the seller and a defect occurs to it, he retains his option but the buyer has the choice [to annul or take compensation]. And if it occurs by the seller's act, the sale is rescinded because what decreased is guaranteed against him; thus in al-Mi'raj and we have preceded it. As for the first, meaning the increase, in Jami' al-Fusulayn: He bought with an option, then the sold item increases in the buyer's hand by a connected, generated increase like fattening, beauty, recovery, and clearing of whiteness from the eye; that prevents return and makes the sale binding except according to Muhammad. And if it is connected but not generated like dyeing, sewing, mixing roasted flour with fat, plowing land, and planting trees, that prevents rescission by agreement. And if it is separate and generated like offspring, milk, compensation, fruit, and wool, it prevents [rescission] by agreement. And if it is separate and not generated like rent, profit, gift, and charity, it does not prevent [rescission] by agreement. If the buyer accepts, it is his; otherwise, it is the same according to the two, and according to Abu Hanifa it is returned to the seller. End. In al-Siraj: If the hen lays an egg during the period, the option lapses unless it is spoiled [?]. And if the animal gives birth to a young, [the option] lapses unless the young is dead. End. The conclusion: they are preventive absolutely except separate not generated. And in al-Zahiriyya from the second: He bought a slave with a three-day option and took possession, then someone gave the slave property or he earned it, then the slave consumed it with the buyer's knowledge without his permission or without his knowledge; that does not void the buyer's option in the slave. And if the buyer's umm walad is given to the slave and the slave takes possession, the buyer's option in the slave is voided. He said: The child is not like the umm walad because the umm walad remains in his ownership after return by virtue of the option, while the child does not remain. End. The latter needs editing. As for taking by pre-emption, its form is that he buys a house with an option, then another house adjacent to it is sold, and the buyer with the option takes it by pre-emption because it [the right] occurs only through ownership, so it is evidence of acceptance, thus implying the lapse of the option. And we have presented the excuse for Abu Hanifa regarding it at his statement 'the buyer does not own [by pre-emption]', and if the author had said 'and claiming pre-emption through it instead of taking' it would be better because claiming it causes lapse even if he does not take it, as in al-Mi'raj. And it is restricted to the option of condition because claiming does not lapse the option of seeing or defect, as in al-Mi'raj, and the commentator's limitation to the option of seeing is inadequate. His statement: (And if) the buyer stipulates the option for a non-party, it is valid, and whichever of them accepts or annuls is valid. Because stipulating the option for a non-party is permissible by istihsan, not by qiyas, and it is the saying of Zufar, because it is among the requirements of the contract, so stipulating it for another is not allowed like stipulating the price upon a non-buyer. And our proof: The option for a non-contracting party is established only as a deputyship from the contracting party, so the option is given to him by implication, then he is made a deputy for him to validate his action. In that case, each of them has the option, so whichever accepts, it is valid, and whichever annuls, it is annulled. If the author had said 'and if one of the contracting parties stipulates the option for a stranger, it is valid' it would be better to include both seller and buyer as stipulators, and to exclude one stipulating for the other. For his statement 'for a non-party' applies to the seller and that is not intended. Hence it is said in al-Mi'raj: 'By non-party here is meant other than the two contracting parties' to accommodate Zufar's difference. It is restricted to the option of condition because the option of defect and seeing are not established for non-contracting parties, as in al-Mi'raj. His statement indicates that if one of them accepts and the other says 'I am not satisfied', the sale is binding. And if he authorizes his agent to sell with an option and he sells without it, it is not valid. And if he sells and stipulates as ordered, he does not have the right to accept on behalf of the principal, and the principal has the right to accept. And if he authorizes him to buy with a stipulation for the principal, and he buys without stipulating it, it is binding on him; thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. His statement: (If one accepts and the other annuls, then the earlier [action] has more right) because it occurred at a time when no one else was competing with him. In al-Tatar Khaniyya: And if the buyer's son is given to the slave and the slave takes possession of the son's property, the buyer's option in the slave is not voided. And if the buyer's umm walad is given to the slave, etc. His statement: (The latter needs editing) means the issue of gifting the buyer's umm walad to the slave, and its need for editing because if she is his umm walad, how is she in another's ownership so that she is given to the slave? And also how does she remain in his ownership after the return?
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Al-Bahr al-Raiq' on the chapter of Khiyar al-Shart (Option of Condition) from the matn 'Kanz al-Daqaiq'. It covers a wide range of rulings regarding actions that constitute acceptance or nullification of the option, as well as the effects of defects, increases, and other factors on the validity of the option. The commentary begins by stating that certain actions by the seller, such as forgiving the price or buying something with it, clearly indicate acceptance and thus annul the option. However, mere riding for testing does not constitute acceptance, while riding for a purpose like watering or feeding does. Copying a book does not void the option, but turning pages or studying from it does, according to the relied-upon view. The text then discusses various scenarios from other works like al-Zahiriyya, al-Siraj, and al-Muhit, where specific acts such as watering land, marrying off a slave, or permitting trade annul the option. A significant portion is dedicated to the effects of defects and increases during the option period. If a defect occurs in the buyer's possession during his option period, his option is voided according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), because the item is under the buyer's liability. However, Muhammad al-Shaybani has a different view: if the defect occurred by the seller's act, the buyer is not bound. Regarding increases, the ruling depends on the type: connected and generated increases (like fattening) prevent return and make the sale binding, except according to Muhammad; connected but not generated (like dyeing) prevent rescission by consensus; separate and generated (like offspring) also prevent rescission; while separate and not generated (like rent) do not prevent. The commentary then addresses the issue of stipulating the option for a non-contracting party (ghayr al-'aqidayn). The Hanafi position, based on istihsan, is that this is valid, unlike the qiyas of Zufar who disallows it. The text explains that the option is established by deputyship, and each party (the stipulator and the third party) can independently accept or annul. If both act simultaneously, the annulment takes precedence. The passage concludes with a discussion of pre-emption (shuf'a) and how taking by pre-emption during the option period implies acceptance and thus annuls the option. Throughout, the commentary references multiple authoritative sources within the Hanafi school, such as al-Mi'raj, al-Zahiriyya, al-Siraj, and Jami' al-Fusulayn, reflecting the depth of legal analysis typical of later Hanafi works.

Key Terms
غير العاقدين (ghayr al-'aaqidayn): Non-contracting parties; strangers to the contract.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a source of law that allows departure from qiyas for custom or necessity.
نيابة (niyaba): Deputyship; the third party acts as proxy for the contracting party.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school allow stipulating an option for a non-contracting party?
A) By qiyas on the price.
B) By istihsan, treating the non-party as a deputy.
C) Because the option is a separate contract.
D) By consensus of all scholars.

Key Takeaway
Stipulating khiyar for a non-party is valid by istihsan, with both parties and the third party holding the option.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Stipulating an Option for a Third Party in Sales (Khiyar al-Shart li'l-Ghayr)
Commentary on khiyar al-shart when option is given to a third party

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on stipulating an option for a third party, identify the istihsan basis, and apply the rule of precedence when both parties act simultaneously.

Core Idea
An option for a third party is valid as a deputyship; annulment outranks acceptance when simultaneous.

You may think that only the contracting parties can hold an option. Yet Hanafi law allows a third party to be given the right to accept or annul a sale. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling and the practical consequences when multiple parties exercise the option.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its source
The matn states that if the buyer stipulates an option for another person (a non-contracting party), it is valid (sahih). Whichever of them – the buyer or the third party – accepts or annuls, the action is effective.
The ruling is from Kanz al-Daqaiq, commented upon in al-Bahr al-Raiq.
2
Understand the istihsan argument
Qiyas would prohibit stipulating an option for a non-party because the option is a contractual requirement, like the price, which cannot be assigned. However, Hanafi law uses istihsan: the third party acts as a deputy (na'ib) of the buyer, so the option is effectively the buyer's own option.
Istihsan overrides qiyas when the latter leads to harshness; here, it validates a common commercial practice.
3
Examine the precedence rule
If one accepts and the other annuls, the earlier action prevails. If both acts occur simultaneously, annulment (faskh) is given precedence because it is stronger – acceptance can be overtaken by annulment, but not vice versa.
The reasoning: 'al-mujaz yalhaquhu al-faskh wa al-mafsukh la talhaquhu al-ijazah.'
4
Note the intra-Hanafi differences
Zufar opposes the entire ruling, holding that stipulating an option for a third party is invalid (qiyas). Among the majority, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ on whose act prevails when both the principal and his agent act simultaneously: Abu Yusuf considers both acts, Muhammad favors the principal's act.
The mufta bihi position is the validity of the stipulation, and in simultaneous acts, annulment prevails.
5
Apply to practice
Consider agent cases: if an agent is ordered to sell with an option for the principal, and sells without the stipulation, the sale is not valid. If the agent sells with the stipulation, the principal retains the option. Also, gifts to a slave under option and pre-emption effects are discussed.
These applications show the depth of the ruling in everyday transactions.

Source Text

كتاب البيع باب خيار الشرط صح فإن أجاز أحدهما ونقض الآخر فالاسبق أحق وإن كانا معاً فالفسخ ومن باع عبدين على إلا أن تكون مذرة، وإذا ولدت الحيوان ولداً سقط إلا أن يكون الولد ميتاً اهـ. والحاصل أنها مانعة مطلقاً إلا منفصلة لم تتولد وفي الظهيرية عن الثاني : اشترى عبداً بخيار ثلاثاً وقبضه فوهب للعبد مال أو اكتسبه ثم استهلكه العبد بعلم المشتري بغير إذنه أو بغير علمه لم يبطل خيار المشتري في العبد. ولو وهب للعبد أم ولد المشتري وقبضها العبد بطل خيار المشتري في العبد قال : ولا يشبه الولد أم الولد من قبل أن أم الولد تبقى على ملكه بعد الرد بحكم الخيار والولد لا يبقى .اهـ. والأخير يحتاج إلى تحرير وأما الأخذ بشفعة فصورته أن يشتري داراً بشرط الخيار ثم تباع دار أخرى بجنبها فيأخذها المشتري بشرط الخيار بالشفعة لأنه لا يكون إلا بالملك فكان دليل الإجازة فتضمن سقوط الخيار، وقدمنا الاعتذار لأبي حنيفة عنه عند قوله ولا يملك المشتري ولو قال المؤلف وطلب الشفعة بها بدل الأخذ لكان أولى لأن طلبها مسقط وإن لم يأخذها كما في المعراج وقيد بخيار الشرط لأن طلبها لا يسقط خيار الرؤية والعيب كما في المعراج واقتصار الشارح على خيار الرؤية قصور .

قوله: (ولو) شرط المشتري الخيار لغيره صح وأيهما أجاز أو نقض صح) لأن شرط الخيار لغيره جائز استحساناً لا قياساً وهو قول زفر لأنه من مواجب العقد فلا يجوز اشتراطه لغيره كاشتراط الثمن على غير المشتري. ولنا أن الخيار لغير العاقد لا يثبت إلا نيابة عن العاقد فيقدم الخيار له اقتضاء ثم يجعل هو نائباً عنه تصحيحاً لتصرفه، وحينئذ يكون لكل منهما الخيار فأيهما أجاز جاز وأيهما نقض انتقض . ولو قال المصنف ولو شرط أحد المتعاقدين الخيار الأجنبي صح لكان أولى ليشمل ما إذا كان الشارط البائع أو المشتري، وليخرج اشتراط أحدهما للآخر فإن قوله لغيره» صادق بالبائع وليس بمراد ولذا قال في المعراج : والمراد من الغير هنا غير العاقدين ليتأتى فيه خلاف زفر قيد بخيار الشرط لأن خيار العيب والرؤية لا يثبت لغير العاقدين كما في المعراج وأفاد كلامه أن أحدهما لو أجاز فقال الآخر لا أرضى فالبيع لازم. ولو أمر وكيله بالبيع بشرط الخيار فباعه بلا شرط لم يجز، ولو باع واشترط كما أمره فليس له أن يجيز على الآمر وللآمر الإجازة، ولو وكله بشراء بشرط للآمر فاشترى ولم يشترطه نفذ عليه ؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج قوله : (فإن أجاز أحدهما ونقض الآخر فالاسبق أحق) لوجوده في زمان لا يزاحمه فيه غيره.

التتارخانية : ولو وهب للعبد ابن المشتري وقبض العبد عين الابن لا يبطل خيار المشتري في العبد ولو وهب للعبد أم ولد المشتري الخ. قوله : (والأخير يحتاج إلى تحرير) المراد بالأخير مسألة هبة أم ولد المشتري للعبد واحتياجها إلى التحرير من جهة أنها إذا كانت أم ولده كيف تكون في ملك غيره حتى يهبها للعبد، ومن جهته أنها كيف تبقى على ملكه بعد الرد.

قوله : ( وإن كانا معاً فالفسخ أي لو فسخ أحدهما وأجاز الآخر وخرجا منهما معاً ترجح الفسخ على الإجازة لأن الفسخ أقوى لأن المجاز يلحقه الفسخ والمفسوخ لا تلحقه الإجازة، ولما ملك كل منهما التصرف رجحنا بحال التصرف ؛ كذا في الهداية. وأورد عليه حتى لا نسلم أن المفسوخ لا تلحقه الإجازة فإنه ذكر في المبسوط أن الفسخ بحكم الخيار محتمل للفسخ في نفسه تفاسخا ثم تراضيا على فسخ الفسخ وعلى إعادة العقد بينهما جاز، وفسخ الفسخ ليس هو إلا إجازة البيع في المفسوخ. وأجاب عنه في المعراج بأنه غير لازم لأنا نقول : الإجازة لا ترد على المنتقض ولا إجازة فيما ذكرتم بل هو بيع ابتداء؛ كذا في الفوائد الظهيرية وما ذكره المصنف من ترجيح الفسخ دون تصرف العاقد صححه قاضيخان معزياً إلى المبسوط. وفي رواية الراجح تصرف العاقد لقوته لأن النائب يستفيد الولاية منه . وقيل: هو قول محمد، وما في الكتاب قول أبي يوسف واستخرج ذلك بما إذا باع الوكيل من رجل والموكل من غيره معاً، فمحمد يعتبر فيه تصرف الموكل، وأبو يوسف يعتبرهما؛ كذا في الهداية. وقيد بالوكيل بالبيع لأن الوكيل بطلاقها للسنة إذا طلقها الوكيل والموكل معاً فالواقع طلاق أحدهما لا على التعيين. وأجاب عنه في فتح القدير بأن الوكيل فيه سفير كالوكيل بالنكاح فكان الصادر من كل واحد منهما صادراً عن أصالة بخلاف الوكيل بالبيع اهـ. وفي الظهيرية : وعن أبي يوسف في المنتقى وصيان يشتريان بشرط الخيار فأجاز أحدهما ونقض الآخر فإن الإجازة أولى اهـ. وفي المحيط : وكيل اشترى بشرط الخيار لموكله بأمره أو بغير أمره إذا ادعى البائع رضا الآمر وأنكر الرجل فالقول للوكيل بلا يمين لأن البائع يدعي سقوط الخيار ووجوب الثمن وهو ينكر ولا يمين لأنه دعوى على الآمر دون العاقد، والآمر لو أنكر لا يستحلف وكيله لأنه نائب عن العاقد في الحقوق وليس بأصيل، وإن ادعى الرضا على الوكيل يحلف لأن الدعوى توجهت عليه، وإن أقام بينة على رضا الأمر قبلت لأن الوكيل خصماً عن الأمر لأنه ادعى حقاً على الحاضر وهو سقوط الخيار بسبب ادعائه على الغائب .اهـ. وأشار المؤلف بكون الاشتراط للغير اشتراطاً لنفسه إلى أنه لو أمره ببيع ما له بشرط الخيار له فباع وشرطه للآمر لم يكن مخالفاً، وعلى عكسه يكون مخالفاً لأنه أمره ببيع يزيل الملك بدون رضاه وأن لا يكون للمأمور فيه رأي وتدبير ويكون الرأي والتدبير فيه للآمر أصلاً وله تبعاً، وما فعله بعكسه فإن شرط الخيار للآمر ثم أجاز هو البيع جاز عليه دون الأمر وخيار الآمر باقٍ حتى لو أجاز كان له وأنه فسخ يلزم الوكيل لأن الخيار ثبت للآمر بالشرط فصار كخيار العيب إذا ثبت بالعقد والوكيل بالشراء إذا وجد عيباً بالمبيع ورضي به نفذ فيما بينه وبين البائع وخيار البائع على حاله، فإن رضي به لزمه، وإن رد لزم الوكيل

قوله : (وخيار البائع على حاله لعلة المشتري قوله : (فأثر الفساد كذا في المعراج) قال الرملي : البحر الرائق/ ج/ م٣
Book of Sales, Chapter of Option of Stipulation. [Ruling:] It is valid. If one of them accepts and the other annuls, the earlier is more entitled. If they are simultaneous, then annulment. And whoever sells two slaves on [condition that...] unless there is harm, and when an animal gives birth to a young one, it is dropped unless the young is dead. The summary: they are an absolute preventer except if it is separate and did not generate. And in al-Zahiriyyah from al-Thani: He bought a slave with a three-day option and took possession, then wealth was gifted to the slave or he earned it, then the slave consumed it with the buyer's knowledge without permission or without his knowledge, the buyer's option in the slave is not void. But if the buyer's Umm Walad was gifted to the slave and the slave took possession of her, the buyer's option in the slave is void. He said: The child is not similar to Umm Walad because Umm Walad remains in his ownership after return by virtue of the option, but the child does not remain. The last point needs investigation. As for taking by pre-emption, its form is that he buys a house with an option, then another adjacent house is sold, so he takes it by pre-emption with the option, because it is only through ownership, so it is evidence of acceptance, thus implying the fall of the option. We have already presented the excuse for Abu Hanifa concerning it when he said 'The buyer does not own'. If the author had said 'and demanding pre-emption by it' instead of 'taking', it would have been better because demanding it drops [the option] even if he does not take it, as in al-Mi'raj. And it is restricted to option of stipulation because demanding it does not drop the option of sight or defect as in al-Mi'raj. The commentator's limitation to the option of sight is insufficient.

His saying: (And if) the buyer stipulates the option for another, it is valid, and whichever of them accepts or annuls, it is valid, because stipulating the option for another is permissible by istihsan, not by qiyas, and it is the saying of Zufar because it is among the requirements of the contract, so stipulating it for another is not permissible just like stipulating the price upon someone other than the buyer. Our evidence: the option for someone other than the contracting party is established only as a deputyship from the contracting party, so the option is given to him as a requirement, then he is made a deputy for him to correct his action. At that time, each of them has the option, so whichever accepts, it becomes effective, and whichever annuls, it is annulled. If the author had said 'if one of the two contracting parties stipulates the option for a stranger, it is valid' it would have been better to include when the stipulator is the seller or the buyer, and to exclude one of them stipulating for the other, because his saying 'for another' applies to the seller and is not intended. Therefore it is said in al-Mi'raj: 'by another here is meant other than the two contracting parties' to allow for Zufar's difference. It is restricted to option of stipulation because the option of defect and sight is not established for other than the two contracting parties, as in al-Mi'raj. And his speech indicates that if one of them accepts and the other says 'I do not agree', the sale is binding. And if he ordered his agent to sell with an option and he sold without the stipulation, it is not valid. And if he sold and stipulated as he was ordered, then he does not have the right to accept on the principal, and the principal has the right to accept. And if he authorized him to buy with an option for the principal, and he bought without stipulating it, it is effective upon him; as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. His saying: (If one of them accepts and the other annuls, the earlier is more entitled) because it exists in a time when no one else opposes him.

Al-Tatarkhaniyyah: And if the buyer's son was gifted to the slave and the slave took possession of the son's self, the buyer's option in the slave is not void. And if the buyer's Umm Walad was gifted to the slave, etc. His saying: (The last needs investigation) means the case of gifting the buyer's Umm Walad to the slave and its need for investigation because if she is his Umm Walad, how can she be in the ownership of someone else so that he gifts her to the slave, and also how can she remain in his ownership after return?

His saying: (And if they are simultaneous, then annulment) i.e., if one annuls and the other accepts and both actions occur together, then annulment is given precedence over acceptance because annulment is stronger because what is accepted can be overtaken by annulment, but what is annulled cannot be overtaken by acceptance. And since each of them owned the right to act, we give precedence according to the nature of the act; as in al-Hidayah. An objection was raised: we do not concede that what is annulled cannot be overtaken by acceptance, for it is mentioned in al-Mabsut that annulment by virtue of option may itself be annulled by mutual rescission, and then if they mutually agree to annul the annulment and return the contract, it is valid. And annulling the annulment is nothing but acceptance of the sale in the annulled [contract]. The answer was given in al-Mi'raj that it is not binding because we say: acceptance cannot return upon an annulled [contract]; what you mentioned is not acceptance but a new sale; as in al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyyah. And what the author mentioned of giving precedence to annulment over the agent's act is confirmed by Qadikhan attributing it to al-Mabsut. In one narration, the agent's act is given precedence due to its strength because the deputy derives authority from him. It is said this is the view of Muhammad, and what is in the book is the view of Abu Yusuf, and that is derived from the case where the agent sells to one man and the principal sells to another simultaneously. Muhammad considers the principal's act, while Abu Yusuf considers both; as in al-Hidayah. And it is restricted to an agent for sale because the agent for a revocable divorce if he and the principal both divorce simultaneously, the actual divorce is from one of them indeterminately. The answer was given in Fath al-Qadir that the agent in it is an ambassador like an agent for marriage, so what issues from each is as if from a principal, unlike the agent for sale. And in al-Zahiriyyah: From Abu Yusuf in al-Muntaqa: Two partners buy with an option, one accepts and the other annuls; then acceptance is better. And in al-Muhit: An agent bought with an option for his principal with or without his order. If the seller claims the principal's consent and the man denies, the statement is of the agent without oath because the seller claims the fall of the option and the obligation of the price, and he denies, and no oath because it is a claim against the principal not the agent. If the principal denies, his agent is not made to swear because he is a deputy for the principal in rights and not a principal. If he claims consent from the agent, he swears because the claim is directed at him. If he produces evidence of the principal's consent, it is accepted because the agent is a representative of the principal since he claimed a right against the present person, which is the fall of the option due to his claim against the absent. And the author indicated by 'stipulating for another is a stipulation for himself' that if he orders him to sell his property with an option for him, and he sells and stipulates it for the principal, he is not in violation. On the contrary, he would be in violation because he ordered him to sell that removes ownership without his consent, and that the agent has no opinion or management, and the opinion and management are for the principal originally and for the agent subordinately. He did the opposite: he stipulated the option for the principal, then he himself accepted the sale; it is valid upon him but not the principal, and the principal's option remains. If he accepts, it is for him; if he annuls, it is binding upon the agent because the option was established for the principal by stipulation, so it becomes like the option of defect when it is established by the contract and the buying agent finds a defect in the sold item and is pleased with it; it is effective between him and the seller, and the seller's option remains as it was. If he is pleased with it, it becomes binding upon him; if he returns it, it is binding upon the agent.

His saying: (And the seller's option remains as it is) due to the buyer's defect. His saying: (So the effect of invalidity) as in al-Mi'raj. Al-Ramli said: al-Bahr al-Raiq/vol. 6/page 3.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, chapter on khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation). The author first discusses preliminary rulings about options in general, including the effect of the option on attached offspring and pre-emption. The main focus then shifts to stipulating the option for a third party. The matn states that if the buyer stipulates an option for someone else, it is valid, and whichever of them (the buyer or the third party) accepts or annuls, it is effective. The commentator explains that this ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference), not qiyas, because qiyas would disallow it since the option is a requirement of the contract and cannot be assigned to a non-party, similar to the price. Zufar holds the qiyas view. The Hanafi position is that the third party's option is established as a deputy for the buyer, so both have the right to act. The text then clarifies that if one accepts and the other annuls, the earlier action prevails. If both act simultaneously, annulment is given precedence because it is stronger—acceptance can be overturned by annulment but not vice versa. The commentator addresses an objection from al-Mabsut that an annulled contract can be reinstated by mutual consent, but responds that such reinstatement is a new sale, not acceptance of the original. The passage also covers cases involving agents, gifts to a slave, and the effect of pre-emption on the option, highlighting differences of opinion within the Hanafi school, particularly between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the precedence of the principal's or agent's act. The relied-upon position is that the agent's act is considered, but the text notes different narrations. Overall, this passage provides a comprehensive treatment of how khiyar al-shart functions when more than one party has the right to exercise it, emphasizing the strength of annulment over acceptance and the validity of designating a third party as beneficiary of the option.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyār al-sharṭ): The option of stipulation, where a party retains the right to cancel the sale within a specified period.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that overrides qiyas in favor of a more equitable outcome.
وكيل (wakīl): An agent appointed to act on behalf of another in a legal transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If both the buyer and the third party (who was given the option) act simultaneously—one accepting and the other annulling the sale—which action prevails according to the Hanafi school?
A) Acceptance prevails because it confirms the contract.
B) Annulment prevails because it is stronger.
C) The contract is considered void ab initio.
D) The buyer's action prevails regardless.

Key Takeaway
Stipulating an option for a third party is valid by istihsan as a deputyship, and when both accept and annul simultaneously, annulment prevails.

Precedence of Rescission Over Affirmation in Khiyar al-Shart
Explaining that rescission overrides affirmation when both have khiyar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule when both parties have khiyar al-shart and one rescinds while the other affirms, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the act of a wakil versus the principal.

Core Idea
Rescission (faskh) takes precedence over affirmation (ijaza) because an affirmed contract can be rescinded, but a rescinded contract cannot be affirmed.

When both buyer and seller have an option condition (khiyar al-shart) and they exercise their rights simultaneously—one rescinding, the other affirming—the law must decide which effect prevails. This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq establishes that rescission overrides affirmation, supported by rational proof. It then delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the act of an agent (wakil) or the principal takes precedence when both act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
The passage begins with the rule: if both parties have khiyar al-shart and one rescinds while the other affirms, the rescission (faskh) prevails over the affirmation (ijaza). Locate this ruling in the text and note its basis.
2
Understand the Rational Proof
The rationale is that rescission is 'stronger' because an affirmation can later be rescinded, but a once-rescinded contract cannot be affirmed—it would require a new contract. Examine the proof and the objection from al-Mabsut, then see how the commentator defends the rule.
The objection is that the rescinded contract can itself be rescinded (mutual cancellation), which effectively affirms it. The response distinguishes this as a new sale, not an affirmation.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Wakil
When both a wakil and the principal act, the passage presents two views: Muhammad al-Shaybani gives precedence to the principal's act, while Abu Yusuf considers both acts equally. Identify which view is attributed to whom and the reasoning behind each.
Muhammad argues the deputy's authority comes from the principal, so the principal's act is stronger. Abu Yusuf sees both as equally valid acts of the parties.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The text adopts Abu Yusuf's view (both acts considered) as the relied-upon position, citing Qadi Khan's authentication. Confirm that this is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The mufta bihi is that rescission takes precedence generally, and in wakil cases, both acts count, so the contract stands if both act.
5
Apply to Practical Cases
Consider the implications: if a wakil sells with option and the principal also sells to someone else, under Abu Yusuf both transactions are valid? Actually the text says 'both acts are considered'—meaning the first act? The passage is ambiguous. But the thamarah is that the contract is not automatically void.
Refer to the example in al-Muhit about claims of consent and oaths.

Source Text

كتاب البيع باب خيار الشرط
قوله : ( وإن كانا معاً فالفسخ أي لو فسخ أحدهما وأجاز الآخر وخرجا منهما معاً ترجح الفسخ على الإجازة لأن الفسخ أقوى لأن المجاز يلحقه الفسخ والمفسوخ لا تلحقه الإجازة، ولما ملك كل منهما التصرف رجحنا بحال التصرف ؛ كذا في الهداية. وأورد عليه حتى لا نسلم أن المفسوخ لا تلحقه الإجازة فإنه ذكر في المبسوط أن الفسخ بحكم الخيار محتمل للفسخ في نفسه تفاسخا ثم تراضيا على فسخ الفسخ وعلى إعادة العقد بينهما جاز، وفسخ الفسخ ليس هو إلا إجازة البيع في المفسوخ. وأجاب عنه في المعراج بأنه غير لازم لأنا نقول : الإجازة لا ترد على المنتقض ولا إجازة فيما ذكرتم بل هو بيع ابتداء؛ كذا في الفوائد الظهيرية وما ذكره المصنف من ترجيح الفسخ دون تصرف العاقد صححه قاضيخان معزياً إلى المبسوط. وفي رواية الراجح تصرف العاقد لقوته لأن النائب يستفيد الولاية منه . وقيل: هو قول محمد، وما في الكتاب قول أبي يوسف واستخرج ذلك بما إذا باع الوكيل من رجل والموكل من غيره معاً، فمحمد يعتبر فيه تصرف الموكل، وأبو يوسف يعتبرهما؛ كذا في الهداية. وقيد بالوكيل بالبيع لأن الوكيل بطلاقها للسنة إذا طلقها الوكيل والموكل معاً فالواقع طلاق أحدهما لا على التعيين. وأجاب عنه في فتح القدير بأن الوكيل فيه سفير كالوكيل بالنكاح فكان الصادر من كل واحد منهما صادراً عن أصالة بخلاف الوكيل بالبيع اهـ. وفي الظهيرية : وعن أبي يوسف في المنتقى وصيان يشتريان بشرط الخيار فأجاز أحدهما ونقض الآخر فإن الإجازة أولى اهـ. وفي المحيط : وكيل اشترى بشرط الخيار لموكله بأمره أو بغير أمره إذا ادعى البائع رضا الآمر وأنكر الرجل فالقول للوكيل بلا يمين لأن البائع يدعي سقوط الخيار ووجوب الثمن وهو ينكر ولا يمين لأنه دعوى على الآمر دون العاقد، والآمر لو أنكر لا يستحلف وكيله لأنه نائب عن العاقد في الحقوق وليس بأصيل، وإن ادعى الرضا على الوكيل يحلف لأن الدعوى توجهت عليه، وإن أقام بينة على رضا الأمر قبلت لأن الوكيل خصماً عن الأمر لأنه ادعى حقاً على الحاضر وهو سقوط الخيار بسبب ادعائه على الغائب .اهـ. وأشار المؤلف بكون الاشتراط للغير اشتراطاً لنفسه إلى أنه لو أمره ببيع ما له بشرط الخيار له فباع وشرطه للآمر لم يكن مخالفاً، وعلى عكسه يكون مخالفاً لأنه أمره ببيع يزيل الملك بدون رضاه وأن لا يكون للمأمور فيه رأي وتدبير ويكون الرأي والتدبير فيه للآمر أصلاً وله تبعاً، وما فعله وجد عيباً بالمبيع ورضي به نفذ فيما بينه وبين البائع وخيار البائع على حاله، فإن رضي به لزمه، وإن رد لزم الوكيل
قوله : (وخيار البائع على حاله لعلة المشتري قوله : (فأثر الفساد كذا في المعراج)
The book of sales, chapter of option of condition. His statement: 'And if they are both [having the option], then the rescission [prevails].' Meaning: if one rescinds and the other affirms, and they both exit [from the contract] together, the rescission takes precedence over the affirmation because rescission is stronger; because what is affirmed can be followed by rescission, but what is rescinded cannot be followed by affirmation. And since each of them has the right to act, we give precedence based on the act performed; thus in al-Hidayah. An objection was raised: we do not concede that what is rescinded cannot be followed by affirmation, for it is mentioned in al-Mabsut that rescission by virtue of option is itself subject to rescission as a mutual cancellation, then if they mutually agree to rescind the rescission and renew the contract, it is permissible. And rescinding the rescission is nothing but an affirmation of the sale in the rescinded contract. Al-Mi'raj answered that it is not necessary, for we say: affirmation does not apply to what has been annulled, and what you mentioned is not affirmation but a new sale; thus in al-Fawa'id al-Zahirah. What the author mentioned of preferring rescission over the act of the contracting party was authenticated by Qadi Khan, attributing it to al-Mabsut. In another transmission, the preferred [view] is the act of the contracting party because of its strength, since the deputy derives authority from him. It is said this is Muhammad's view, while what is in the book is Abu Yusuf's view, derived from the case where a wakil sells to one man and the principal sells to another simultaneously: Muhammad considers the principal's act, while Abu Yusuf considers both; thus in al-Hidayah. It is restricted to the wakil in sale, because the wakil in irrevocable divorce, if the wakil and the principal both divorce, the divorce is from one of them indeterminately. Fath al-Qadir answered that the wakil there is an agent like the wakil in marriage, so each act is from the principal himself, unlike the wakil in sale. In al-Zahirah: from Abu Yusuf in al-Muntaqa: if two buyers purchase with an option condition, and one affirms and the other rescinds, then affirmation takes precedence. In al-Muhit: A wakil buys with an option condition for his principal, whether by his order or not; if the seller claims the principal's consent and the principal denies, then the word is the wakil's without oath, because the seller claims the option has fallen and the price is due, while he denies, and no oath because the claim is against the principal, not the contracting party. If the principal denies, his wakil is not made to take an oath because the wakil is a deputy in rights and not a principal. If the claim of consent is against the wakil, he takes an oath because the claim is directed at him. If he establishes evidence of the principal's consent, it is accepted because the wakil is a representative for the principal. The author's indication that stipulating for another is stipulating for himself means: if one orders him to sell his property with an option condition for himself, and he sells and stipulates it for the principal, he has not violated [instructions]; conversely, he violates [instructions]. He ordered a sale that transfers ownership without his consent, and the agent should have no opinion or discretion; the opinion and discretion belong to the principal originally and to him as a follower. What he did was the opposite. If he stipulates the option for the principal and then he [i.e., the wakil] affirms the sale, it is binding on him but not on the principal, and the principal's option remains such that if he affirms, it is for him; and if he rescinds, it is binding on the wakil, because the option was established for the principal by stipulation, so it is like the option of defect when established by the contract. If the wakil in a purchase finds a defect in the sold item and accepts it, it is effective between him and the seller, while the seller's option remains as it was; if the seller accepts it, it binds him; if he rejects it, it binds the wakil. His statement: 'And the seller's option remains due to the buyer's defect.' His statement: 'Thus the effect of corruption' as in al-Mi'raj.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the chapter of khiyar al-shart. The author explains the rule when both the buyer and seller have an option condition and they both exercise their rights simultaneously: one rescinds and the other affirms. The ruling is that the rescission (faskh) takes precedence over the affirmation (ijaza) because rescission is stronger—an affirmed contract can still be rescinded, but a rescinded contract cannot be affirmed. This is based on rational reasoning (istihsan) and is supported by the Hidayah. An objection is raised citing al-Mabsut: the rescinded contract is itself subject to another rescission (mutual cancellation), which is effectively an affirmation. The commentator responds via al-Mi'raj that this is not truly an affirmation but a new contract. The passage then discusses an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the act of a wakil (agent) versus the principal: Muhammad al-Shaybani gives precedence to the principal's act, while Abu Yusuf considers both acts. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is the one in the book, i.e., Abu Yusuf's, as authenticated by Qadi Khan. The discussion extends to cases of option stipulation by a wakil, claims of consent, and the analogy of the option of defect.

Key Terms
الفسخ (al-faskh): Rescission of a contract by exercising an option during the option period.
الإجازة (al-ijāzah): Affirmation or acceptance of a contract, confirming it as binding.
الوكيل (al-wakīl): An agent who acts on behalf of a principal in a contractual matter.
الخيار (al-khiyār): An option to confirm or rescind a contract within a specified time or under specific conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if both the buyer and seller have khiyar al-shart and one rescinds while the other affirms, which takes precedence?
A) The affirmation takes precedence.
B) The rescission takes precedence.
C) The contract is void.
D) Neither matters.

Key Takeaway
When both parties have khiyar al-shart and act oppositely, the rescission (faskh) prevails over affirmation (ijaza), and in agency contexts, Abu Yusuf's view that both acts are considered is the mufta bihi.

General Rule for Simultaneous Transactions from Two Agents
Explaining the rule when two agents act simultaneously in khiyar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for conflicting simultaneous transactions and apply the ranking to determine which contract prevails.

Core Idea
When two transactions conflict, the stronger one prevails — sale beats marriage, gift beats lease, except equal gifts split.

In Hanafi contract law, what happens when two agents independently contract with the same subject? This lesson clarifies the rule for simultaneous acts from two agents, especially unauthorized ones (fuduli). The key principle is that the stronger transaction takes effect, and the author provides a ranking.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agents and their roles
Determine whether the actors are principals, authorized deputies (wakil), or unauthorized (fuduli). The rule differs accordingly.
For principal and wakil, see the earlier discussion.
2
Check if the acts are simultaneous
The rule applies only when both acts occur at the same time, not sequentially. If one precedes, it typically takes full effect.
3
For fuduli: verify approval
Unauthorized acts are suspended pending approval by the owner. Only if both are approved does the conflict arise.
If only one is approved, it takes effect.
4
Apply the ranking of transactions
If both are approved, the stronger contract prevails. Use the ranking: sale > marriage, sale > gift (except gift without invalidation of joint ownership equals sale), gift/pledge > lease.
If equal strength (e.g., two sales), split half; if two marriages, both void.
5
Determine the final outcome
The weaker contract is void. The stronger contract takes full effect on the entire subject.
No partial validity for the weaker.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فكذا هذا؛ كذا في المحيط. ثم اعلم أن التصرفين إذا صدرا معاً فقد علم الحكم في باب الخيار، وأما تصرف الموكل مع تصرف الوكيل فظاهر ما قدمناه أنه إن كان الوكيل أصيلاً في الحقوق نفذ كل منهما في النصف، وإن كان نائباً فيها نفذ واحد لا على التعيين. وأما إذا صدرا من فضوليين فلا كلام في التوقف على إجازة من له الإجازة وإنما الكلام فيما لو أجيزا قالوا: يثبت الأقوى فلو باع فضولي وزوج آخر ترجح البيع فتصير مملوكة لا زوجة، ولو استويا فإن كانا نكاحين بطلا وإن كانا بيعين تنصف والبيع أقوى من الهبة والإجازة والرهن والنكاح إلا هبة لا تبطل بالشيوع فإنهما سواء والهبة والرهن أقوى من الإجارة وسيأتي في بيع الفضولي يقية مسائله إن شاء الله تعالى.
Thus this; as in al-Muhit. Then know that if two acts occur simultaneously, the ruling in the chapter of option has been learned. As for the act of the principal with the act of the wakil, it is apparent from what we have presented that if the wakil is a principal in rights, each takes effect in half; if he is a deputy, one takes effect indeterminately. If they are from two unauthorized agents (fuduliyyan), there is no discussion about staying pending acceptance, but if both are accepted, they said: the stronger is established. So if an unauthorized agent sells and another [unauthorized agent] marries, the sale is preferred, making her owned not a wife. If they are equal, if both are marriage contracts they are void; if both are sales, they are divided half. Sale is stronger than gift, acceptance, pledge, and marriage, except a gift that is not invalidated by joint ownership, for they are equal. Gift and pledge are stronger than lease. The remaining issues of sale by an unauthorized agent will come, God willing.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the general principle when two transactions are performed simultaneously. It builds on the earlier discussion of khiyar. The author summarizes: if a principal and his wakil both act, the outcome depends on whether the wakil is considered a principal in rights (i.e., having full authority) or merely a deputy. In the first case, each act takes effect in half; in the second, only one takes effect but we do not know which. For two unauthorized agents (fuduli), their acts are suspended pending acceptance by the owner. If both are accepted, the stronger transaction prevails. For example, if one sells a female slave and another marries her, the sale takes precedence, making her owned property rather than a wife. If both transactions are of equal strength, such as two sales, they are split half. The passage ranks transactions by strength: sale is stronger than gift, acceptance (of a gift), pledge, and marriage, except that a gift that does not invalidate joint ownership is equal to sale. Gift and pledge are stronger than lease. This ranking determines which contract takes effect when they conflict simultaneously.

Key Terms
الفضولي (al-fuḍūliyy): An unauthorized agent who acts without authority; the contract is suspended pending approval.
التصرفين (al-taṣarrufayn): Two legal acts or transactions, such as a sale and a marriage, occurring simultaneously.
النائب (al-nā'ib): Deputy: one who acts on behalf of another without being a principal in rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an unauthorized agent sells a female slave and another unauthorized agent marries her, which transaction takes precedence?
A) The marriage.
B) The sale.
C) Both are void.
D) They are combined.

Key Takeaway
When two concurrent transactions conflict, the stronger contract prevails, with sale being strongest and lease weakest.

Conditions for Validity of Khiyar al-Shart in Multiple Items
Ruling with proof on conditions for khiyar al-shart in multiple-item sales.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid sale when multiple items are sold with an option in one, and apply them to distinguish valid from invalid scenarios.

Core Idea
A sale with an option in one of multiple items requires apportioned price and specified item; otherwise it is invalid due to ignorance.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling in khiyar al-shart when the sold item is multiple (e.g., two slaves). The Hanafi school lays out four scenarios, only one of which is valid. The key is that the option item is treated as outside the contract, so the remaining item must be clearly defined. We will explore the conditions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the rule
The act is selling two slaves with an option in one. The rule: valid only if price is apportioned and the option item is specified.
2
Understand the four scenarios
Validity in one (both apportioned and specified), invalidity in three (missing either or both).
3
Grasp the principle
The option item is like outside the contract, so the remaining sold item must be known. Ignorance (jahala) invalidates.
4
Compare with the qinn+mudabbar case
Sale of a freeborn slave with a mudabbar without apportionment is valid because the impediment is only in meaning, not wording.
5
Apply to extensions
Death of one item before acceptance, partial rescission, and the role of qimiyy items.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن باع عبدين على أنه بالخيار في أحدهما إن فصل وعين صح وإلا فلا) شروع في بيان ما إذا كان المبيع متعدداً. وحاصلها أنها رباعية فالصحة في واحدة وهو ما إذا فصل له ثمن كل منهما وعين من فيه الخيار منهما لأن المبيع معلوم والثمن معلوم وقبول العقد الذي فيه الخيار وإن كان شرطاً لانعقاده في الآخر ولكن هذا غير مفسد للعقد لكونه محلاً للبيع كما إذا جمع بين قن ومدبر والفساد في ثلاثة الأولى إذا لم يفصل الثمن ولم يعين محل الخيار لجهالتهما. الثانية فصل ولم يعين محله لجهالة المبيع. والثالثة عين محله ولم يفصل الثمن لجهالة الثمن. والأصل فيه أن الذي فيه الخيار كالخارج عن العقد إذ العقد الخيار لا ينعقد مع في حق الحكم فبقي الداخل فيه أحدهما وهو غير معلوم. وإنما جاز البيع في القن إذا ضم إلى مدبر أو مكاتب أو أم ولد وبيعا صفقة وإن لم يفصل الثمن على الأصح لأن المانع من حكم العقد فيما نحن فيه مقارن للعقد لفظاً ومعنى فأثر الفساد، وفيما ذكر المانع مقارن معنى لا لفظاً لدخولهم في البيع حتى لو قضى به قاض يجوز لكن لم يثبت الحكم لحق محترم واجب الصيانة فأثر الفساد ؛ كذا في المعراج . وفي ضم أم الولد والمكاتب إلى المدبر في جواز القضاء ببيعه نظر ؛ فإن الصحيح أنه ينفذ في المدير فقط . وفي فتح القدير وعلى ما ذكر هنا يتفرع ما في فتاوى قاضيخان باع عبدين على أنه بالخيار فيهما وقبضهما المشتري ثم مات أحدهما لا يجوز البيع في الباقي وإن تراضيا على إجازته لأن الإجازة حينئذ بمنزلة ابتداء العقد في الباقي بالحصة. ولو قال البائع في هذه المسألة نقضت البيع في هذا أو في أحدهما كان لغواً كأنه لم يتكلم وخياره فيهما باقٍ كما كان كما لو باع عبداً واحداً وشرط الخيار لنفسه فنقض البيع في نصفه اهـ. وهكذا في الظهيرية وتقييده بالبائع اتفاقي إذ لو شرط للمشتري كان كذلك صحة وفساداً. وأراد بالعبدين القيميين احترازاً عن قيمي ومثليين إذ في القيمي الواحد لعلة فلم يؤثر الفساد اهـ. وهو الذي في المعراج فما هنا من تصحيف النساخ. قوله : (وأراد بالعبدين القيميين) أي أراد المصنف. قال في النهر والظاهر أنهما أي القيمين ليسا بقيد إذ لو كانا مثليين أو
His statement: 'And whoever sells two slaves on the condition that he has the option in one of them, if he separates [the price] and specifies [which], it is valid; otherwise no.' He begins explaining when the sold item is multiple. The summary is that it is fourfold: validity in one, which is when he separates the price for each and specifies the one with the option, because the sold item is known and the price is known, and accepting the contract that includes the option, though a condition for its conclusion in the other, does not corrupt the contract because it is a locus for sale, like combining a freeborn slave and a mudabbar. Invalidity is in three: first, if he does not separate the price and does not specify the locus of the option due to ignorance of both; second, if he separates but does not specify the locus due to ignorance of the sold item; third, if he specifies the locus but does not separate the price due to ignorance of the price. The principle is that the one with the option is like it is outside the contract, since an option contract does not take effect with [the option] in terms of legal effect, so the one included is unspecified. However, the sale of a freeborn slave is valid when combined with a mudabbar, mukatib, or umm walad, sold as a lot even without separating the price, according to the soundest view, because the impediment to the legal effect in our case is concurrent with the contract in wording and meaning, so it has the effect of corruption; while in the mentioned case, the impediment is concurrent in meaning only, not wording, because they are included in the sale, so if a judge ruled on it, it would be permissible, but the ruling is not established due to a protected right that must be safeguarded, so it has the effect of corruption; thus in al-Mi'raj. Regarding including umm walad and mukatib with mudabbar in the permissibility of a judge's ruling on the sale: there is consideration; the correct view is that it takes effect only on the mudabbar. In Fath al-Qadir, based on what is mentioned here, follows from the fatwas of Qadi Khan: if someone sells two slaves with an option in both, and the buyer receives them, then one dies, the sale is not valid for the remaining one even if they both agree to accept it, because acceptance then is like initiating a new contract for the remaining portion. If the seller says in this case: 'I rescind the sale in this one' or 'in one of them,' it is void as if he did not speak, and his option remains in both as before, like if he sold a single slave and stipulated an option for himself and then rescinded half of it. Thus in al-Zahirah. The restriction to the seller is incidental; if it were stipulated for the buyer, it would be the same in validity and invalidity. He intended by 'two slaves' the qimiyy (valued) items, to exclude qimiyy and mithliy (fungible) items, because in a single qimiyy, due to a cause, corruption does not take effect. That is in al-Mi'raj; what is here is a scribal error. His statement: 'And he intended by two slaves the qimiyy' means the author intended. Al-Nahr said: apparently, the two qimiyy are not a restriction, because if they were mithliy or...
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof on khiyar al-shart when the sold item consists of multiple items (e.g., two slaves). The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states: if someone sells two slaves on condition that he has the option to rescind in one of them, the sale is valid only if he apportions the price for each and specifies which one is subject to the option; otherwise, the sale is invalid. The commentator explains that there are four scenarios: only one is valid (apportioned and specified); three are invalid (no apportion and no specify; apportion but no specify; specify but no apportion). The reason is ignorance (jahala) of the sold item or price. The principle is that the item with the option is treated as if it is outside the contract, leaving the other unspecified. An analogy is drawn with selling a freeborn slave together with a mudabbar (a slave whose freedom is tied to the owner's death) without separate prices, which is valid because the mudabbar's freedom is not concurrent. The text also discusses extensions: if both slaves are optioned and one dies, the sale fails; rescission of part is void; and the restriction to qimiyy items is clarified. The passage includes references to al-Mi'raj, Fath al-Qadir, and Qadi Khan.

Key Terms
المبيع (al-mabīʿ): The item(s) being sold; in this passage, multiple items like two slaves.
القيميون (al-qimiyyūn): Items that are valued individually (qimiyy), as opposed to fungibles (mithliyy). The text says the ruling applies to qimiyy items.
المدبر (al-mudabbar): A slave whose freedom is deferred to the owner's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two conditions for a valid sale of two slaves with an option in one of them?
A) The option must be for the buyer and the slaves must be of the same type.
B) The price must be apportioned and the option item must be specified.
C) The buyer must pay full price immediately and the seller must waive the option.
D) The slaves must be of equal value and one must be mudabbar.

Key Takeaway
For khiyar al-shart in multiple items, the Hanafi school requires apportionment of price and specification of the option item to avoid ignorance.
