Validity of Khiyar al-Ta'yin and the Limit of Three
Ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin with istihsan justification and Zufar's qiyas objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin, distinguish between the istihsan and qiyas arguments, and apply the rule to limit of three items.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-ta'yin is valid for up to three items because need is satisfied and ignorance does not lead to dispute.

This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi dispute over khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification). While strict analogy (qiyas) would invalidate the option for any number due to uncertainty, the Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa, permits it for up to three items based on istihsan (juristic preference) grounded in need. We will examine the arguments and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
1. State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: khiyar al-ta'yin is valid when the sale involves up to three items (e.g., one of two slaves, one of three cloths). The option may be for the seller or buyer.
The text explicitly states: 'وصح خيار التعيين فيما دون الأربعة' (the option of specification is valid for less than four).
2
2. Identify the opponent and their view
Zufar holds that the option is invalid for any number, including three, based on qiyas (analogy) because the sold item is unknown (jahalah) just as with four items.
Zufar's view is a minority opinion within the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi is the majority view.
3
3. Follow the opponent's proof
Zufar's qiyas: The invalidity of khiyar al-ta'yin with four items is due to ignorance of the sold item. The same ignorance exists with three, so the ruling should be identical.
"والقياس الفساد كالأربعة لجهالة المبيع" (Analogy would require invalidity as with four due to ignorance of the sold item).
4
4. Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses istihsan: The need (hajah) for this option is real—e.g., buyer wants to choose the best among similar items. Three items cover the typical range (good, medium, poor). Ignorance in three does not lead to dispute because the option holder alone chooses; with four the need is not increased and dispute may arise.
"وجه الاستحسان أن شرع الخيار للحاجة إلى دفع الغبن ليختار ما هو الأرفق والأوفق والحاجة إلى هذا النوع من البيع متحققة" (The basis of istihsan is that the option was legislated due to need to avoid deception).
5
5. Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: According to the Hanafi view, a sale of three items with khiyar al-ta'yin is valid and the option is enforceable. According to Zufar, it would be invalid.
The dispute has no effect on four or more items, as both agree the option is invalid there.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا شرط الخيار في نصفه مطلقاً، يصح وفي المثليين كذلك لعدم التفاوت كما ذكره الشارح اه قوله : (وصح خيار التعيين فيما دون ا أن الأربعة) وهو أحد العبدين أو الثلاثة أو أحد يبيع الثوبين أو الثلاثة على أن يأخذ المشتري واحداً والقياس الفساد كالأربعة لجهالة المبيع وهو قول زفر. وجه الاستحسان أن شرع الخيار للحاجة إلى دفع الغبن ليختار ما هو الأرفق والأوفق والحاجة إلى هذا النوع من البيع متحققة لأنه يحتاج إلى اختيار من يثق به أو إختيار من يشتريه لأجله ولا يمكنه البائع من الحمل إليه إلا بالبيع فكان في معنى ما ورد به الشرع غير أن هذه تندفع بالثلاث لوجود الجيد والوسط والرديء فيها والجهالة لا تفضي إلى المنازعة في الثلاثة لتعيين من ! له الخيار، وكذا في الأربعة إلا أن الحاجة إليها غير متحققة والرخصة ثبوتها بالحاجة، وكون الجهالة موجودة غير مفضية إلى المنازعة فلا يثبت بأحدهما. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان للبائع أو للمشتري وهو المذكور في المأذون وهو الأصح ؛ ذكره في شرح التلخيص . وفي جامع الفصولين : يجوز خيار التعيين في جانب البائع كما يجوز في جانب المشتري اهـ. وفي الظهيرية وللبائع أن يلزم أيهما شاء على المشتري، فإن هلك أحدهما في يد البائع فله أن يلزمه الباقي لا الهالك، ولو حدث في أحدهما عيب في يد البائع فله أن يلزمه السليم، وليس له أن يلزمه المعيب إلا برضا المشتري، فإن ألزمه المعيب ولم يرض به ليس له أن يلزمه الآخر بعد ذلك، ولو قبضهما المشتري وخيار التعيين للبائع فهلك فالبيان بحاله اهـ . وأما إذا كان الخيار للمشتري فالبيع لازم في أحدهما إلا أن يكون . معه خيار شرط وما هو مبيع مضمون بالثمن وغير المبيع أمانة، فلو اشترى ثلاثة أثواب وعين لكل ثمناً على أن له خيار التعيين فاحترق ثوبان ونصف الثالث رد النصف الباقي ولا شيء عليه من ضمان النصف المحترق وضمن نصف ثمن المحترقين ولو كان ثوبان فاحترق نصف كل معاً رد أيهما شاء بغير ضمان وضمن ثمن الآخر، ولو احترق أحدهما ونصف الآخر لزمه ثمن المحترق لتعينه مبيعاً الآخر بغير ضمان ويسقط خيار التعيين بما يسقط به خيار الشرط . وإذا بيع أحدهما أو هلك تعين هو مبيعاً والآخر أمانة، ولو هلكا معاً ضمن نصف ثمن كل واحد منهما، ولو اختلفا في الهالك أوّلاً تحالفا على العلم على قول الإمام الأول ثم رجع إلى قوله ورد يصح مع مع يرد على ما التفصيل التفصيل أحدهما مثلياً والآخر قيمياً وفصل وعين فالحكم كذلك فيما ينبغي اهـ . قلت : وهذا لا قاله الشارح هنا من كونه قيداً احترازياً إذ المراد الاحتراز عما عدا القيميين لصحته والتعيين وبدونهما ولذا قال : مطلقاً لأنه في القيميين لا يصح بدونهما فعلم أنه والتعيين يصح في القيميين وغيرهما فتدبر نعم ينبغي تقييد المثليين بما إذا كانا من جنس واحد إذا لو اختلفا كبر وشعير صارا كالقيميين في اشتراط التفصيل والتعيين ليحصل العلم بالثمن والمبيع تأمل. قوله: (وللبائع أن يلزم الخ) أي إذا كان خيار التعيين مشروطاً له قوله : (ويسقط خيار التعيين بما
When the option is stipulated in half of it absolutely, it is valid, and in the case of two mithliy (fungible items) likewise because there is no disparity, as the commentator mentioned. His saying: (And the option of specification is valid for less than four) meaning one of the two slaves or three, or one who sells two cloths or three on condition that the buyer takes one; analogy would require invalidity as with four due to ignorance of the sold item, and this is the opinion of Zufar. The basis of istihsan is that the option was legislated due to the need to avoid deception, so that he may choose what is more suitable and agreeable, and the need for this type of sale is real because he needs to choose someone he trusts or choose for someone he buys for, and the seller cannot bring it to him except by sale, so it is in the meaning of what the Law has brought; however, this need is satisfied with three because it includes good, medium, and bad, and the ignorance does not lead to dispute in three for the one who has the option, and similarly in four except that the need for it is not real, and concessions are established by need, and the existence of ignorance that does not lead to dispute, so it is not established. He (the author) gave it absolutely, so it includes whether the option is for the seller or the buyer, and this is mentioned in al-Ma'dhun and it is the soundest; mentioned in Sharh al-Talkhis. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: the option of specification is permissible on the side of the seller as it is permissible on the side of the buyer. And in al-Zahiriyyah: the seller may oblige whichever he wishes upon the buyer; if one of them is destroyed in the seller's hand, he may oblige the remaining one, not the destroyed one; if a defect occurs in one in the seller's hand, he may oblige the sound one; he may not oblige the defective one except with the buyer's consent; if he obliges the defective one and the buyer does not consent, he may not then oblige the other afterwards; if the buyer takes possession of both and the option of specification is for the seller and then destruction occurs, the statement remains as it is. And if the option is for the buyer, the sale is binding in one of them unless there is a stipulated option with it; what is sold is guaranteed by the price, and what is not sold is a trust. If he buys three cloths and specifies a price for each on condition that he has the option of specification, and two cloths and half of the third burn, he returns the remaining half and owes nothing for the guarantee of the burned half, and he guarantees half the price of the burned two. And if there were two cloths and half of each burned together, he returns whichever he wishes without guarantee and guarantees the price of the other. And if one burned and half of the other, he owes the price of the burned one because it has become determined as sold, and the other without guarantee. And the option of specification is nullified by whatever nullifies the stipulated option. And if one of them is sold or destroyed, it becomes determined as sold, and the other is a trust. And if both are destroyed together, he guarantees half the price of each. And if they disagree about which was destroyed first, they both take an oath on knowledge according to the first imam's opinion, then he retracted to his saying... and it is valid with... detail, one being mithli and the other qimi, and he separates and specifies, the ruling is likewise as appropriate. I say: this is not what the commentator said here about it being a restrictive condition, for the intent is to exclude other than qimiyyin for its validity with specification and without them, hence he said absolutely, because in qimiyyin it is not valid without them, so it is known that specification is valid in qimiyyin and others, so ponder. Yes, it is appropriate to restrict mithliy to when they are of the same genus, for if they differ like wheat and barley, they become like qimiyyin in requiring separation and specification for knowledge of price and sold item, reflect. His saying: (and the seller may oblige...) meaning when the option of specification is stipulated for him. His saying: (and the option of specification is nullified by...)
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage deals with khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification) in sales. It begins by stating that the option is valid for up to three items, not four. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) contrary to qiyas (analogy), which would invalidate it for any number due to ignorance of the specific item. The istihsan reasoning cites the need (hajah) for this type of sale—to allow a buyer to choose the best or most suitable item, or for a seller to facilitate a purchase for someone else. The need is satisfied with three items (good, medium, poor); with four, the need is not pressing and the ignorance may lead to dispute. The option is valid for both buyer and seller, as the author states absolutely. The passage then details the effects: if the option is for the seller, he can force any item on the buyer; if one is destroyed or defective, he can oblige the remaining or sound item, but not the defective without consent. If the option is for the buyer, the sale is binding on one item at his selection, and the other items are held as trust. Detailed scenarios of partial destruction and liability are given. The passage ends with a note that the restriction to qimiyy (unique) items is not intended; the rule applies to mithliy (fungible) items of the same genus, but if they differ, they require separation and specification like qimiyy items. The option is nullified by the same factors that nullify khiyar al-shart.

Key Terms
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): A contractual option giving the buyer or seller the right to specify which of multiple items will be the final subject of the sale within a fixed period.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that abandons strict analogy (qiyas) for a more equitable ruling based on need, custom, or public interest.
قيمي (qimi): A non-fungible good of unique value, requiring specification in sale; its loss is compensated by assessment (qimah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does istihsan permit khiyar al-ta'yin for up to three items but not four according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because three items provide the necessary variety (good, medium, poor) and the need is met without leading to dispute.
B) Because the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) specifically mentioned three items in a hadith.
C) Because four items would make the price too high for the buyer.
D) Because Zufar's qiyas requires invalidity for any number, so the Hanafi side chose three as a compromise.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-ta'yin is valid for up to three items in Hanafi fiqh, based on istihsan due to need, and the option is enforceable for both buyer and seller.

Validity of Khiyar al-Ta'yin: Istihsan Overriding Qiyas
Explaining the ruling on option of specification via istihsan and responding to qiyas-based objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin, explain the role of istihsan, and identify the conditions under which it is valid.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-ta'yin is valid by istihsan for ≤3 items, despite qiyas requiring invalidity due to ignorance.

The option of specification allows a party to choose from a limited set of items after concluding a sale. While qiyas would invalidate this due to uncertainty (jahalah), the Hanafi school recognizes a genuine need (hajah) and applies istihsan to uphold it for up to three items. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and the intra-madhhab disagreement with Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the operative ruling
The matn states: 'The option of specification is valid for less than four.' This is the rule to be justified.
2
Recognize the qiyas objection
By qiyas on the case of four or more items, the sale would be invalid due to ignorance of the object (gharar). This is Zufar's view.
Zufar is a Hanafi scholar known for strict adherence to qiyas.
3
Understand istihsan as the basis
Istihsan overrides qiyas because of a genuine need (hajah): the buyer may need to choose a trusted person or buy for another, and ignorance does not lead to dispute when the option is given for a limited number (≤3).
The Hanafi school considers istihsan a primary source of law.
4
Note Zufar's position and the Hanafi response
Zufar holds the sale invalid by qiyas. The Hanafi response is that istihsan is stronger because need justifies the concession, and the limited scope prevents harm.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the validity of khiyar al-ta'yin by istihsan, as stated in the matn and commentary.
The fatwa follows this view.

إذا شرط الخيار في نصفه مطلقاً، يصح وفي المثليين كذلك لعدم التفاوت كما ذكره الشارح اه قوله : (وصح خيار التعيين فيما دون الأربعة) وهو أحد العبدين أو الثلاثة أو أحد الثوبين أو الثلاثة على أن يأخذ المشتري واحداً والقياس الفساد كالأربعة لجهالة المبيع وهو قول زفر. وجه الاستحسان أن شرع الخيار للحاجة إلى دفع الغبن ليختار ما هو الأرفق والأوفق والحاجة إلى هذا النوع من البيع متحققة لأنه يحتاج إلى اختيار من يثق به أو اختيار من يشتريه لأجله ولا يمكنه البائع من الحمل إليه إلا بالبيع فكان في معنى ما ورد به الشرع غير أن هذه تندفع بالثلاث لوجود الجيد والوسط والرديء فيها والجهالة لا تفضي إلى المنازعة في الثلاثة لتعيين من له الخيار، وكذا في الأربعة إلا أن الحاجة إليها غير متحققة والرخصة ثبوتها بالحاجة، وكون الجهالة موجودة غير مفضية إلى المنازعة فلا يثبت بأحدهما. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان للبائع أو للمشتري وهو المذكور في المأذون وهو الأصح؛ ذكره في شرح التلخيص. وفي جامع الفصولين: يجوز خيار التعيين في جانب البائع كما يجوز في جانب المشتري اهـ. وفي الظهيرية: وللبائع أن يلزم أيهما شاء على المشتري، فإن هلك أحدهما في يد البائع فله أن يلزمه الباقي لا الهالك، ولو حدث في أحدهما عيب في يد البائع فله أن يلزمه السليم، وليس له أن يلزمه المعيب إلا برضا المشتري، فإن ألزمه المعيب ولم يرض به ليس له أن يلزمه الآخر بعد ذلك، ولو قبضهما المشتري وخيار التعيين للبائع فهلك فالبيان بحاله اهـ. وأما إذا كان الخيار للمشتري فالبيع لازم في أحدهما إلا أن يكون معه خيار شرط وما هو مبيع مضمون بالثمن وغير المبيع أمانة، فلو اشترى ثلاثة أثواب وعين لكل ثمناً على أن له خيار التعيين فاحترق ثوبان ونصف الثالث رد النصف الباقي ولا شيء عليه من ضمان النصف المحترق وضمن نصف ثمن المحترقين ولو كان ثوبان فاحترق نصف كل معاً رد أيهما شاء بغير ضمان وضمن ثمن الآخر، ولو احترق أحدهما ونصف الآخر لزمه ثمن المحترق لتعينه مبيعاً الآخر بغير ضمان ويسقط خيار التعيين بما يسقط به خيار الشرط. وإذا بيع أحدهما أو هلك تعين هو مبيعاً والآخر أمانة، ولو هلكا معاً ضمن نصف ثمن كل واحد منهما، ولو اختلفا في الهالك أولاً تحالفا على العلم على قول الإمام الأول ثم رجع إلى قوله ورد يصح مع مع يرد على ما التفصيل التفصيل أحدهما مثلياً والآخر قيمياً وفصل وعين فالحكم كذلك فيما ينبغي اهـ. قلت: وهذا لا قاله الشارح هنا من كونه قيداً احترازياً إذ المراد الاحتراز عما عدا القيميين لصحته والتعيين وبدونهما ولذا قال: مطلقاً لأنه في القيميين لا يصح بدونهما فعلم أنه والتعيين يصح في القيميين وغيرهما فتدبر نعم ينبغي تقييد المثليين بما إذا كانا من جنس واحد إذا لو اختلفا كبر وشعير صارا كالقيميين في اشتراط التفصيل والتعيين ليحصل العلم بالثمن والمبيع تأمل.
If he stipulates the option in half of it absolutely, it is valid, and similarly in fungible items due to lack of disparity, as the commentator mentioned. End. His statement: (And the option of specification is valid for less than four) meaning one of two slaves, or three, or one of two garments, or three, on condition that the buyer takes one. The analogy is invalidity, as with four, due to ignorance of the object sold, and this is the view of Zufar. The basis of istihsan is that the option was legislated due to need to prevent harm, so that one chooses what is most beneficial and suitable. The need for this type of sale is real because he needs to choose someone he trusts or chooses for someone he buys for, and the seller cannot let him take them except through sale, so it is analogous to what the Law has brought. However, this need is met with three because there is good, medium, and poor among them, and ignorance does not lead to dispute in three because the one with the option specifies. Likewise in four, but the need is not real, and concession is established by need, and the existence of ignorance that does not lead to dispute does not establish it by either one. He made it absolute, so it includes whether the option is for the seller or the buyer, and this is mentioned in al-Ma'dhun and it is the most correct; mentioned in Sharh al-Talkhis. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: Option of specification is valid on the seller's side as it is on the buyer's side, end. And in al-Zahiriyyah: The seller may oblige whichever he wishes upon the buyer. If one of them perishes in the seller's hand, he may oblige the remaining one, not the perished. If a defect occurs in one of them in the seller's hand, he may oblige the sound one, and he may not oblige the defective one except with the buyer's consent. If he obliges the defective one and the buyer does not consent, he may not afterward oblige the other. If the buyer takes possession of both and the option of specification is for the seller, and they perish, the declaration remains, end. As for when the option is for the buyer, the sale is binding in one of them unless there is an option of stipulation with it. What is sold is guaranteed by the price, and what is not sold is a trust. So if he buys three garments and designates a price for each on condition that he has the option of specification, and two and a half garments are burned, he returns the remaining half and owes nothing for the guarantee of the burned half, and he guarantees half the price of the two burned. If there were two garments and half of each burns together, he returns whichever he wishes without guarantee and guarantees the price of the other. If one of them and half of the other burn, he owes the price of the burned one because it is determined as sold, the other without guarantee. The option of specification is nullified by whatever nullifies the option of stipulation. If one of them is sold or perishes, it becomes determined as sold and the other is a trust. If both perish together, he guarantees half the price of each. If they differ about which perished first, they take an oath based on knowledge according to the first imam's statement, then he retracted to his statement. It is [؟] valid with [؟] and is [؟] returns to what [؟] detail detail one is fungible and the other non-fungible, and he specifies and designates, so the ruling is likewise in what is appropriate, end. I say: This is not said by the commentator here as a restrictive qualification, for the intent is restriction to other than non-fungibles for its validity with specification and without them. Hence he said 'absolutely' because in non-fungibles it is not valid without them. So you know that it and specification are valid in non-fungibles and others, so ponder. Yes, it is appropriate to restrict fungibles to when they are of the same type, because if they differ like wheat and barley, they become like non-fungibles in requiring detail and specification to attain knowledge of the price and sold object. Reflect.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification). The commentator begins by stating that if the option is stipulated in half of the items, it is valid absolutely, and similarly in fungible items (mithlayn) because there is no disparity. He then cites the matn: 'The option of specification is valid for less than four.' This means one can buy one of two slaves or one of two/three garments with the option to choose later. By qiyas (analogy), such a sale would be invalid due to ignorance of the specific object, as in the case of four or more, and this is Zufar's view. However, the Hanafi school prefers istihsan (juristic preference) based on need (hajah). The need is real: the buyer may need to choose a trustworthy person or buy for someone else, and the seller cannot hand over the items without a sale. This need is met with three items (good, medium, poor) because ignorance does not lead to dispute when the buyer has the right to specify. For four items, the need is not as strong, so the concession is not extended. The option is valid for both buyer and seller, as stated in several sources. The commentator then details various scenarios: if the option is for the seller, he can enforce whichever he wants; if one is destroyed, he enforces the remaining; if a defect occurs, he enforces the sound one unless the buyer agrees to the defective. If the option is for the buyer, the sale is binding in one, but the buyer can choose. Detailed rules about destruction or sale of the items are given: the buyer guarantees half the price in certain cases. The option of specification is lost by the same factors that nullify the option of stipulation. Finally, the commentator discusses a nuance: the ruling applies to fungibles of the same type; if they differ (e.g., wheat and barley), they are treated like non-fungibles requiring specification and detail. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of combining qiyas with istihsan based on custom and need.

Key Terms
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): An option granted to the buyer or seller in a sale of one of multiple items to specify which item is the subject of the sale within a stipulated period
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference overriding qiyas (analogy) in favor of a ruling that better serves human welfare or is based on a stronger evidence
مثليان (mithlayn): Two items that are fungible (same type and quality, like wheat and wheat), where replacing one with another is feasible

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the maximum number of items for which khiyar al-ta'yin is valid?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Unlimited

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-ta'yin is valid by istihsan for up to three items, overriding the qiyas-based objection of ignorance.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
10 min
Applications of Khiyar al-Ta'yin: Buyer vs Seller, Destruction, Defects, and Fungibles
Detailing specific applications of khiyar al-ta'yin including buyer/seller options, destruction, defects, and fungibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the detailed rules of khiyar al-ta'yin when the option is for the seller or buyer, and determine the effect of destruction, defects, and the distinction between fungibles and non-fungibles.

Core Idea
The specifics of khiyar al-ta'yin depend on who holds the option, what happens to the items, and whether they are fungible.

Beyond the basic validity, the Hanafi fiqh literature provides detailed scenarios: if the option belongs to the seller, he can enforce any remaining item after destruction; if to the buyer, different rules apply. The type of item (fungible or non-fungible) also affects the conditions. This lesson explores these applications from the passage.

Guided Path
1
Determine who holds the option
The passage gives separate rules for khiyar al-ta'yin when it belongs to the seller and when it belongs to the buyer. Identify which party has the right to specify.
The option can be stipulated for either party.
2
Apply the rules for seller's option
If the seller has the option, he may oblige the buyer to take whichever item he (seller) chooses. If one item perishes in the seller's hand, he can oblige the remaining. If a defect occurs, he can oblige the sound one but not the defective without buyer's consent.
These rules are found in the Zahiriyya quotation.
3
Apply the rules for buyer's option
If the buyer has the option, the sale is binding in one of the items, and the buyer can choose. The items not yet chosen are trusts. Detailed rules apply to destruction: e.g., if both perish, buyer guarantees half the price of each; if one perishes, it becomes determined as the sold item.
The buyer does not bear the risk of destruction for items not chosen.
4
Distinguish between fungibles and non-fungibles
For fungibles (mithlayn) of the same type, khiyar al-ta'yin is valid without further detail. For non-fungibles (qimiyyat), specification (tafsil) and designation (ta'yin) are required at the contract to eliminate ignorance of the price and object.
If two items are of different types (e.g., wheat and barley), they are treated as non-fungibles.
5
Understand the effect of destruction and defects on the option
The option is nullified if one of the items is sold or perishes, as it becomes determined as the sold item. The remaining item becomes a trust (amanah) if not chosen. Defects affect the seller's option as noted.
The option of specification is lost by the same factors that nullify the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart).

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification). The commentator begins by stating that if the option is stipulated in half of the items, it is valid absolutely, and similarly in fungible items (mithlayn) because there is no disparity. For four items, the need is not as strong, so the concession is not extended. The option is valid for both buyer and seller, as stated in several sources. The commentator then details various scenarios: if the option is for the seller, he can enforce whichever he wants; if one is destroyed, he enforces the remaining; if a defect occurs, he enforces the sound one unless the buyer agrees to the defective. Key Terms
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): An option granted to the buyer or seller in a sale of one of multiple items to specify which item is the subject of the sale within a stipulated period
مثليان (mithlayn): Two items that are fungible (same type and quality, like wheat and wheat), where replacing one with another is feasible
قيميان (qimiyyan): Two items that are non-fungible (unique, like a cow and a sheep), where replacement is not straightforward

According to the passage, if a seller has khiyar al-ta'yin and one of the two items develops a defect in the seller's hand, what can the seller do?

D) The sale becomes void

Key Takeaway
The detailed rules of khiyar al-ta'yin protect both parties by allocating risk according to who holds the option and the nature of the items.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

8 min
Core Scenarios of Khiyar al-Ta'yin: Defects, Acts of Ownership, and Manumission
Detailed rulings on khiyar al-ta'yin scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid khiyar al-ta'yin and identify which acts (such as dyeing, selling, or manumission) determine the selection of the sold item.

Core Idea
In khiyar al-ta'yin, any act of ownership by the buyer automatically determines the sold item.

The option of specification allows a buyer to choose one of multiple items within a set period. This lesson explores the intricate scenarios that arise when either party acts during the option period, including defects, disposal, and manumission. We will see how the Hanafi school applies rules of ownership and guarantee to determine the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic rule when defects occur
Distinguish between simultaneous defect (option remains) and successive defect (first defective becomes sold item).
If both become defective at the same time, the buyer still has the option to choose.
2
Analyze acts of ownership by the buyer
If the buyer dyes one item, it becomes the sold item. If he sells both and then chooses one, the sale of that item is valid.
Dyeing is a clear act of ownership that determines specification.
3
Examine the seller's manumission
If the seller manumits both slaves, only the one returned to him is freed. If he manumits the item the buyer chose, the manumission is invalid.
The buyer's choice overrides the seller's manumission during the option period.
4
Understand the contractual requirement
The contract must explicitly include the phrase 'on condition that you take whichever you wish' (أيتهما شئت) for the option to be valid. Without it, the sale is corrupt due to ignorance of the sold object.
This requirement distinguishes khiyar al-ta'yin from a simple undefined sale.
5
Resolve the objection about death
The matn claims the option is nullified by whatever nullifies khiyar al-shart, but death nullifies khiyar al-shart while it does not nullify khiyar al-ta'yin. The commentator notes this inconsistency.
Khiyar al-ta'yin survives death, passing to the heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وللبائع أن يلزم الخ) أي إذا كان خيار التعيين مشروطاً له قوله : (ويسقط خيار التعيين بما يسقط به خيار الشرط يرد عليه أن خيار الشرط يبطل بالموت وخيار التعيين لا يسقط اهـ. ذكره في حاشية الرملي وسيأتي آخر القولة تفصيل ما يبطله عن البدائع . الثاني من أن القول للمشتري مع يمينه وبينة البائع أولى. ولو تعيبا معاً فالخيار بحاله وإن على التعاقب تعين الأول مبيعاً، وإن اختلفا في الأول فعلى ما ذكرنا، ولو باعهما المشتري ثم اختار أحدهما صح بيعه فيه، ولو صبغ المشتري أحدهما تعين هو مبيعاً ورد الآخر، ولو أعتقهما البائع عتق الذي يرد عليه وإن كان أعتق ما اختاره المشتري للبيع لم يصح إعتاقه . ولو استولدهما المشتري تعينت الأولى للبيع وضمن عقر الأخرى للبائع، ولا يثبت نسب ولدها منه لعدم الملك ويؤمر المشتري بالبيان أيتهما استولدها أولاً، فإن مات قبل البيان فخيار التعيين للورثة، فإن لم تعرف الورثة الأول منهما ضمن المشتري نصف ثمن كل واحدة منهما ونصف عقرهما للبائع ويسعيان في نصف قيمتهما للبائع وروي أن الولدين يسعيان أيضاً في نصف قيمتهما للبائع. ولو وطئهما البائع والمشتري فولدتا وادعى كل واحد منهما الولدين صدق المشتري في التي وطئها أولاً وضمن عقر الأخرى ويثبت نسب الأخرى من البائع لأنه استولد جارية نفسه ويضمن البائع عقر الأخرى للمشتري. وإن ماتا قبل البيان ولم تعلم ورثة المشتري الأول منهما لم يثبت نسب الولد من أحد لوقوع الشك وعتقوا وضمن المشتري نصف ثمن كل واحدة منهما ونصف عقرها للبائع والبائع يضمن نصف عقر كل واحدة للمشتري ويتقاصان وولاؤهم بينهما . وقيل : لا ولاء على الولدين؛ كذا في الظهيرية . ثم قال بعده ويجوز خيار التعيين في الفاسد أيضاً إلا أنها هنا ما يتعين للبيع كان مضموناً بالقيمة والباقي كما قلنا في الجائز. وإن ماتا معاً ضمن نصف قيمة كل واحد منهما، ولو أعتقهما المشتري عتق أحدهما والتعيين إليه ولو أعتق أحدهما المشتري بعينه أو باعه جاز وعليه قيمته ولا يجوز إعتاق المبهم لا من البائع ولا من المشتري لأن العتق المبهم بين المملوكين للمعتق ولم يوجد ولو أعتق البائع أحدهما بعينه ثم أعتق المشتري ذلك أو عينه للبيع أو مات فعتق البائع باطل ولو رد ذلك على البائع صح عتقه، ولو كان أعتقهما وردا عليه عتق أحدهما والتعيين إليه .اهـ. وقيدوا صورة خيار التعيين بأن يقول على أن تأخذ أيهما شئت لأنه لو لم يذكر هذه الزيادة وقال بعتك أحد هذين العبدين فقبل يكون فاسداً لجهالة المبيع، فإن قبضهما ومانا عنده ضمن نصف قيمة كل واحد منهما، وإن مات أحدهما قبل صاحبه لزمه قيمة الآخر؛ كذا في المحيط وتقدم تفاريعه ولم يذكر المؤلف خيار الشرط مع خيار التعيين للاختلاف، فقيل يشترط أن يكون فيه خيار الشرط مع خيار التعيين وهو المذكور في الجامع الصغير . قال شمس الأئمة وهو الصحيح فإذا ذكرا فله ردهما في المدة وإذا مضت لزم في أحدهما وله التعيين وقيل : لا وهو المذكور في الجامع الكبير وصححه فخر الغزي
His statement: (And the seller may oblige, etc.) meaning when the option of specification is stipulated for him. His statement: (And the option of specification is nullified by whatever nullifies the option of stipulation) is objected to because the option of stipulation is invalidated by death, while the option of specification is not nullified, end. Mentioned in Hashiyat al-Ramli. Later at the end of the statement will come details of what nullifies it from al-Bada'i. Second: The statement is that of the buyer with his oath, but the seller's evidence is preferable. If both are defective together, the option remains. If they are defective successively, the first becomes the sold item. If they differ about the first, it is as we mentioned. If the buyer sells both then chooses one, his sale of it is valid. If the buyer dyes one, it becomes the sold item and he returns the other. If the seller manumits both, the one that is returned is freed, and if he manumits what the buyer chose for sale, his manumission is not valid. If the buyer has children from them (umm walad), the first becomes the sold item, and he guarantees the 'aqr (dower) of the other to the seller, and the lineage of her child is not established due to lack of ownership. The buyer is ordered to declare which he had children from first. If he dies before declaration, the option of specification goes to the heirs. If the heirs do not know the first, the buyer guarantees half the price of each and half their 'aqr to the seller, and they (the children) also earn half their value for the seller. It is reported that the two children also earn half their value for the seller. If the seller and the buyer both have intercourse with them and they give birth, and each claims the children, the buyer is believed regarding the one he had intercourse with first, and he guarantees the 'aqr of the other, and the lineage of the other is established from the seller because he had a child from his own slave girl. The seller guarantees the 'aqr of the other to the buyer. If they die before declaration and the buyer's heirs do not know the first, the lineage of the child is not established from anyone due to doubt, and they are freed. The buyer guarantees half the price of each and half her 'aqr to the seller, and the seller guarantees half the 'aqr of each to the buyer, and they offset, and their wala' is between them. It is said: there is no wala' over the two children; thus in al-Zahiriyyah. Then he said after it: The option of specification is also valid in a corrupt sale, except that here what becomes determined as sold is guaranteed by value, and the rest as we said in the valid sale. If both perish together, he guarantees half the value of each. If the buyer manumits both, one is freed and the choice is his. If the buyer manumits one specifically or sells it, it is valid and he owes its value. It is not permissible to manumit an ambiguous slave, neither by the seller nor the buyer, because ambiguous manumission between two owned slaves is not realized. If the seller manumits one specifically, then the buyer manumits that one or designates it for sale or dies, the seller's manumission is void. If he returns that one to the seller, his manumission is valid. If he had manumitted both and they are returned to him, one is freed and the choice is his. End. They restricted the form of option of specification to saying 'on condition that you take whichever you wish,' because if he does not mention this addition and says 'I sell you one of these two slaves' and the other accepts, it is corrupt due to ignorance of the sold object. If he takes possession of both and they die in his possession, he guarantees half the value of each. If one dies before the other, he owes the value of the other; thus in al-Muhit. Its branches preceded. The author did not mention the option of stipulation together with the option of specification due to disagreement. It is said that an option of stipulation must be present with the option of specification, and this is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir. Shams al-A'imma said it is the correct view. So if both are mentioned, he may return both during the period, and when it passes, it becomes binding in one, and he has the choice to specify. It is also said: no, and this is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir and endorsed by Fakhr al-Ghazzi.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the commentary on khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification). The commentator addresses a potential objection: the matn says the option is nullified by whatever nullifies khiyar al-shart, but death nullifies khiyar al-shart while it does not nullify khiyar al-ta'yin. This is noted from the margin. Then he discusses the scenario when the option is for the buyer: the buyer's statement is taken with his oath, but the seller's evidence is stronger. If both identical items become defective, the option remains; if they become defective successively, the first to become defective is the sold item. If the buyer sells both items and then chooses one, the sale of that item is valid. If he dyes one, it becomes the sold item. If the seller manumits both, only the one that is eventually returned to the seller is freed; if the seller manumits the item the buyer chooses for sale, the manumission is invalid. Complex rules follow about cases where the buyer makes one an umm walad (concubine mother of a child): the first becomes the sold item, he must pay the dower for the other, and the lineage of her child is not established. Detailed succession rules apply if the buyer dies before declaration. If both buyer and seller have intercourse with the two slave girls and each claims paternity, the buyer is believed regarding the one he had intercourse with first, and the seller's claim about the other is accepted. If the parties die and the order is unknown, the children are freed and financial adjustments are made. The passage then moves to khiyar al-ta'yin in a corrupt sale (bay' fasid): it is still valid, but the guaranteed item is by value, not price. Various rules about manumission in this context are given. Finally, there is a dispute about whether khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) can be combined with khiyar al-ta'yin: one view (from al-Jami' al-Saghir, preferred by Shams al-A'imma) requires both options to be mentioned together; another view (from al-Jami' al-Kabir, endorsed by Fakhr al-Ghazzi) allows the option of specification without a separate stipulation. The passage is a rich collection of fiqhi scenarios demonstrating the Hanafi school's meticulous casuistry.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated by either party in a sale to have the right to rescind the contract within a specified period
الأمة الولد (umm walad): A female slave who bears a child to her master, thereby becoming free upon his death and the child is free and legitimate
البيع الفاسد (al-bay' al-fasid): A sale that is legally defective (e.g., missing a condition) but can be rectified; the contract is not void but the transaction is not lawful until corrected

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer has khiyar al-ta'yin over two items. Both items become defective, but one becomes defective first. Which item becomes the sold item?
A) The buyer may choose either item
B) The item that became defective first becomes the sold item
C) The item that became defective second becomes the sold item
D) The sale becomes void

Key Takeaway
During khiyar al-ta'yin, any unilateral act of ownership by the buyer determines the sold item, and the option is not nullified by death.

Complex Cases: Umm Walad, Corrupt Sale, and Combination with Khiyar al-Shart
Detailed rulings on khiyar al-ta'yin with umm walad, corrupt sales, and dispute on combination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on khiyar al-ta'yin when the buyer makes a slave an umm walad, and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute regarding the combination of khiyar al-ta'yin with khiyar al-shart.

Core Idea
Umm walad status during khiyar al-ta'yin determines the sold item and creates complex financial and lineage obligations.

When the buyer exercises khiyar al-ta'yin over slave girls, the stakes rise dramatically if he has children with one. This lesson unpacks the detailed Hanafi rules for such cases, including the buyer's duty to declare the first umm walad and the consequences of uncertainty. It also addresses the validity of khiyar al-ta'yin in corrupt sales and the intra-madhhab dispute on combining it with khiyar al-shart.

Guided Path
1
Understand the umm walad scenario
If the buyer makes one slave an umm walad, that slave becomes the sold item, and he must pay the dower ('aqr) for the other to the seller.
The first umm walad is determined by the order of intercourse.
2
Follow the rules for uncertainty
If the buyer dies without declaring which slave was first made umm walad, the heirs inherit the option and must determine. If they cannot, financial adjustments occur.
The buyer is ordered to declare; his silence leads to complex compensation.
3
Analyze the dual intercourse case
If both buyer and seller have intercourse with the slaves, paternity and financial claims are resolved: the buyer is believed regarding the first he had intercourse with, and the seller for the other.
Lineage is established accordingly, and both parties pay dower for the other's slave.
4
Apply khiyar al-ta'yin to a corrupt sale
When the original sale is corrupt (fasid), the option of specification remains valid, but the guarantee for the chosen item is by value (qimah) rather than price (thaman).
This shows the option's robustness even in defective contracts.
5
Evaluate the dispute on combining with khiyar al-shart
There is an intra-madhhab disagreement: one view (al-Jami' al-Saghir, Shams al-A'imma) requires khiyar al-shart to be explicitly mentioned alongside khiyar al-ta'yin for the buyer to have the right to return both items. Another view (al-Jami' al-Kabir, Fakhr al-Ghazzi) holds that khiyar al-ta'yin alone suffices.
The mufta bihi is the view requiring both options.

The commentator addresses a potential objection: the matn says the option is nullified by whatever nullifies khiyar al-shart, but death nullifies khiyar al-shart while it does not nullify khiyar al-ta'yin. This is noted from the margin. Then he discusses the scenario when the option is for the buyer: the buyer's statement is taken with his oath, but the seller's evidence is stronger. If both identical items become defective, the option remains; if they become defective successively, the first to become defective is the sold item. If the buyer sells both items and then chooses one, the sale of that item is valid. If he dyes one, it becomes the sold item. If the seller manumits both, only the one that is eventually returned to the seller is freed; if the seller manumits the item the buyer chooses for sale, the manumission is invalid. Complex rules follow about cases where the buyer makes one an umm walad (concubine mother of a child): the first becomes the sold item, he must pay the dower for the other, and the lineage of her child is not established. Detailed succession rules apply if the buyer dies before declaration. If both buyer and seller have intercourse with the two slave girls and each claims paternity, the buyer is believed regarding the one he had intercourse with first, and the seller's claim about the other is accepted. If the parties die and the order is unknown, the children are freed and financial adjustments are made. The passage then moves to khiyar al-ta'yin in a corrupt sale (bay' fasid): it is still valid, but the guaranteed item is by value, not price. Various rules about manumission in this context are given. Finally, there is a dispute about whether khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) can be combined with khiyar al-ta'yin: one view (from al-Jami' al-Saghir, preferred by Shams al-A'imma) requires both options to be mentioned together; another view (from al-Jami' al-Kabir, endorsed by Fakhr al-Ghazzi) allows the option of specification without a separate stipulation. The passage is a rich collection of fiqhi scenarios demonstrating the Hanafi school's meticulous casuistry.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated by either party in a sale to have the right to rescind the contract within a specified period
الأمة الولد (umm walad): A female slave who bears a child to her master, thereby becoming free upon his death and the child is free and legitimate
البيع الفاسد (al-bay' al-fasid): A sale that is legally defective (e.g., missing a condition) but can be rectified; the contract is not void but the transaction is not lawful until corrected

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on khiyar al-ta'yin in a corrupt sale (bay' fasid)?
A) The option is invalid because the contract is defective.
B) The option is valid, but the guarantee is by value (qimah) instead of price (thaman).
C) The option is valid with the same rules as a valid sale.
D) The option becomes an option of stipulation.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-ta'yin is robust: it remains valid even in corrupt sales and generates complex derivative rulings, and the school's preferred view requires combining it with khiyar al-shart to fully protect the buyer's rights.

Basic Scenarios in Khiyar al-Ta'yin: Defects and Acts of Determination
Listing rulings for defects, sale, dyeing, and freeing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when defects appear in both items under khiyar al-ta'yin and identify which acts by the buyer (sale, dyeing) determine the sold item.

Core Idea
In khiyar al-ta'yin, the buyer's use of one item makes it the sold item; defects do not eliminate the option.

Khiyar al-ta'yin allows a buyer to postpone specifying which item they want from a set. But what happens if the items become defective or the buyer takes an action like reselling or dyeing? This lesson explains the fiqh rulings for such situations.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the scenario
Identify what action is taken (defect, sale, dyeing, freeing) and by whom (buyer or seller).
2
Determine the ruling
For each action, state whether the option remains or which item is fixed as the sold item.
3
Understand the principle
Acts indicating choice (like dyeing) fix the item; defects do not destroy the option.
4
Apply to hypothetical
Given a scenario, apply the ruling from the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني من أن القول للمشتري مع يمينه وبينة البائع أولى. ولو تعيبا معاً فالخيار بحاله وإن على التعاقب تعين الأول مبيعاً، وإن اختلفا في الأول فعلى ما ذكرنا، ولو باعهما المشتري ثم اختار أحدهما صح بيعه فيه، ولو صبغ المشتري أحدهما تعين هو مبيعاً ورد الآخر، ولو أعتقهما البائع عتق الذي يرد عليه وإن كان أعتق ما اختاره المشتري للبيع لم يصح إعتاقه . ولو استولدهما المشتري تعينت الأولى للبيع وضمن عقر الأخرى للبائع، ولا يثبت نسب ولدها منه لعدم الملك ويؤمر المشتري بالبيان أيتهما استولدها أولاً، فإن مات قبل البيان فخيار التعيين للورثة، فإن لم تعرف الورثة الأول منهما ضمن المشتري نصف ثمن كل واحدة منهما ونصف عقرهما للبائع ويسعيان في نصف قيمتهما للبائع وروي أن الولدين يسعيان أيضاً في نصف قيمتهما للبائع. ولو وطئهما البائع والمشتري فولدتا وادعى كل واحد منهما الولدين صدق المشتري في التي وطئها أولاً وضمن عقر الأخرى ويثبت نسب الأخرى من البائع لأنه استولد جارية نفسه ويضمن البائع عقر الأخرى للمشتري. وإن ماتا قبل البيان ولم تعلم ورثة المشتري الأول منهما لم يثبت نسب الولد من أحد لوقوع الشك وعتقوا وضمن المشتري نصف ثمن كل واحدة منهما ونصف عقرها للبائع والبائع يضمن نصف عقر كل واحدة للمشتري ويتقاصان وولاؤهم بينهما . وقيل : لا ولاء على الولدين ؛ كذا في الظهيرية
The second [section]: The statement is of the buyer with his oath, and the evidence of the seller is preferable. If both become defective, the option remains as it was. If they become defective consecutively, the first one is determined as the sold item. If they differ about which was first, it is as we stated. If the buyer sells both then chooses one, his sale is valid regarding it. If the buyer dyes one, it is determined as the sold item and he returns the other. If the seller frees both, the one that is returned to him becomes free, but if he freed the one the buyer chose for sale, his freeing is invalid. If the buyer has intercourse with both, the first is determined for the sale, and he guarantees the 'uqr (dower) of the other to the seller, and the lineage of her child is not established from him due to lack of ownership. The buyer is ordered to clarify which one he first had intercourse with. If he dies before clarification, the option of specification goes to the heirs. If the heirs do not know which was first, the buyer is liable for half the price of each and half their dowers to the seller, and the two [slave women] must work for half their value for the seller. It is narrated that the two children also must work for half their value for the seller. If both the seller and buyer have intercourse with the two [slave women] and they give birth, and each claims the children, the buyer is believed regarding the one he first had intercourse with, and he guarantees the dower of the other, and the lineage of the other child is established from the seller because he had intercourse with his own slave woman, and the seller guarantees the dower of the other to the buyer. If both die before clarification and the buyer's heirs do not know which was first, the lineage of the child is not established from anyone due to doubt, and they are freed. The buyer guarantees half the price of each and half her dower to the seller, and the seller guarantees half the dower of each to the buyer, and they offset each other. Their [the children's] wala' is between them. It is said: there is no wala' upon the two children. So in al-Zahiriyya.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the second type of option: khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification). In this option, the buyer purchases two items with the right to choose one as the actual sold item. The passage enumerates various scenarios affecting which item becomes the sold item and the associated liabilities. The author presents the rulings without proofs, as this is a commentary expanding on the matn. Key scenarios include: if both items become defective, if the buyer sells both then chooses, if the buyer dyes one, if the seller frees them, if the buyer has intercourse with both (concubinage), and if both parties have intercourse. In each case, the ruling determines which item is deemed the sold item and what compensation is due. For example, if the buyer dyes one, that item automatically becomes the sold item. If the buyer has intercourse with both, the first one he had intercourse with is the sold item, and he must pay the 'uqr (dower) for the other. If he dies before clarifying, the heirs have the option. If all information is lost, complex calculations of half shares apply. This passage is from the section on khiyar al-ta'yin, which is valid only for non-fungible goods (mutafawwita) like slaves and clothes.

Key Terms
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): The option of specification: a sale of two or more items where the buyer has the right to choose one as the actual sold item within a specified period.
عقر ('uqr): The dower or compensation paid for intercourse with a slave woman whose ownership is not established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer dyes one of two garments under khiyar al-ta'yin, which garment becomes the sold item?
A) The dyed garment
B) The undyed garment
C) The buyer can still choose
D) The seller chooses

Key Takeaway
Acts that indicate the buyer's choice, like dyeing or selling, determine the sold item in khiyar al-ta'yin.

Complex Scenarios in Khiyar al-Ta'yin: Intercourse, Heirs, and Disputes
Listing rulings for intercourse, inheritance, and disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the sold item when the buyer has intercourse with slave women under khiyar al-ta'yin and apply the rules for compensation and inheritance when unknown.

Core Idea
When the buyer has intercourse with multiple slave women, the first determines the sold item; if unknown, half-shares and compensation apply.

Khiyar al-ta'yin becomes particularly complex when the items are slave women and the buyer exercises his right of concubinage. The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details rules for determining the sold item, compensating for the other (by paying 'uqr), and handling cases when the buyer dies before specifying.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts
Determine who had intercourse with which slave woman (buyer or seller) and the order.
2
Determine sequence
Order matters: the first intercourse fixes the sold item; the other requires 'uqr.
3
Apply the ruling
First intercourse fixes sold item; 'uqr owed for the other; lineage follows ownership.
4
Handle unknowns
If buyer dies without clarifying, heirs have the option; if still unknown, half-shares apply.
Half of price and half of 'uqr for each slave woman.
5
Understand the calculation
When both parties have intercourse and die, compensations are offset and children's status is disputed.
There is ikhtilaf on whether the children have wala'.

Rulings of Khiyar al-Ta'yin in Fasid Sales
Extending khiyar al-ta'yin to fasid sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissibility of khiyar al-ta'yin in fasid sales, explain the liability for market value, and apply the rulings when the objects die or are freed ambiguously.

Core Idea
In a fasid sale, khiyar al-ta'yin is valid, but the chosen item is guaranteed by its market value.

This lesson extends the concept of khiyar al-ta'yin (option to determine the object of sale) from valid sales to corrupt (fasid) sales. While the essence of the option remains, the liability shifts to market value, and specific rules apply to the scenarios of death and freeing. Understanding these nuances is crucial for correctly applying the option in imperfect transactions.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the permissibility
Identify that khiyar al-ta'yin is permitted (jā'iz) in fasid sales, just as in valid sales. The phrase 'ويجوز خيار التعيين في الفاسد أيضاً' confirms this extension.
The option is not invalidated by the corruption of the sale; it continues to operate.
2
Understand the value liability
In a fasid sale, the item determined for sale is held with liability for its market value (qimah), not the agreed price. The passage says 'ما يتعين للبيع كان مضموناً بالقيمة'.
This is because the price in a corrupt sale is not binding; value compensates for loss.
3
Analyze death scenarios
If both items die together before specification, the buyer guarantees half the value of each. This treats the buyer as having possession of both until selection.
The ruling applies 'إن ماتا معاً ضمن نصف قيمة كل واحد منهما'.
4
Examine freeing by buyer
If the buyer frees both slaves, one becomes free and specification is his. If he frees one specifically or sells it, it is valid and he owes its value. Ambiguous freeing is invalid because it does not specify which slave is freed.
The text explicitly prohibits 'إعتاق المبهم' from both buyer and seller.
5
Interact with seller's freeing
If the seller frees one slave specifically, then later the buyer frees that same slave, or specifies it for sale, or dies, the seller's freeing becomes void. However, if the buyer returns that slave to the seller, the seller's freeing is valid. If both were freed and returned, one is freed at the seller's choice.
The passage details the interplay: 'ولو رد ذلك على البائع صح عتقه'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال بعده ويجوز خيار التعيين في الفاسد أيضاً إلا أنها هنا ما يتعين للبيع كان مضموناً بالقيمة والباقي كما قلنا في الجائز. وإن ماتا معاً ضمن نصف قيمة كل واحد منهما، ولو أعتقهما المشتري عتق أحدهما والتعيين إليه ولو أعتق أحدهما المشتري بعينه أو باعه جاز وعليه قيمته ولا يجوز إعتاق المبهم لا من البائع ولا من المشتري لأن العتق المبهم بين المملوكين للمعتق ولم يوجد ولو أعتق البائع أحدهما بعينه ثم أعتق المشتري ذلك أو عينه للبيع أو مات فعتق البائع ،باطل ولو رد ذلك على البائع صح عتقه، ولو كان أعتقهما وردا عليه عتق أحدهما والتعيين إليه .اهـ.
Then he said after it: And khiyar al-ta'yin is permitted also in a corrupt [sale], except that here the one which becomes determined for sale is held with [liability for] its value, and the remainder as we said in the valid [sale]. If they both die together, he guarantees half the value of each. If the buyer frees both, one becomes free and specification is his. If the buyer frees one specifically or sells it, it is permissible and he owes its value. It is not permissible to free ambiguously, whether by seller or buyer, because ambiguous freeing among two owned slaves does not occur. If the seller frees one specifically then the buyer frees that one, or specifies it for sale, or dies, the seller's freeing is void. If he returns that one to the seller, his freeing is valid. If he had freed both and they are returned to him, one becomes free and specification is his. End.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement continuing the discussion of khiyar al-ta'yin, now applied to fasid (corrupt) sales. A fasid sale is valid in essence but has a defect that can be removed; khiyar al-ta'yin remains valid. The key difference is that the item determined for sale is held with liability for its market value (qimah) rather than the agreed price, because the sale is corrupt and the price may not be binding. The passage then outlines rulings when both items die, or when the buyer frees them. Freeing ambiguously (ibham) is invalid because it does not specify which slave is freed. If the seller frees one specifically, then later the buyer's actions or death void the seller's freeing unless the item is returned to the seller. This section is drawn from the commentary tradition of Kanz al-Daqa'iq.

Key Terms
بيع فاسد (bay' fasid): A sale that is valid in essence but defective in description, correctable by removing the defect.
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): Option to determine the object of sale from among multiple items within a specified period.
قيمة (qimah): Market value; compensation assessed at time of liability.
إعتاق مبهم (i'tāq mubham): Ambiguous freeing that does not specify which slave is freed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, is ambiguous freeing (ibham) of a slave permissible in a fasid sale with khiyar al-ta'yin?
A) Yes, it is permissible
B) No, it is not permissible because it does not specify which slave
C) Only if the seller agrees
D) Only after the sale is completed

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-ta'yin remains valid in fasid sales, but liability attaches to market value, and any freeing must be specific, not ambiguous.

intermediate

Required Wording for Khiyar al-Ta'yin
Specifying the exact wording to make khiyar al-ta'yin valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required wording for khiyar al-ta'yin and determine the validity and liability consequences when the wording is missing.

Core Idea
For khiyar al-ta'yin, the contract must say 'on condition that you take whichever you wish'; otherwise, it is fasid due to jahalah.

The option of choice (khiyar al-ta'yin) gives the buyer the right to choose between multiple items after the contract. However, the precise wording matters greatly. Without the correct phrase, the subject matter remains unknown at the time of contract, making the sale corrupt. This lesson unpacks the required wording and the legal consequences of its omission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that we are analyzing khiyar al-ta'yin. Determine when it is valid (sahih) and when it is corrupt (fasid).
2
Extract the required wording
Find the specific phrase that must be included: 'on condition that you take whichever you wish' (على أن تأخذ أيهما شئت). Understand that this addition removes uncertainty.
3
Understand the underlying cause
The omission leads to jahalah (ignorance) of the sold item, which makes the contract fasid according to Hanafi fiqh.
Jahalah that leads to dispute invalidates the contract.
4
Analyze the consequences of invalid possession
If the buyer takes possession under a fasid contract and the items perish, he is liable: for both, half the value of each; for one, the value of the other.
The details of khiyar al-ta'yin's furu' are referenced in al-Muhit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيدوا صورة خيار التعيين بأن يقول على أن تأخذ أيهما شئت لأنه لو لم يذكر هذه الزيادة وقال بعتك أحد هذين العبدين فقبل يكون فاسداً لجهالة المبيع، فإن قبضهما ومانا عنده ضمن نصف قيمة كل واحد منهما، وإن مات أحدهما قبل صاحبه لزمه قيمة الآخر؛ كذا في المحيط وتقدم تفاريعه
They restricted the form of khiyar al-ta'yin to him saying: 'on the condition that you take whichever you wish'; because if he does not mention this addition and says 'I sold you one of these two slaves' and he accepts, it is fasid due to the ignorance of the sold item. If he takes possession of both and they die in his possession, he guarantees half the value of each. If one dies before the other, he is liable for the value of the other. So in al-Muhit, and its details have preceded.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage specifies the contractual wording necessary for khiyar al-ta'yin to be valid. The buyer must say 'on the condition that you take whichever you wish' or similar. Without this phrase, saying 'I sold you one of these two' makes the sale fasid (corrupt) because the specific sold item is unknown at the time of contract (jahalah). The passage then gives the consequence: if the buyer takes possession of both and they die, he is liable for half the value of each; if one dies before the other, he owes the value of the other. This ruling is from al-Muhit and earlier details are referenced.

Key Terms
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about the subject matter of a contract, which can render the contract fasid.
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): Option of choice: the right given to the buyer to choose between multiple items after the contract, within a specified period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a seller says 'I sold you one of these two slaves' without adding 'whichever you wish'?
A) The sale is valid because the buyer can choose later.
B) The sale is fasid due to ignorance of the sold item.
C) The seller must specify which slave.
D) The buyer must take both.

Key Takeaway
For khiyar al-ta'yin to be valid, the contract must explicitly condition the buyer's right to choose; otherwise, the sale is corrupt and possession carries liability.

Combining Khiyar al-Shart with Khiyar al-Ta'yin
Intra-Hanafi dispute on coexistence of two options.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on combining khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-ta'yin and identify the preferred view with its evidence.

Core Idea
Two options can coexist: khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-ta'yin operate differently, so they can be combined.

The Hanafi school internally debates whether a buyer can stipulate both a time-bound option to rescind (khiyar al-shart) and an option to choose between items (khiyar al-ta'yin) in the same sale. This lesson unpacks the two positions, their supporting authorities, and the practical consequence for the contract.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the core question: can khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-ta'yin be stipulated together in one sale contract?
2
Identify the two views
Locate the view that allows combination (al-Jami' al-Saghir) and the view that rejects it (al-Jami' al-Kabir). Associate each with its leading scholar.
3
Analyze the proof for combination
Understand the reasoning that the two options are distinct: khiyar al-shart ends at death, while khiyar al-ta'yin does not, so they can coexist.
4
Analyze the proof against combination
Understand the opposing argument that khiyar al-shart nullifies khiyar al-ta'yin, based on a reported authentication by Fakhr al-Islam.
5
Determine the tarjih and thamarah
Identify which view is considered correct (Shams al-A'immah's endorsement) and the practical difference: the buyer can return both items during the khiyar al-shart period, then specify one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The author did not mention khiyar al-shart with khiyar al-ta'yin due to difference of opinion. It is said: it is required that there be khiyar al-shart together with khiyar al-ta'yin, and this is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir. Shams al-A'immah said: it is the correct [view]. If they mention both, he has the right to return both within the period, and when it passes, it becomes binding in one of them and he has the choice of specification. And it is said: no, and this is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Kabir, and Fakhr [al-Islam] authenticated it: it [khiyar al-shart] nullifies [khiyar al-ta'yin]? The response: that khiyar al-shart becomes void by death while khiyar al-ta'yin does not become void. End. Mentioned in the Hashiya of al-Ramli, and later in the chapter details what invalidates it from al-Bada'i'. Al-Ghazzi: like so.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) and khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification) can coexist in the same contract. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq did not mention this combination due to the disagreement. One view, reported in al-Jami' al-Saghir and considered correct by Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi, requires that both options be stipulated: the buyer can return both items during the khiyar al-shart period, and after it expires, he must choose one. Another view, in al-Jami' al-Kabir and authenticated by Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, says khiyar al-shart nullifies khiyar al-ta'yin. The response to this is that khiyar al-shart ends at death, while khiyar al-ta'yin does not, so they are different. Al-Ramli's Hashiya and later al-Bada'i' detail what invalidates the option. This shows the internal debate within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in the contract allowing one or both parties to rescind within a specified period (max 3 days in Hanafi).
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): An option where the buyer chooses one of two or more items as the sold object within a period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the view of al-Jami' al-Saghir, what happens if khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-ta'yin are both stipulated?
A) Khiyar al-shart nullifies khiyar al-ta'yin.
B) The buyer can return both items during the khiyar al-shart period.
C) The buyer must choose immediately.
D) The sale is void.

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi view allows combining khiyar al-shart and khiyar al-ta'yin because they operate on different aspects of the contract.

Joint Purchase with Option: The Effect of One Buyer's Satisfaction
Intra-Hanafi dispute on joint purchase option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi difference on whether one buyer's satisfaction extinguishes the other buyer's option in a joint purchase.

Core Idea
When two buy jointly with option, one's satisfaction cancels the other's right to return (Abu Hanifa), but Sahibayn disagree.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a joint purchase with an option condition. The core question: if two buyers purchase an item together on the condition that both have the right to return the item (khiyar al-shart), and one of them declares satisfaction (i.e., releases his option), does the other buyer still retain his option? Abu Hanifa holds that the other loses the right to return, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) maintain that he may still do so. This dispute also extends to other options like khiyar al-'ayb and khiyar al-ru'ya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the joint purchase scenario
Two buyers jointly purchase an item with a stipulation that both have the option to rescind the sale within a specified period.
The sale is one contract with two buyers and the seller.
2
State the dispute
One buyer voluntarily releases his option (declares satisfaction). Determine whether the other buyer's option remains valid.
Dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's opinion
Abu Hanifa: The other buyer cannot return the item. The option is joint, so release by one binds both. The sold item has left exclusive control of the buyers?
Implication: satisfaction by one makes the sale binding as to his share and extinguishes the other's option.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's opinion
The Sahibayn: The other buyer may still return the item. Each has an independent option right; dropping by one does not affect the other's right.
Emphasizes individual ownership of the option right.
5
Extend to other options
The passage notes that the same difference applies to khiyar al-'ayb and khiyar al-ru'ya when multiple buyers are involved.
Consistency of principle across option types.

The explicit: 'I choose this' or 'I wish it' or 'I am satisfied with it' or 'I have accepted it' and what takes its place. As for indicative voluntary, it is that an action occurs from him in one of them that indicates specification of ownership in it, as we have presented in khiyar al-shart. As for compulsory: destruction of one after possession and its defect. If both are defective, one is not determined for sale, and the buyer may take whichever he wishes at its price, but he cannot return both because the sale becomes binding in one of them due to both being defective in his hand, and khiyar al-shart becomes void. And he specified it in al-Binaya to the case after possession, but before it he does not have the return, meaning by agreement of the two that establishing the option for both is establishing it for each of them, so it is not invalidated by his companion's dropping due to what it contains of annulling his right. Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage covers several interrelated topics. The opening ruling addresses a joint purchase by two buyers with an option for both: if one buyer is satisfied (i.e., releases his option), the other retains the right to return the item, according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the satisfied buyer's action does not bind the other, and the other may still return. This difference also applies to khiyar al-'ayb (defect option) and khiyar al-ru'ya (sight option). The passage then delves into the timing of khiyar al-ta'yin, with conflicting views: some say it must be limited to three days, others to any known period, and some say no timing is needed. It also discusses when khiyar al-shart is combined with khiyar al-ta'yin, the benefit (or lack thereof) of stipulating a time limit. The passage further specifies that khiyar al-ta'yin applies only to non-fungible goods (mutafawwita). Finally, it enumerates what invalidates khiyar al-ta'yin: voluntary acts (explicit choice or indicative actions) and compulsory causes (destruction or defect of one item). The commentary from al-Hidaya and other sources is referenced to clarify the positions.

Key Terms
خيار العيب (khiyar al-'ayb): Option of defect: the right to return a purchased item if a defect is discovered that existed before the sale.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): Option of sight: the right to rescind a sale after seeing the item if it does not meet expectations (for items bought unseen).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if one buyer releases his option in a joint purchase, what happens to the other buyer's option?
A) The other's option is unaffected and he may still return.
B) The other's option is also extinguished.
C) The sale becomes void.
D) The option is transferred to the seller.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi jurisprudence, when two buyers jointly purchase with an option, Abu Hanifa rules that one buyer's satisfaction ends the option for both, while the Sahibayn allow the other to retain his individual right—a key intra-madhhab difference.

The Option of Specification: Timing, Scope, and Invalidators
Discussion of timing, scope, and invalidators of khiyar al-ta'yin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the timing of khiyar al-ta'yin, identify its scope (disparate vs fungible items), and distinguish its voluntary and compulsory invalidators.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-ta'yin is valid only for disparate items; its timing is disputed between three days (Abu Hanifa) and any period (Sahibayn).

This lesson unpacks the option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin), a unique Hanafi contract device that allows a buyer to choose which of two or more items to purchase after the sale. The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores the critical dispute over whether this option requires a fixed time limit, and if so, how long. It also clarifies that khiyar al-ta'yin applies only to disparate items (like slaves or garments) and not to fungibles of one type. Finally, it details the actions that nullify the option: voluntary (explicit or implied) and compulsory (destruction or defect). Understanding these rules prevents misuse of this option in modern sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Read the passage to determine what is debated: the timing of khiyar al-ta'yin. Note the positions of Abu Hanifa (three days) and the Sahibayn (any fixed period).
Also note that some later mashayikh require timing, while others argue it is unnecessary.
2
Determine the scope of application
The passage states that khiyar al-ta'yin is restricted to disparate items (al-ashya' al-mutafawita) like slaves and garments, not fungibles of one type. Identify why: no benefit due to lack of disparity.
This limits the option's use in practice.
3
Classify the invalidators
The text divides invalidators into voluntary (ikhtiyari) and compulsory (daruri). Voluntary includes explicit statements like 'I choose this' or implied acts like using the item. Compulsory includes destruction of one item after possession or its defect.
Note the ruling if both items become defective: the buyer may choose any but cannot return both.
4
Examine the opinion of most mashayikh
Qadikhan's view that stipulation of timing is the saying of most mashayikh. Also note the comment from Fath al-Qadir that timing is not beneficial in khiyar al-ta'yin because the contract is binding in one item before time expires.
This shows the depth of ikhtilaf within the school.
