ولو اشترى عبداً على أنه خباز أو كاتب من من أيام من عند مضي الإسلام، فيكون ذكره في الجامع الصغير وفاقاً لا شرطاً. ورجحه في فتح القدير ولكن ذكر قاضيخان أن الاشتراط قول أكثر المشايخ، وإذا لم يذكر خيار الشرط على هذا القول فلا بد تأقيت خيار التعيين بالثلاث عنده، وبأي مدة معلومة كانت عندهما؛ كذا في الهداية. وذكر في المحيط أنه لا يتأقت عنده بالثلاث فيجوز إلى أربعة عنده وفيها : ثم ذكر في بعض النسخ: اشترى ثوبين وفي بعضها اشترى أحد الثوبين وهو الصحيح لأن المبيع في الحقيقة أحدهما والآخر أمانة والأول تجوز واستعارة .اهـ. وفي فتح القدير: وإذا أقت خيار التعيين وكان فيه خيار الشرط فمضت المدة حتى انبرم في أحدهما ولزم التعيين أن يتقيد التعيين بثلاثة ذلك الوقت، وحينئذ فإطلاق الطحاوي قوله خيار الشرط مؤقت بالثلاث في قوله غير مؤقت بها عندهما وخيار التعيين مؤقت فيه نظر .اهـ. وذكر الشارح أنه إذا لم يذكر خيار الشرط فلا معنى لتأقيت خيار التعيين بخلاف خيار الشرط فإن التأقيت فيه يفيد لزوم العقد المدة، وفي خيار التعيين لا يمكن ذلك لأنه لازم في أحدهما قبل مضي الوقت ولا يمكن تعيينه بمضي الوقت بدون تعيينه فلا فائدة لشرط ذلك، والذي يغلب على الظن أن التوقيت لا يشترط فيه .اهـ. ويمكن أن يراد قسم آخر وهو ارتفاع العقد فيهما بمضي المدة غير تعيين بخلاف مضيها في خيار الشرط فإنه إجازة ليكون لكل خيار ما يناسبه. وأطلق في محل الخيار وقيده في البدائع بالأشياء المتفاوتة كالعبيد والثياب، فعلى هذا لا يدخل خيار التعيين في المثليات من جنس واحد لأنه لا فائدة له لعدم التفاوت وفيها: وأما ما يبطل هذا الخيار وهو نوعان: اختياري وضروري والاختياري :نوعان صريح وما يجري مجراه فالاختياري اخترت هذا أو شئته أو رضيت به أو أجزته وما يجري مجراه، وأما الاختياري دلالة فهو أن يوجد منه فعل في أحدهما يدل على تعيين الملك فيه كما قدمناه في خيار الشرط. وأما الضروري فهلاك أحدهما بعد القبض وتعيبه، وأما إذا تعيبا لم يتعين أحدهما للبيع وللمشتري أن يأخذ أيهما شاء بثمنه لكن ليس له ردهما للزوم البيع في أحدهما بتعيبهما في يده وبطل خيار الشرط، وهذا يؤيد قول من يقول بأن فيه خيارين.
And if he bought a slave on condition that he is a baker or scribe... from some days from the passing of Islam, so his mention in al-Jami' al-Saghir is by agreement, not condition. And he preferred it in Fath al-Qadir, but Qadikhan mentioned that the stipulation is the saying of most shaykhs. And if the option of condition is not mentioned according to this saying, then it is necessary to specify the option of specification as three days according to him (Abu Hanifa), and by any known period according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); thus in al-Hidayah. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit that it is not restricted to three according to him, so it is permissible up to four according to him and them. Then it is mentioned in some copies: 'he bought two garments' and in some copies 'he bought one of the two garments', and that is correct because the sold item in reality is one of them and the other is a trust, and the first is a metaphor and borrowing. In Fath al-Qadir: And when the option of specification is time-bound and there is an option of condition in it, and the period passes such that it becomes binding in one of them, then the specification must be restricted to three of that time. And then the absolute statement of al-Tahawi that the option of condition is time-bound by three in his saying, and it is not time-bound by them, and the option of specification is time-bound, requires consideration. And the commentator mentioned that if the option of condition is not mentioned, there is no meaning to specifying the option of specification, unlike the option of condition, because specification in it benefits the binding of the contract for a period. And in the option of specification, that is not possible because it is binding in one of them before the passage of time, and it cannot be specified by the passage of time without him specifying it, so there is no benefit to stipulating that. And the dominant opinion is that timing is not required. And it is possible that another type is intended, which is the termination of the contract in both by the passage of time without specification, unlike its passage in the option of condition, because it is acceptance, so that each option has what suits it. And it was left unrestricted in the place of option and was restricted in al-Bada'i' to disparate items like slaves and garments. On this basis, the option of specification does not enter into fungibles of one type because there is no benefit due to lack of disparity. And in it: As for what nullifies this option, it is of two types: voluntary and compulsory. The voluntary is of two types: explicit and what takes its ruling. The explicit is 'I choose this' or 'I willed it' or 'I am pleased with it' or 'I accepted it' and what takes its ruling. As for the implied voluntary, it is that an action occurs from him regarding one of them that indicates specification of ownership in it, as we mentioned in the option of condition. As for the compulsory, it is the destruction of one of them after possession and its defect. And if both become defective, one of them is not specified for sale, and the buyer may take whichever he wants at its price, but he cannot return both because the sale has become binding in one of them due to their defect in his hand, and the option of condition is nullified. And this supports the saying of those who say that there are two options in it.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin) within the Hanafi school. The commentator begins by referencing a matn about a slave described as a baker or scribe but quickly moves into the rules of khiyar al-ta'yin. The key issue is its timing: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, khiyar al-ta'yin must be limited to three days, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow any specified period. The passage also discusses when the option of condition (khiyar al-shart) is present alongside it, and the debate over whether timing is necessary when only khiyar al-ta'yin exists. The commentator notes that most mashayikh hold that timing is required, but some argue it is not beneficial. The passage then defines what nullifies the option: voluntary acts (explicit statements like 'I choose this' or implied actions) and compulsory causes (destruction of one item, defects). It also clarifies that khiyar al-ta'yin applies only to disparate items (like slaves or garments), not to fungibles of one type, because there is no benefit. The discussion is strictly based on the Hanafi sources cited, without venturing outside the text.

Key Terms
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): The option of specification, where the buyer buys two or more items with the choice to specify one as the sold item within a period.
تأقيت (ta'qit): The specification of a time limit for the option.
اختياري (ikhtiyari): Voluntary nullification of the option through explicit statement or implied action.
ضروري (daruri): Compulsory nullification due to destruction or defect of one item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the timing of khiyar al-ta'yin?
A) No time limit is required.
B) It must be limited to three days.
C) It can be any period agreed by the parties.
D) It is valid only when combined with khiyar al-shart.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-ta'yin is a flexible option for disparate items; its timing is disputed between three days (Abu Hanifa) and any period (Sahibayn), and it is nullified by voluntary or compulsory acts.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Joint Purchase with Option: Effect of One Party's Satisfaction
Explanation of an intra-Hanafi dispute on joint options

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on a joint buyer's right to return after the other's satisfaction, and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) behind Abu Hanifa's view.

Core Idea
One buyer's satisfaction does not automatically extinguish the other's option—Abu Hanifa blocks return to avoid causing a defect.

When two people buy an item together with a condition that both have an option, what happens if one of them decides to keep it? Does the other still have the right to return the item? This passage from al-Hidayah and its commentaries reveals an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the dissatisfied buyer may not return, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow it. We'll examine their proofs and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the issue
The scenario: two buyers jointly purchase a single item with a stipulated option (khiyar al-shart). One buyer is satisfied (i.e., accepts the sale). The issue: can the still-dissatisfied buyer later return the item?
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa says the dissatisfied buyer may not return. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he may return. Note that this dispute also extends to khiyar al-ayb (option of defect) and khiyar al-ru'ya (option of sight).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a cross-madhhab one.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that the option is established for each buyer individually (li kulli wahid minhuma). Therefore, one's satisfaction does not nullify the other's right. They also note that if the option existed before possession, the other's right to return is uncontested.
They consider it a basic principle: each person's option is independent.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that if the dissatisfied buyer returns the item after possession, the item would come back with a 'defect'—namely, the share that now belongs to the satisfied buyer. This imposes an extra harm (darar za'id) on the seller. Since the option is not conditioned on the possibility of unilateral return (the two could have agreed to return together), this harm is avoidable, so the return is blocked.
The key concept: 'returning it defective' (raddahu ma'iban) due to the satisfied buyer's share.
5
Consider the analogous case of two sellers
The text notes that if two sellers have the option and one accepts, the other cannot unilaterally reject. This symmetry reinforces Abu Hanifa's position: the right is not individual in a way that allows partial disaffirmation.
Reference to al-Khaniyah confirms this consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو اشتريا على أنهما بالخيار فرضي أحدهما لا يرده الآخر) عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : له أن يرده وعلى هذا الخلاف خيار العيب والرؤية ؛ كذا في الهداية. وخصه في البناية بما إذا كان بعد القبض، أما قبله فليس له الرد يعني اتفاقاً لهما أن إثبات الخيار لهما إثباته لكل واحد منهما فلا يسقط باسقاط صاحبه لما فيه من إبطال حقه. وله أن المبيع خرج عن ملكه غير معيب بعيب الشركة فلو رده أحدهما لرده معيباً به وفيه الزام ضرر زائد، وليس من ضرورة إثبات الخيار لهما الرضا برد أحدهما لتصور اجتماعهما على الرد. وقوله رضا أحدهما لا يرده الآخر اتفاقي إذ لو رد أحدهما لا يجيزه الآخر ولم أره صريحاً ولكن قولهم «لو رده أحدهما لرده معيباً يدل عليه . وكذا قوله «اشتريا» إذ لو باعا ليس لأحدهما الانفراد إجازة أو رداً لما في الخانية : رجل اشترى عبداً من رجلين صفقة واحدة على أن البائعين بالخيار فرضي أحدهما بالبيع ولم يرض الآخر لزمهما البيع في قول أبي حنيفة .اهـ. وأشار إلى أن المبيع لو كان متعدداً والخيار لأحدهما ليس له أن يجيز في البعض ويرد في البعض، وكذا لو كان واحداً فأجاز من له الخيار في النصف ورده في النصف كما قدمناه وصرح به في الخانية لكن ذكروه فيما إذا كان الخيار للبائع ولا فرق بينهما
His statement: (And if two persons buy with the condition that they both have the option, and one of them is satisfied, the other may not return it) according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He may return it, and upon this difference is the option of defect and the option of sight; thus in al-Hidayah. And he specified it in al-Binayah as being after possession; before that, there is no return for him, meaning by agreement of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that the establishment of the option for the two is its establishment for each of them, so it is not dropped by the dropping of his companion because that would nullify his right. And because the sold item has left his ownership without being defective with the defect of partnership; so if one of them returns it, he would return it defective with that defect, and that involves imposing an extra harm. And it is not necessary for the establishment of the option for both to accept the return by one of them, because it is conceivable that they both agree on the return. And his statement 'satisfaction of one of them does not allow the other to return it' is agreed upon? Because if one of them returns it, the other does not validate it, and I have not seen it explicitly, but their statement 'if one of them returns it, he would return it defective' indicates it. And similarly his statement 'they both bought' because if they both sold, neither of them has the right to unilaterally accept or return, as in al-Khaniyah: A man bought a slave from two men in one transaction on condition that the sellers have the option; one of them was satisfied with the sale and the other was not; the sale is binding on both according to Abu Hanifa. And he indicated that if the sold item were multiple and the option belongs to one of them, he may not accept some and return others, and similarly if it is one item and the one who has the option accepts half and returns half, as we mentioned and as stated in al-Khaniyah, but they mentioned it in the case where the option is for the seller, and there is no difference between them.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific intra-Hanafi dispute regarding joint buyers who stipulate a joint option. The matn states that if two people buy an item with the condition that both have the option, and one of them is satisfied (i.e., chooses to keep it), the other may not return the item. Abu Hanifa holds this view, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the dissatisfied buyer can still return. The commentator explains Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the sold item is not defective merely because of joint ownership; if one returns it, a defect (the share of the other) would be introduced, causing harm. Moreover, the option is established for each individually, so one's satisfaction does not negate the other's right entirely, but the harm principle overrides. The passage also cites al-Khaniyah for the analogous case of two sellers with option. The lesson is limited to explaining the positions and reasoning, without going beyond the text.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): The option of condition, where parties stipulate an option for a specified period.
الصفقة الواحدة (al-safqah al-wahidah): A single transaction involving multiple items or parties.
ضرر زائد (darar za'id): Extra harm, here referring to the harm caused to the seller if the item is returned with a share belonging to the satisfied buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling when two buyers jointly purchase with an option and one of them is satisfied?
A) The satisfied buyer may return the item.
B) The dissatisfied buyer may still return the item.
C) Neither buyer may return the item.
D) The dissatisfied buyer may not return the item.

Key Takeaway
In joint purchases with option, Abu Hanifa holds that once one buyer is satisfied, the other loses the right to return to prevent causing a defect and extra harm to the seller.

Purchase of a Slave with a Stipulated Skill: Baker or Scribe
Ruling on buying a slave with a skill condition; option of return.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a slave bought on the description of baker or scribe lacks the skill, explain why the contract remains valid, and apply the minimal skill threshold.

Core Idea
A desired description gives an option if absent but does not void the sale.

In Hanafi fiqh, stipulating a specific skill in a slave does not affect the validity of the contract. Instead, if the skill is missing, the buyer has the right to either keep the slave for the full price or return him. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the crucial distinction between professional-level skill and minimal ability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is buying a slave on the condition that he is a baker or scribe. The ruling: if the slave lacks that skill, the buyer has the option (khiyar) to either take him for the full price or leave him.
2
Recognize the description's legal status
The description (wasf marghub fihi) is a desired attribute, not an essential condition. Its absence does not invalidate the contract; it grounds an option similar to khiyar al-ayb (option of defect).
The text compares it to describing an animal's gender or safety from defects.
3
Understand the proof via analogy
The ruling is based on qiyas: the loss of a desired description is like the loss of safety (a defect). Both give the buyer an option because the buyer was not satisfied without that attribute.
The asl is khiyar al-ayb, and the illa is the loss of a stipulated beneficial attribute.
4
Apply the minimal threshold rule
Not every performance of the activity counts. The slave must be a professional, not just able to perform minimally (e.g., writing barely legible letters). If only minimal ability, no option exists.
Muhammad's view in al-Ziyadat: 'adna ma yantaliq 'alayhi al-ism' is not enough.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that the buyer has the option when the skill is genuinely absent at a professional level. The minimal threshold is a safeguard against frivolous returns.
The option transfers to heirs by consensus if the buyer dies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو اشترى عبداً على أنه خباز أو كاتب فكان بخلافه أخذه بكل الثمن أو تركه لأن هذا وصف مرغوب فيه فيستحق بالعقد بالشرط ثم فواته يوجب التخيير لأنه ما رضي به دونه، وهذا يرجع إلى اختلاف النوع لقلة التفاوت في الأغراض ولا يفسد بعدمه العقد بمنزلة وصف الذكورة والأنوثة في الحيوانات فصار كفوات وصف السلامة، وإذا أخذه أخذه بجميع الثمن لأن الأوصاف لا يقابلها شيء من الثمن لكونها تابعة في العقد على ما عرف وفي المعراج : قوله «على أنه خباز» أي عبد حرفته هكذا لأنه لو فعل هذا الفعل أحياناً لا خبازاً. وفي الذخيرة قال محمد في الزيادات : فإن قبضه المشتري فوجده كاتباً أو خبازاً على أدنى ما ينطلق عليه الاسم لا يكون له حق الرد لا النهاية في الجودة. ومعنى أدنى ما ينطلق عليه الاسم أن يفعل من ذلك ما يسمى به الفاعل خبازاً أو كاتباً لأن كل واحد لا يعجز في العادة من أن يكتب على وجه تتبين حروفه، وأن يخبز مقدار ما يدفع الهلاك عن نفسه وبذلك لا يسمى خبازاً ولا كاتباً اهـ . وفي فتح القدير : لو مات هذا المشتري انتقل الخيار إلى وارثه اجماعاً لأنه في ضمن ملك العين هي . واختلف تفقه الشيخ علي المقدسي والشيخ محمد الغزي في هذه المسألة
His statement: (And if he bought a slave on condition that he is a baker or scribe, and it turned out contrary, he takes him for the full price or leaves him) because this is a desired description, so it is entitled by the contract by stipulation; then its loss necessitates the choice because he was not satisfied without it. And this goes back to difference of type due to lack of disparity in intentions, and the contract is not invalidated by its absence, like the description of masculinity and femininity in animals, so it becomes like the loss of the description of safety. And if he takes him, he takes him for the full price because descriptions are not allocated any part of the price, being subsidiary in the contract as is known. And in al-Mi'raj: His statement 'on condition that he is a baker' means a slave whose profession is thus because if he does this act occasionally, he is not a baker. And in al-Dhakhirah, Muhammad said in al-Ziyadat: If the buyer takes possession and finds him a scribe or baker at the minimal extent that the name applies, he has no right of return, not even for lack of excellence. And the meaning of the minimal extent that the name applies is that he does something such that the doer is called a baker or scribe, because every person ordinarily is not incapable of writing such that his letters are distinguishable, and of baking an amount that wards off destruction from himself, but by that he is not called a baker or scribe. And in Fath al-Qadir: If this buyer dies, the option transfers to his heir by consensus because it is within the ownership of the essence. And the two fiqh scholars Shaykh Ali al-Maqdisi and Shaykh Muhammad al-Ghazzi differed on this issue.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn about buying a slave with a specific skill description (baker or scribe). The ruling: if the slave does not possess the described skill, the buyer has the option to either keep him for the full price or return him. The reason is that the description was a desired attribute, and its absence gives a choice, similar to khiyar al-ayb (option of defect). The commentator clarifies that a minimal level of the skill does not trigger the right of return; the slave must actually be a professional, not just able to perform the activity occasionally. For example, being able to write barely recognizable letters does not make one a scribe. The passage also notes that the option transfers to the buyer's heir by consensus if the buyer dies. The lesson is strictly based on the Hanafi schools' positions as stated.

Key Terms
وصف مرغوب فيه (wasf marghub fihi): A desired attribute that is stipulated in the contract; its absence gives a choice.
أدنى ما ينطلق عليه الاسم (adna ma yantaliq 'alayhi al-ism): The minimal level at which the name (e.g., baker, scribe) applies; this threshold determines whether the description is fulfilled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of buying a slave described as a baker, which of the following gives the buyer the right of return?
A) The slave can bake only enough to save himself from starvation.
B) The slave cannot bake at all.
C) The slave can bake well but not at a professional level.
D) The slave sometimes bakes for his own consumption.

Key Takeaway
A desired description in a sale does not affect validity; its absence grants an option, but only if the description is professionally meaningful.
